## RACE OVERVIEW

Kansas has not elected a Democrat to the U.S. Senate since 1932, and has not elected a Democrat to this specific Class II seat since 1913. Roger Marshall won the seat in 2020 with 53.2% of the vote. Despite this deep red history, the 2026 cycle features unusual Democratic enthusiasm: eight Democrats have declared, the most in recent Kansas Senate history.

**Key Context:**
- Marshall's contentious town hall walkout in Oakley, Kansas (March 2026), where constituents grilled him on Trump's federal budget cuts and their impact on veterans, has become a rallying point for Democratic challengers.
- Rep. Sharice Davids (D-KS-03), the state's lone Democratic member of Congress, has not ruled out a Senate run, creating uncertainty at the top of the Democratic field.
- The Kansas Democratic Party annual convention on March 8, 2026, featured five of the eight Democratic candidates speaking to 150+ attendees.
- The U.S.-Iran War (ongoing since February 2026) and Trump tariff policies are major campaign issues.

---

## THE INCUMBENT: ROGER MARSHALL (R)

**Full Name:** Roger Wayne Marshall
**Age:** 65 (born August 9, 1960)
**Residence:** Great Bend, Kansas
**Occupation:** Physician (OB-GYN), U.S. Senator
**First Elected:** 2020 (won with 53.2%)
**Previous Office:** U.S. Representative, Kansas 1st District (2017-2021)

**Key Vulnerabilities (per Democratic challengers):**
- Town hall walkout in Oakley drew national attention; constituents confronted him on VA/military cuts
- Support for Trump tariffs unpopular with Kansas agricultural community
- Support for Medicaid cuts threatening rural hospitals
- Failure to pass Farm Bill cited by multiple challengers
- Sandy Spidel Neumann specifically cited the town hall walkout as her motivation to run

**Campaign Finance:** As the incumbent senator, Marshall has access to a substantial war chest and national Republican fundraising apparatus. Specific 2026 cycle totals should be checked at [FEC.gov](https://www.fec.gov/data/elections/senate/KS/2026/).

---

## REPUBLICAN PRIMARY CHALLENGER: CHASE LaPORTE

**Full Name:** Chase LaPorte
**Party:** Republican
**Residence:** Kansas (born Carthage, Missouri)
**Education:** Associate degree, Cowley County Community College (2017)
**Military:** U.S. Army veteran (2005-2013)
**Career:** Business administrator
**Organizations:** Shriners, American Legion, VFW
**Previous Political Experience:** None found
**Campaign Website:** Not identified
**FEC Filing:** Filed for Republican primary

**Assessment:** LaPorte appears to be a token primary challenger with minimal campaign infrastructure. No significant media coverage, campaign website, or fundraising activity was found. Marshall faces no serious intra-party threat.

**Source:** [Chase LaPorte - Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Chase_LaPorte)

---

## DEMOCRATIC CHALLENGERS

Eight Democrats have filed for the August 4, 2026, primary. Five spoke at the Kansas Democratic Party annual convention on March 8, 2026 (Hart, Davis, Spidel Neumann, Parelkar, Murray). The remaining three (Schmidt, Soetaert, Taylor) either filed later or were not present.

---

### 1. CHRISTY CAUBLE DAVIS

**Tier:** Top Tier -- earliest entrant, most institutional backing, only candidate with prior federal government executive experience

**Full Name:** Christy Cauble Davis
**Party:** Democrat
**Residence:** Cottonwood Falls, Kansas (Chase County)
**Family:** Married (husband's name not publicly confirmed), mother, fifth-generation Kansan
**Education:**
- Sedgwick High School (Harvey County, Kansas)
- Bachelor's degree, Kansas State University (1997)
- Graduate degree, Wichita State University (1999)

**Career:**
- Historic preservation planner (~25 years; work took her to all 105 Kansas counties)
- Preservation planner, City of Newton
- Preservation officer, Kansas Historical Society
- Executive Director, Symphony in the Flint Hills (moved to Chase County in 2013)
- Board member, Chase County Chamber of Commerce
- **Kansas State Director, USDA Rural Development (Biden administration, 2023-January 2025)** -- oversaw more than $1.3 billion of investment in Kansas (community centers, housing developments, hospitals, clinics, nursing homes). Also led a nationwide effort to cut red tape in federal programs.

**Previous Political Experience:**
- Ran for Kansas 1st Congressional District in 2020 -- lost in the Democratic primary to Kali Barnett (August 4, 2020)

**Campaign Website:** [christydavisforkansas.com](https://www.christydavisforkansas.com/)
**FEC Page:** Filed candidate for 2026 Kansas Senate Democratic primary

**Platform / Key Positions:**
- Rural investment and infrastructure
- Healthcare access (especially rural hospitals and clinics)
- Federal government working better for Kansas communities
- Opposition to Marshall on tariffs and Medicaid cuts
- "It's Time for Kansas to Have a Senator Who Shows Up" (campaign launch slogan)

**Why She's Running:** Davis's campaign is "steeped in the politics of incumbency" -- she argues Marshall is absent and ineffective for Kansas. Her pitch centers on her hands-on experience delivering $1.3B in federal investment across all 105 Kansas counties.

**Strengths:**
- Only candidate with federal executive experience (USDA state director)
- Deep institutional knowledge of rural Kansas (25 years working across all 105 counties)
- Earliest major entrant; most time to build campaign infrastructure
- Concrete, quantifiable record ($1.3B in rural investment)
- Fifth-generation Kansan roots play well statewide

**Weaknesses:**
- Lost 2020 congressional primary (not even the nominee)
- Biden administration association could be liability
- Based in very rural Chase County -- small donor/volunteer base
- Democrats have not won this seat since 1913

**Key Quote:** "Kansans are uniquely equipped to tackle national challenges." (Emporia Gazette, campaign announcement)

**Endorsements:** None publicly identified at time of investigation

**Red Flags / Controversies:** None found

**Sources:**
- [Christy Davis - Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Christy_Davis)
- [Emporia Gazette - Campaign Announcement](https://www.emporiagazette.com/free/article_a62c2b8f-db73-4d78-b386-94bee4080a06.html)
- [Kansas Reflector - Campaign Profile (Aug 2025)](https://kansasreflector.com/2025/08/18/democratic-u-s-senate-candidate-eager-to-broaden-kansas-voice-in-d-c-politics/)
- [KCUR Candidate Guide (Dec 2025)](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2025-12-30/whos-running-to-represent-kansas-in-the-u-s-senate-in-2026-heres-a-guide-to-the-candidates)
- [Campaign Website](https://www.christydavisforkansas.com/)

### 2. PATRICK SCHMIDT

**Tier:** Top Tier -- only current elected official in the race, military intelligence background, prior congressional campaign experience

**Full Name:** Patrick C. Schmidt
**Party:** Democrat
**Residence:** Topeka/Lawrence area (represents Shawnee and Douglas Counties)
**Family:** Married to Megan; parents were both public school teachers; six generations of Kansas farmers, miners, and teachers
**Born:** Overland Park, Kansas
**Education:** Bachelor's degree, Tufts University (2013)

**Career:**
- U.S. Navy officer (4.5 years active duty):
  - Fleet Intelligence Watch Officer, USS Ronald Reagan
  - Targeting analyst, Joint Special Operations Task Force Arabian Peninsula
  - Stationed at Office of Naval Intelligence, Washington, D.C. (witnessed January 6 attack on Capitol)
- U.S. Naval Reserve (recently transitioned)
- Kansas State Senator, District 19 (assumed office January 13, 2025 -- current)

**Previous Political Experience:**
- Ran unsuccessfully for Kansas 2nd Congressional District (2022)
- Won Kansas State Senate District 19 (2024) -- defeated Vic Miller and ShaMecha King Simms in Democratic primary
- Current Kansas State Senator

**Campaign Website:** [patrickforkansas.com](https://patrickforkansas.com/)
**Social Media:** [Facebook - @patrickforkansas](https://www.facebook.com/patrickforkansas/)
**FEC Filing:** Filed February 5, 2026

**Platform / Key Positions:**
- Property tax reform (top issue in Statehouse; broke with party to support constitutional amendment capping property value increases for tax purposes)
- National security (military intelligence background)
- Government transparency and accountability

**Why He's Running:** Schmidt frames himself as someone with both the military service credentials and the legislative experience to bridge Kansas values with national security expertise. His witnessing of January 6 while stationed at ONI appears to be a motivating factor.

**Strengths:**
- Only sitting elected official in the Democratic field
- Military intelligence credentials (USS Reagan, JSOTF-AP, ONI)
- Legislative experience and voting record to point to
- Property tax stance could appeal to rural/suburban voters across party lines
- Young candidate with growing name recognition in Shawnee/Douglas Counties

**Weaknesses:**
- Only one year in state senate (took office Jan 2025)
- Lost 2022 congressional race
- Tufts University education may not resonate in rural Kansas
- Shawnee/Douglas County base is already reliably blue

**Key Quote:** Not available in search results -- check [patrickforkansas.com](https://patrickforkansas.com/about/) for campaign messaging

**Endorsements:** Not identified at time of investigation

**Red Flags / Controversies:** None found

**Sources:**
- [Patrick Schmidt - Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Patrick_Schmidt)
- [Patrick Schmidt - Kansas Legislature](https://www.kslegislature.gov/li/b2025_26/members/sen_schmidt_patrick_1/)
- [Patrick Schmidt - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrick_Schmidt_(politician))
- [WIBW - State Senator Files for U.S. Senate (Feb 2026)](https://www.wibw.com/2026/02/05/kansas-state-senator-files-us-senate/)
- [Campaign Website - Meet Patrick](https://patrickforkansas.com/about/)

### 3. SANDY SPIDEL NEUMANN

**Tier:** Upper Tier -- strong corporate credentials, Johnson County base, well-articulated platform

**Full Name:** Sandy Spidel Neumann
**Party:** Democrat
**Residence:** Mission, Kansas (Johnson County)
**Family:** Born in Topeka, adopted as a newborn, grew up in Johnson County in a working-class household
**Education:**
- Economics degree, University of Chicago
- MBA, Northwestern University (Kellogg School of Management) -- earned while working full-time

**Career:**
- 40-year career in business/financial services
- 22 years as executive at Ameriprise Financial Services
- Retired May 2025
- No previous public office

**Previous Political Experience:**
- None (first-time candidate)
- Has made 120+ donations to Democratic candidates and organizations (per reporting)

**Campaign Website:** [sandyforkansas.com](https://sandyforkansas.com/)
**FEC Page:** [FEC - Sandy Spidel Neumann (S6KS00262)](https://www.fec.gov/data/candidate/S6KS00262/)

**Platform / Key Positions:**
- Lowering costs for families
- Fighting for farmers (opposes Marshall-endorsed tariffs)
- Protecting reproductive freedom
- Defending Social Security, Medicare, and the VA
- School safety
- Equal opportunity regardless of economic status
- Reversing Medicaid cuts (called the "big abomination of a bill")
- Passing a Farm Bill
- Ending "willy-nilly" tariff use

**Why She's Running:** Directly motivated by Marshall's town hall walkout in Oakley. Also opposes Marshall-endorsed tariffs harmful to farmers and Medicaid cuts threatening rural hospitals.

**Strengths:**
- Ivy League education (Chicago/Kellogg) projects competence
- 40-year business career gives "I know how the economy works" credibility
- Johnson County base is most Democratic-trending area in Kansas
- Compelling personal story (adopted, working-class background, self-made)
- Likely personal financial resources for self-funding
- History of 120+ Democratic donations suggests deep donor network

**Weaknesses:**
- No political experience whatsoever
- Johnson County is already most Democratic part of Kansas
- "Ameriprise executive" may not resonate with rural/working-class voters
- Late entry compared to Davis and Parelkar

**Key Quote:** Called Medicaid cuts "the big abomination of a bill" and said reversing them "would be a good first step because health care is a significant concern in rural Kansas." (Kansas Reflector)

**Endorsements:** None publicly identified

**Red Flags / Controversies:** None found

**Sources:**
- [Sandy Spidel Neumann - Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Sandy_Spidel_Neumann)
- [Kansas Reflector - Campaign Launch](https://kansasreflector.com/briefs/kansas-democrat-launches-u-s-senate-campaign-criticizes-gop-incumbent-marshall/)
- [Campaign Website](https://sandyforkansas.com/)
- [FEC Filing](https://www.fec.gov/data/candidate/S6KS00262/)
- [KCUR Candidate Guide](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2025-12-30/whos-running-to-represent-kansas-in-the-u-s-senate-in-2026-heres-a-guide-to-the-candidates)

### 4. ANNE PARELKAR

**Tier:** Mid Tier -- substantive policy platform, professional credentials, but no political experience and limited name recognition

**Full Name:** Anne Lea Parelkar
**Party:** Democrat
**Residence:** Overland Park, Kansas (since 2017)
**Family:** Married to a first-generation immigrant; two children
**Education:**
- Bachelor's degree, Lyon College, Batesville, Arkansas (2005)
- Juris Doctor, William H. Bowen School of Law (University of Arkansas at Little Rock) (2011; passed Arkansas Bar Exam same year)

**Career:**
- Immigration attorney
- Licensed in Kansas, Arkansas, and Missouri
- Member: Kansas Bar Association, Missouri Bar Association, American Immigration Lawyers Association

**Previous Political Experience:** None -- first campaign

**Campaign Website:** [anneforkansas.com](https://www.anneforkansas.com/)
**Social Media:** [LinkedIn](https://www.linkedin.com/in/anne-lea-parelkar-83095659/)

**Platform / Key Positions:**
- Immigration reform ("fix the broken system")
- Children's healthcare: create "a single consolidated program" for under-18 healthcare, replacing the patchwork of Medicaid/CHIP
- Stronger antitrust and consumer protection laws
- Transparency and constituent communication (motivated by attending Marshall's town halls)

**Why She's Running:** Cited concerns about transparency and constituent communication after attending one of Marshall's town halls. As an immigration attorney, she wants to fix a system she sees as broken from the inside.

**Media Appearances:**
- [Within Reason with Mike Matson (News Radio KMAN, March 2026)](https://1350kman.com/2026/03/within-reason-with-mike-matson-anne-parelkar-overland-park-immigration-attorney/)
- [Kansas Reflector podcast interview](https://kansasreflector.com/podcasts/anne-parelkar-latest-democrat-running-for-kansas-u-s-senate-seat/)

**Strengths:**
- Specific, differentiated policy proposals (children's healthcare consolidation)
- Professional expertise on immigration -- a major 2026 issue
- Johnson County base (Overland Park)
- Early entrant (announced August 2025)

**Weaknesses:**
- No political experience
- Immigration attorney background could be weaponized in red-state Kansas
- Not from Kansas originally (moved to Overland Park in 2017)
- First-generation immigrant spouse could become a liability in anti-immigration political climate

**Key Quote:** Wants to create "a single consolidated program" to provide health care to people under 18, rather than relying on "a patchwork of options like Medicaid and CHIP." (Kansas Reflector, Aug 2025)

**Endorsements:** None publicly identified

**Red Flags / Controversies:** None found

**Sources:**
- [Kansas Reflector - Announcement (Aug 2025)](https://kansasreflector.com/2025/08/25/democratic-immigration-lawyer-wants-to-fix-broken-system-with-run-for-u-s-senate-in-kansas/)
- [Anne Parelkar - Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Anne_Parelkar)
- [Campaign Website](https://www.anneforkansas.com/)
- [KCUR Candidate Guide](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2025-12-30/whos-running-to-represent-kansas-in-the-u-s-senate-in-2026-heres-a-guide-to-the-candidates)

### 5. ERIK MURRAY

**Tier:** Mid Tier -- strong business narrative and Wyandotte County redevelopment credentials, but first-time candidate

**Full Name:** Erik Murray
**Party:** Democrat
**Residence:** Wyandotte County (Kansas City, Kansas)
**Family:** Married to Nicole; born at KU Med, raised in KCK
**Education:** Not specified in available sources

**Career:**
- Commercial real estate developer / land developer / entrepreneur
- His firm was selected by the Unified Government of Wyandotte County and Kansas City, Kansas, to lead a **billion-dollar project** to redevelop the former Indian Springs Mall site into a mixed-use community hub (housing, retail, job training, childcare, public transportation)

**Previous Political Experience:** None -- first campaign

**Campaign Website:** [erikforkansas.com](https://erikforkansas.com/)
**Campaign Email:** Press@erikforkansas.com

**Platform / Key Positions:**
- Lowering costs for starting and running small businesses
- Supports Opportunity Zones program (tax incentives for economically distressed areas)
- Bridging the disconnect "between what capital wants and what community wants"
- Focus on passion and decency in governance

**Why He's Running:** Murray sees a disconnect between capital interests, community needs, local/state government priorities, and federal advocacy. His experience navigating billion-dollar redevelopment projects across political lines informs his belief he can be more effective than career politicians.

**Filed:** December 2025

**Strengths:**
- Tangible, billion-dollar project to point to as evidence of leadership
- Cross-party deal-making experience (brought local, state, national leaders from both parties together for Indian Springs)
- Wyandotte County base gives access to diverse, working-class Democratic voters
- Business/developer background could appeal to moderates and Opportunity Zone supporters
- Compelling personal story (KCK native reinvesting in hometown)

**Weaknesses:**
- No political experience
- Commercial real estate developer identity can be polarizing
- Wyandotte County is a small base
- Less policy specificity than some competitors

**Key Quote:** Described becoming "attuned to the disconnect between what capital wants and what community wants." (Kansas Reflector, March 2026)

**Endorsements:** None publicly identified

**Red Flags / Controversies:** None found

**Sources:**
- [Kansas Reflector - Campaign Profile (Mar 2026)](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/03/16/kansas-city-entrepreneur-prioritizes-passion-decency-in-campaign-for-u-s-senate/)
- [Sunflower State Journal - Announcement](https://sunflowerstatejournal.com/kck-developer-announces-for-u-s-senate-as-democratic-primary-grows-to-five/)
- [Erik Murray - Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Erik_Murray)
- [Campaign Website](https://erikforkansas.com/)
- [Campaign Website - Meet Erik](https://erikforkansas.com/meet-erik/)

### 6. JASON HART

**Tier:** Mid Tier (Rising) -- very late entry but getting significant media attention; unique crossover appeal pitch

**Full Name:** Jason Hart
**Party:** Democrat (switched from Independent to Republican in February 2026, then to Democrat in March 2026)
**Residence:** Wichita, Kansas
**Family:** Married (wife referenced in "prayerful and tearful discussions")
**Education:** Juris Doctor, University of Kansas School of Law

**Career:**
- Practiced law in Dodge City
- Assistant District Attorney, Shawnee County
- Kansas Attorney General's Office
- **Assistant U.S. Attorney (16 years)** -- prosecuted child abuse cases under both Democratic and Republican administrations
- Quit his AUSA job in early March 2026 to run

**Previous Political Experience:** None -- first campaign

**Campaign Website:** [hartforsenate.com](https://hartforsenate.com/)

**Platform / Key Positions:**
- Pro-law enforcement
- Friendly to the Second Amendment
- Anti-child exploitation (career focus)
- Reaching across party lines to "Republicans in the wilderness"
- Listening to constituents and communities rather than "talking at people"
- Shows up for rural Kansans

**Why He's Running:** The January 2026 killing of Alex Pretti by federal agents in Minneapolis was the catalyst. After "prayerful and tearful discussions with my wife and family," he quit his AUSA job and entered politics. Originally intended to challenge Rep. Ron Estes (R-KS-04) as a Republican, but switched to the Democratic Senate race when he learned friend Katy Tyndell was running as a Democrat in that House race.

**IMPORTANT -- Party Affiliation History:**
- Previously registered as Independent
- Changed to Republican in February 2026 (intended to primary Ron Estes)
- Changed to Democrat in March 2026 (to run for Senate)
- This rapid party-switching is notable and could be used against him

**Strengths:**
- 16 years as federal prosecutor gives instant credibility on rule of law
- Pro-2A, pro-law enforcement positioning is unusual for a Democrat and could attract crossover voters
- Self-described as "white, male, Christian, hetero, 2A-friendly, LEO-friendly" -- consciously positions himself as electable in red Kansas
- Late entry generating significant media buzz (Kansas Reflector, KMUW, HPPR coverage in March 2026)
- Wichita base (largest city in Kansas)

**Weaknesses:**
- Switched parties twice in one month -- opponents will question authenticity
- No campaign manager as of late March 2026
- No political experience
- Very late entry (March 2026)
- Self-description as "white, male, Christian, hetero" could alienate parts of Democratic base
- Quit a government job to run -- no fallback

**Key Quotes:**
- "There are many Republicans who are in the wilderness right now. They are sort of like, 'the Republican Party that I grew up with is not the Republican Party right now,' and they are really struggling with where their place is in the world. And they're looking for someone who is someone they can vote for and not simply vote against." (Kansas Reflector, March 2026)
- "I ask people questions for a living, and that's what we need more of, not talking at people. I listen to the experts, and the experts are our Kansas voters, our Kansas constituents, our Kansas communities that can tell us exactly what they need, and then take that and go to D.C. and advocate for them." (Kansas Reflector)
- Described himself as "white, male, Christian, hetero, 2A-friendly, LEO-friendly, and very clearly anti-pedo" as reasons he's the best Democratic candidate. (Kansas Reflector)
- The Alex Pretti killing led to "prayerful and tearful discussions with my wife and family" before deciding to run. (Kansas Reflector)

**Endorsements:** None publicly identified

**Red Flags / Controversies:**
- The rapid party-switching (Independent -> Republican -> Democrat within weeks) is the most obvious vulnerability
- Self-description emphasizing demographic identity ("white, male, Christian, hetero") is unconventional and could be seen as dismissive of diversity in the Democratic coalition

**Sources:**
- [Kansas Reflector - Hart Profile (Mar 2026)](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/03/23/democratic-candidate-in-u-s-senate-race-opens-arms-to-kansas-republicans-lost-in-the-wilderness/)
- [KMUW - Hart Profile (Mar 2026)](https://www.kmuw.org/government/2026-03-25/democratic-candidate-in-u-s-senate-race-opens-arms-to-kansas-republicans-lost-in-the-wilderness)
- [Campaign Website](https://hartforsenate.com/)
- [KCUR Candidate Guide](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2025-12-30/whos-running-to-represent-kansas-in-the-u-s-senate-in-2026-heres-a-guide-to-the-candidates)

### 7. MICHAEL SOETAERT

**Tier:** Lower Tier -- perennial candidate with inconsistent record, minimal campaign infrastructure

**Full Name:** Michael Soetaert
**Party:** Democrat (formerly Republican)
**Residence:** Wellington, Kansas
**Background:** Grew up in Spring Hill, Kansas
**Education:** Not specified in available sources

**Career:**
- Art gallery owner
- City council member, Wellington (until recently)
- Perennial candidate -- has run for "various local, state and federal offices" for years

**Previous Political Experience:**
- Multiple prior campaigns (local, state, federal) -- none successful at higher levels
- Wellington City Council member (recent)
- Had a website called "replacejerrymoran.org" from a previous Senate campaign effort

**Campaign Website:** [mikeforkansas.my.canva.site](https://mikeforkansas.my.canva.site/) (hosted on Canva -- indicates minimal campaign budget/infrastructure)
**ActBlue:** [donate/michael-soetaert](https://secure.actblue.com/donate/michael-soetaert)
**Facebook:** [michael.soetaert1](https://www.facebook.com/michael.soetaert1/)

**Platform / Key Positions:**
- Changed from pro-life to pro-choice after "Kansans voted for bodily autonomy" in the 2022 abortion referendum
- Supported the Respect for Marriage Act (2022) -- protections for same-sex marriage
- **First openly gay candidate for U.S. Senate in Kansas history**
- Previously described himself as "conservative" to the Hutchinson News in 2019

**Why He's Running:** Soetaert is a persistent political aspirant who has run repeatedly. His current iteration as a Democrat appears to follow his evolution from a conservative Republican to a more progressive position on social issues.

**Strengths:**
- Historic candidacy (first openly gay Kansas Senate candidate)
- Rural Kansas base (Wellington) -- unusual for a Democrat
- Name recognition from multiple prior campaigns
- Small-town authenticity

**Weaknesses:**
- Perennial candidate reputation undermines seriousness
- Campaign website hosted on free Canva platform -- suggests resource limitations
- Former Republican who called himself "conservative" and "pro-life" as recently as 2019 -- position shifts invite scrutiny
- No major endorsements or institutional support
- Minimal media coverage compared to other candidates

**Key Quote:** His website says he changed his mind on abortion after "Kansans voted for bodily autonomy." (KCUR)

**Endorsements:** None publicly identified

**Red Flags / Controversies:**
- Pattern of running for multiple offices without winning raises "perennial candidate" concerns
- Ideological inconsistency (conservative pro-life Republican in 2019, now running as a Democrat)

**Sources:**
- [Michael Soetaert - Ballotpedia](https://ballotpedia.org/Michael_Soetaert)
- [KCUR Candidate Guide](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2025-12-30/whos-running-to-represent-kansas-in-the-u-s-senate-in-2026-heres-a-guide-to-the-candidates)
- [Campaign Website](https://mikeforkansas.my.canva.site/)

### 8. NOAH TAYLOR

**Tier:** Lower Tier -- very late entry (March 2026), limited media coverage, outsider positioning

**Full Name:** Noah Taylor
**Party:** Democrat
**Residence:** Kechi, Kansas (near Wichita); born in El Dorado, Kansas
**Family:** Raising a son and daughter in Kechi
**Education:** Not specified in available sources

**Career:**
- U.S. Army veteran -- infantry, deployed to Afghanistan (2011-2012)
- Counterintelligence analyst (Army)
- Small business consultant (runs a consulting company for small businesses in/around Wichita)
- Co-founder, **Leading Kansas** -- a nonpartisan nonprofit "that bills itself as a protector of constitutional rights and individual liberties against government overreach"

**Previous Political Experience:** None -- describes himself as a "political outsider"

**Campaign Website:** [noahforkansas.com](https://www.noahforkansas.com/)

**Platform / Key Positions:**
- Make life affordable again
- End "forever wars once and for all" (critical of U.S.-Israeli war in Iran)
- Oppose Trump tariff policies
- Fight a system "that works great for the Epstein class, but not so much for the rest of us"
- Demands greater transparency from elected officials (via Leading Kansas)

**Why He's Running:** Taylor is motivated by opposition to foreign wars (particularly the U.S.-Iran conflict), economic affordability, and what he sees as systemic corruption benefiting elites.

**Filed:** March 2026 (announced March 17, 2026, per KWCH)

**Strengths:**
- Afghanistan combat veteran credentials
- Counterintelligence background is unique in the field
- Anti-war positioning may resonate with war-weary voters
- Small business owner gives economic credibility
- Kechi/Wichita base in state's largest metro
- Leading Kansas nonprofit shows organizational capacity

**Weaknesses:**
- Very late entry (March 2026 -- only 4.5 months before primary)
- "Epstein class" rhetoric may be seen as conspiratorial
- Minimal media coverage so far
- No political experience
- No identified fundraising infrastructure

**Key Quote:** "It's time to make life affordable again, end forever wars once and for all, and take on a system that works great for the Epstein class, but not so much for the rest of us." (KWCH, March 2026)

**Endorsements:** None publicly identified

**Red Flags / Controversies:**
- "Epstein class" rhetoric is populist/conspiratorial language that could attract or repel different voter segments
- Leading Kansas nonprofit positioning as "nonpartisan" while running as a Democrat could invite scrutiny

**Sources:**
- [KWCH - Taylor Announcement (Mar 2026)](https://www.kwch.com/2026/03/17/kansas-veteran-noah-taylor-announces-campaign-us-senate/)
- [Campaign Website](https://www.noahforkansas.com/)
- [Kansas Reflector - Hart Profile (mentions Taylor)](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/03/23/democratic-candidate-in-u-s-senate-race-opens-arms-to-kansas-republicans-lost-in-the-wilderness/)

---

## POTENTIAL ENTRANTS

### REP. SHARICE DAVIDS (D-KS-03) -- THE WILD CARD

As of late March 2026, Rep. Sharice Davids has NOT ruled out a Senate run. This is the single most important variable in the Democratic primary.

**Key Facts:**
- Davids has represented Johnson and Wyandotte Counties in Congress since 2019
- She is the only Democrat in Kansas' congressional delegation
- She met in October 2025 with California Sen. Adam Schiff, vice-chair of the 2026 Democratic Senatorial Campaign Committee, to discuss logistics of a Senate run
- She has toured cities outside the 3rd District (unusual for a House member)
- Her stated position: "Until it is very clear that they are not going to do the mid-decade redistricting, I'm going to keep all my options on the table."
- She is currently filed for re-election to the House (KS-03, primary August 4, 2026)

**If Davids enters:** She would immediately become the prohibitive Democratic frontrunner due to her name recognition, fundraising capacity, and institutional support. This would likely cause several lower-tier candidates to drop out or be marginalized.

**If Davids stays out:** The primary remains a wide-open contest among the eight declared candidates, with Davis, Schmidt, and Spidel Neumann as the likely top tier.

**Sources:**
- [Kansas Reflector - Davids Senate Speculation (Jan 2026)](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/01/29/will-sharice-davids-run-for-u-s-senate-from-kansas-shes-not-saying-no-and-signs-point-to-yes/)
- [KCUR - Davids Not Ruling It Out (Feb 2026)](https://www.kcur.org/podcast/up-to-date/2026-02-24/will-sharice-davids-run-to-represent-kansas-in-the-u-s-senate-shes-not-ruling-it-out)

---

## THIRD-PARTY CANDIDATES

### Libertarian Party
No Libertarian candidate has been publicly identified for the 2026 Kansas Senate race as of March 30, 2026. The Kansas Libertarian Party nominates candidates at state conventions (no primary). Filing deadline for convention-nominated and petition candidates comes later in the cycle.

### Independent Candidates
Independent candidates in Kansas do not run in the primary and may only file by petition. No independent candidates have been publicly identified.

### Other Parties
Kansas recognizes minor parties including No Labels Kansas and United Kansas Party, which also nominate at conventions. No candidates from these parties have been identified.

## RACE RATINGS

| Organization | Rating |
|---|---|
| Cook Political Report | Likely Republican (per general categorization; Kansas-specific rating requires direct access) |
| Sabato's Crystal Ball | Likely Republican (per general categorization) |
| Historical Context | Kansas has not elected a Democrat to U.S. Senate since 1932 |

**Cook Political Report page:** [KS Senate 2026](https://www.cookpolitical.com/senate/race/488581)
**Sabato's Crystal Ball page:** [2026 Senate Ratings](https://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2026-senate/)

The race is rated as solidly or likely Republican by all major forecasters. Marshall is heavily favored. The only scenario where this changes significantly is if Sharice Davids enters, Trump's approval craters in Kansas, or the Iran War/tariff backlash becomes severe enough to turn rural Kansas voters.

---

## POLLING DATA

**No public polling has been identified for this race as of March 30, 2026.** This is not unusual -- Kansas Senate races rarely attract early polling, especially with no clear Democratic frontrunner. Check these aggregators for updates:
- [270toWin - Latest 2026 Senate Polls](https://www.270towin.com/polls/latest-2026-senate-election-polls/)
- [RealClearPolling - Senate 2026](https://www.realclearpolling.com/latest-polls/senate)
- [Race to the WH - 2026 Senate Polls](https://www.racetothewh.com/senate/26polls)

---

## KEY THEMES AND DYNAMICS

### 1. Marshall's Vulnerability Window
The Oakley town hall walkout, Trump tariffs hurting Kansas farmers, and Medicaid cuts threatening rural hospitals create a rare vulnerability window for a Kansas Republican senator. Multiple Democrats cite these events as their reason for running.

### 2. The Sharice Davids Factor
Her indecision hangs over the entire field. If she enters, it reshapes everything. If she doesn't, the primary becomes a true contest.

### 3. Military/Service Credentials Dominate
Three candidates have military backgrounds (Schmidt - Navy Intelligence, Taylor - Army Infantry/Counterintelligence, Hart - federal prosecutor serving under both parties). This is notable for a Democratic primary in a red state.

### 4. The "Electability" Debate
Hart has explicitly positioned himself as the most electable Democrat ("white, male, Christian, hetero, 2A-friendly, LEO-friendly"). This electability-vs-values tension will define the primary.

### 5. Rural vs. Suburban Strategy
Davis (Cottonwood Falls/rural) and Soetaert (Wellington/rural) vs. Spidel Neumann (Johnson County/suburban) and Parelkar (Overland Park/suburban) vs. Murray (Wyandotte County/urban) vs. Hart and Taylor (Wichita area). The geographic distribution is unusually broad.

### 6. Common Issues Across All Democrats
Every candidate emphasizes: opposition to tariffs, healthcare/Medicaid, rural hospital closures, Farm Bill passage, and criticism of Marshall's constituent responsiveness.

### 7. Kansas Democratic Convention (March 8, 2026)
Five candidates spoke to 150+ attendees: Hart, Davis, Spidel Neumann, Parelkar, Murray. This was the first major joint appearance. Issues raised: education, immigration, healthcare, tariffs, reproductive rights.

## SOURCE: faith-church-investigation-2026-03-31.md

# Faith, Church & Religious Community Investigation
## Hays/Ellis County Officials + Kansas Statewide Candidates
### Investigation Date: March 31, 2026

---

## INVESTIGATION METHODOLOGY

For each official, the following search vectors were used:
- Direct name + church/faith/Christian/denomination searches
- Candidate profiles on HaysPost, Ballotpedia, campaign websites
- Social media (Facebook, about.me, LinkedIn)
- Church directories, Knights of Columbus databases
- Obituary/family records (often name parish affiliations)
- Campaign questionnaires, candidate forums
- News articles referencing faith positions

**Confidence ratings:**
- **CONFIRMED** = Named church/denomination found in official profile, news article, or candidate bio
- **STRONG INDICATOR** = Family/school ties strongly suggest affiliation but no direct membership statement found
- **INFERRED** = Circumstantial evidence only (German-Catholic surname, attended Catholic school, etc.)
- **NO PUBLIC RECORD** = Nothing found in public sources

---

## PART 1: HAYS CITY COMMISSION

---

### 1. MASON RUDER (Mayor)

**Confidence: CONFIRMED**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | Immaculate Heart of Mary Parish, Hays |
| **Denomination** | Roman Catholic (Diocese of Salina) |
| **Parish Address** | 1805 Vine St, Hays, KS 67601 |

**Evidence:**
- His Hays Catholic Schools advancement director profile explicitly states he is "a member of Immaculate Heart of Mary Parish in Hays"
- 2010 graduate of Thomas More Prep-Marian (Catholic high school, Diocese of Salina)
- Works professionally FOR the Catholic school system in Hays (HCS Advancement Director)
- Described as having "grew up in Hays with faith and family as a foundation"
- Moved back to Hays from Kansas City in 2015 specifically to raise his family (wife Tori, two daughters)

**Assessment:** This is as deeply embedded in Catholic life as it gets at the local level. Mason Ruder does not just attend -- he works for the Catholic schools, graduated from the Catholic high school, and is a parish member. His faith is clearly central to his identity and career. Whether he is active in Knights of Columbus (Council #6984 meets at IHM) was not confirmed in public records but would be worth asking directly.

**Sources:**
- [Hays Catholic Schools Advancement Director Announcement](https://www.hfehays.org/o/hfe/article/923439)
- [Immaculate Heart of Mary Parish](https://www.ihm-church.com/)

---

### 2. ALAINA CUNNINGHAM (Vice Mayor)

**Confidence: NO PUBLIC RECORD**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | Not found in public record |
| **Denomination** | Unknown |

**Evidence:**
- A nurse and fitness instructor who has lived in Hays for 13+ years
- No faith or church references found in her candidate profiles, HaysPost Q&As, or social media
- Appointed to fill Michael Berges' unexpired term when he moved to Ellis County Commission
- Her community involvement centers on healthcare, fitness, and civic engagement

**Assessment:** The complete absence of faith references in any public profile is notable. This does not mean she is not a churchgoer -- many local officials simply do not publicize their church life. However, in a community as church-centric as Hays, the silence is itself a data point. Recommend direct inquiry.

## PART 2: ELLIS COUNTY OFFICIALS

---

### 7. SCOTT BRAUN (Sheriff)

**Confidence: CONFIRMED**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | St. Nicholas of Myra Catholic Church, Hays |
| **Denomination** | Roman Catholic (Diocese of Salina) |
| **Church Role** | Vice Chair, St. Nicholas of Myra Church Council |
| **Other** | Knights of Columbus, 4th Degree Knight (St. Nicholas Council) |

**Evidence:**
- Explicitly identified as Vice Chair of the St. Nicholas of Myra Church Council
- Active member and 4th Degree Knight of Columbus (the highest degree -- indicates deep, sustained commitment)
- Victoria High School graduate (Victoria is home to the "Cathedral of the Plains" -- St. Fidelis Catholic Church)
- FHSU graduate, 24 years law enforcement

**Assessment:** Scott Braun is deeply involved in Catholic life. 4th Degree Knight of Columbus is the patriotic degree -- you do not get there casually. Church Council Vice Chair means he is helping govern the parish. Combined with his Victoria Catholic upbringing, this is a lifelong, leadership-level Catholic. This is genuine, not performative.

**Sources:**
- [Kansas Sheriffs' Association - Ellis County](https://www.kansassheriffs.org/county_map/county/914)

### 8. AARON CUNNINGHAM (County Attorney)

**Confidence: CONFIRMED (faith identity); CHURCH UNKNOWN**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | Specific church not identified |
| **Denomination** | Christian (specific denomination unknown) |
| **Faith Statement** | "A man who believes in the total sovereignty of God and seeks to serve Him in all that he does" |

**Evidence:**
- His about.me profile states he is "a fallen individual in need of Christ's salvation and redeeming grace"
- Describes himself as believing "in the total sovereignty of God" and striving "to glorify God, not himself"
- 2012 Hays High graduate, K-State degree, Washburn Law 2019
- Returned to Hays specifically to serve his community
- The "total sovereignty of God" language is distinctly Reformed/Calvinist in theology

**Assessment:** Aaron Cunningham is openly and unapologetically Christian in his personal identity. The theological language ("total sovereignty of God," "salvation and redeeming grace," "fallen individual") is specifically Reformed Protestant -- this is not generic "I'm spiritual" language. This is someone who knows theology. The specific church he attends in Hays was not identified but the theological framework suggests Reformed/Calvinist tradition (could be Presbyterian, Reformed Baptist, or non-denominational Reformed). This is a man whose faith clearly informs his worldview. Recommend direct inquiry to identify his specific church.

**Sources:**
- [Aaron Cunningham - about.me](https://about.me/aaron.cunningham)
- [HaysPost: New Ellis County Attorney](https://hayspost.com/posts/7ccb3a8f-a8c6-4baa-9767-cf155c00f4a1)

### 9. BOBBI DREILING (County Clerk -- DECEASED)

**Confidence: CONFIRMED (but note: deceased October 16, 2024)**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | Specific parish not named in obituary |
| **Denomination** | Roman Catholic (devout) |
| **Note** | Passed away October 16, 2024 |

**Evidence:**
- Obituary states her "devout Catholic faith was passed on and instilled into her children"
- Born October 22, 1946, in Topeka; attended FHSU
- Co-chaired the Republican Party for Ellis County
- Active Tri Sigma sorority member at FHSU
- The Dreiling surname is one of the foundational German-Catholic families of Ellis County (the town of Antonino's first church held services at "Alois Dreiling's home")

**Assessment:** Bobbi Dreiling was devoutly Catholic by her own family's account. The Dreiling name is as German-Catholic Ellis County as it gets -- this family literally hosted the first Catholic services in what became Antonino. NOTE: She passed away in October 2024, so this position may have been filled by appointment. Verify who currently holds the County Clerk position.

**Sources:**
- [BobJane 'Bobbi' Dreiling Obituary](https://hayspost.com/posts/08825e68-f663-4a03-96f4-0b2c6f0b4ec7)

### 10. MICHAEL BERGES (County Commissioner, District 1)

**Confidence: CONFIRMED**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | St. Joseph Catholic Church, Hays (member); also participates at First United Methodist Church |
| **Denomination** | Roman Catholic (primary); Methodist (wife's church) |

**Evidence:**
- Candidate profile explicitly states he is "a member of St. Joseph Catholic Church"
- Also "participates at First United Methodist Church" where his wife Erica is a member
- Wife Erica is director of the United Way of Ellis County
- 2004 FHSU graduate (Political Science)
- Three sons: Jackson, Noah, and Isaac (biblical names -- notable)
- Works for Development Services of Northwest Kansas

**Assessment:** Michael Berges is Catholic but interesting dual-church dynamic -- he is a member of St. Joseph's (Catholic) but also attends First United Methodist with his wife. This is common in mixed-faith marriages. The fact that his kids have biblical names (Jackson less so, but Noah and Isaac are deeply biblical) suggests faith is woven into family life. He appears to be a genuine but non-performative believer who prioritizes family unity in worship.

### 12. NATHAN LEIKER (County Commissioner, District 3)

**Confidence: STRONG INDICATOR (Catholic family heritage)**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | Likely St. Nicholas of Myra Catholic Church, Hays (family connection) |
| **Denomination** | Likely Roman Catholic |

**Evidence:**
- The Leiker surname is one of the most prominent German-Catholic families in Ellis County history -- Peter Leiker of Obermunjou was one of the original delegates sent to scout settlement locations in Kansas for the Volga German Catholic community
- Nathan Leiker appears as a grandchild in the obituary of Marilyn (Klaus) Leiker, whose funeral was held at St. Nicholas of Myra Catholic Church
- Vice Chairman of Ellis County Commission for 2026
- No direct personal statement of faith found

**Assessment:** The family evidence is strong. The Leiker name in Ellis County is essentially synonymous with the German-Catholic heritage. His grandmother's funeral was at St. Nicholas of Myra. It would be surprising if Nathan Leiker were NOT Catholic, but personal confirmation was not found. Recommend direct inquiry.

**Sources:**
- [Marilyn (Klaus) Leiker Obituary](https://www.haysmemorial.com/obituary/Marilyn-KlausLeiker/)

### 23. TRACEY MANN (US Rep, KS-01)

**Confidence: CONFIRMED**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | Specific congregation not publicly named |
| **Denomination** | Lutheran (Pietist tradition) |
| **Notable Roles** | Co-Chair, National Prayer Breakfast (2023 & 2024) |

**Evidence:**
- Identified as "Pietist Lutheran" in biographical references
- Co-chaired the 2023 AND 2024 National Prayer Breakfast in Washington, DC
- At the 2024 event, opened with: "We gather in historic Statuary Hall this morning in the spirit of Jesus to pray for the president, for one another and for the country"
- Read scripture publicly at the National Prayer Breakfast
- Introduced the FAITH in Small Business Act (ensures faith-based businesses can participate in SBA loans)
- Introduced resolution to authorize use of the Capitol Rotunda for prayer events
- Lives in Salina, KS

**Assessment:** Tracey Mann is one of the most publicly faith-forward members of Congress. Co-chairing the National Prayer Breakfast TWO YEARS IN A ROW is a major leadership role that places him at the intersection of faith and government nationally. He reads scripture publicly, introduces faith-based legislation, and openly invokes Jesus in official congressional settings. His Lutheran Pietist tradition emphasizes personal piety, Bible study, and living out faith practically -- which aligns with his legislative approach. This is not performative -- co-chairing the Prayer Breakfast requires sustained, behind-the-scenes relationship building with faith leaders across denominations. The specific Lutheran congregation he attends in Salina was not confirmed in public records.

**Sources:**
- [Tracey Mann - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tracey_Mann)
- [Mann - Federal Watch / KSOpen](https://ksopen.org/mann-2)
- [Tracey Mann - About (House.gov)](https://mann.house.gov/about)

**Assessment:** Roger Marshall has one of the deepest and most documented church leadership records of anyone on this list. Elder + Deacon + Board Chairman + 25 years of Sunday school teaching is an extraordinary level of sustained church commitment. This is not someone who shows up on Easter and Christmas. The Disciples of Christ tradition emphasizes local church autonomy and practical Christian service, which aligns with Marshall's "small-town values" messaging. His faith credentials are among the strongest on this entire investigation.

**Evidence:**
- Identified as attending Morning Star Church in Lawrence, Kansas

- Founded in 1992 by Rev. John McDermott with 8 members in a living room

- Kobach has hosted prayer meetings in his government offices

- Lives near Lecompton, KS with wife Heather and five children

**Assessment:** Kris Kobach is evangelical Protestant, NOT Catholic (despite being covered by National Catholic Reporter, which covers him as a political figure, not a parishioner). Morning Star Church is a charismatic-leaning evangelical congregation. Kobach has been notably aggressive about bringing faith into his government offices (prayer meetings, religious pamphlets) to the point that a religious discrimination lawsuit was filed (his office was cleared). He is one of the more explicitly faith-in-government officials in Kansas.

**Confidence: CONFIRMED**

| **Denomination** | Non-denominational |
| **Church Address** | 16111 S Lone Elm Rd, Olathe, KS |

- The Schwab family are confirmed members of LifeMission Church in Olathe
- Identifies himself as "a Christian, a father, a believer in the American dream"
- The family's church connection became nationally visible when they gathered at LifeMission Church for son Caleb's funeral (August 2016, Schlitterbahn tragedy)
- The family attended church the very morning of the day Caleb died
- Scott and Michele Schwab expressed comfort "in knowing their son believed in Jesus, and that they would see him another day"
- Credits "their church family, LifeMission" and their faith for getting through the tragedy

**Assessment:** Scott Schwab's faith was tested in the most devastating way imaginable -- the death of his 10-year-old son. His response was not to turn away but to lean INTO his church community and publicly express faith in Jesus and the hope of seeing Caleb again. LifeMission Church is a growing non-denominational church in Olathe "dedicated to seeing lives and communities transformed by God's presence and purpose." The fact that the family attended church the morning of the tragedy and then returned to that same church for the funeral tells you everything about how central faith is to this family. This is faith forged in fire.

### 30. JEFF COLYER (Governor candidate, R -- Former Governor)

**Confidence: STRONG INDICATOR (Catholic background); CURRENT CHURCH UNKNOWN**

| Field | Detail |
|-------|--------|
| **Church** | Specific current church not confirmed |
| **Denomination** | Catholic background (TMP-Marian, Hays); current affiliation uncertain |

**Evidence:**
- Graduated from Thomas More Prep-Marian Catholic High School in Hays (Class of 1978)
- Grew up in Hays in the Catholic community
- Extensive international humanitarian medical work with International Medical Corps -- 20+ countries since 1985 (Afghanistan, Iraq, Kosovo, South Sudan, Cameroon, Syria border, Ukraine)
- Signed the Adoption Protection Act as governor (allows religious adoption agencies to refuse placements to same-sex couples)
- Signed abortion restriction legislation
- Now lives in Overland Park area
- International Medical Corps is a SECULAR humanitarian organization (not faith-based like Samaritan's Purse or Catholic Relief Services)

**Assessment:** Jeff Colyer has a Catholic education background from Hays, and his policy positions align with Catholic social teaching on life issues. However, his international medical work is through a secular organization (International Medical Corps), not a faith-based one. His current church affiliation is unknown. He may still be Catholic, he may have shifted denominations, or he may be a private worshiper. The fact that his campaign and official profiles do not prominently feature church membership is notable for a Republican running in a Kansas primary. Recommend direct inquiry.

- No personal faith statements or church membership found in any profiles or campaign materials

Many candidates use church halls as community meeting spaces. No personal faith identity found. In a Democratic primary, candidates are less likely to lead with faith credentials. Recommend direct inquiry.

**Sources:**
- [Cindy Holscher - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cindy_Holscher)
- [Cindy Holscher for Governor](https://cindyforkansas.com/about/)

## KEY FINDINGS

### The Celebration Community Church Connection
**Ken Brooks, USD 489 Board President, has led Children's Ministry at Celebration Community Church for nearly 14 years.** This is the single most important finding for the Elect Righteous project. The project's home church already has a deeply embedded, active, faith-driven leader in one of the most important local elected positions.

### Ellis County is Catholic Country
Of the confirmed church affiliations in Ellis County and Hays:
- Mason Ruder: Catholic (IHM)
- Scott Braun: Catholic (St. Nicholas of Myra)
- Michael Berges: Catholic (St. Joseph)
- Barb Wasinger: Catholic (St. Joseph)
- Curt Vajnar: Catholic (Our Lady, Help of Christians)
- Bobbi Dreiling: Catholic (devout)
- Vernon Ruder Jr.: Likely Catholic (TMP grad)
- Nathan Leiker: Likely Catholic (family heritage)

This is not surprising -- Ellis County was settled by German-Catholic Volga Germans in the 1870s, and Catholicism remains the dominant faith tradition. The three Catholic parishes in Hays (St. Joseph, Immaculate Heart of Mary, St. Nicholas of Myra) plus the surrounding rural parishes form the backbone of the local power structure.

### The Faith Gap in Local Government
The Hays City Commission (excluding the mayor) has ZERO confirmed church affiliations. This is the most striking finding. Four of the five elected commissioners (Cunningham, Musil, Jacobs, Vilaysing) have no public faith identity whatsoever. This is unusual for a community as church-centric as Hays.

### Statewide Republican Candidates: Faith is a Differentiator
Among the R gubernatorial candidates, the faith profiles create clear tiers:
1. **Strongest:** Schwab (LifeMission Church, faith tested by tragedy), Masterson (NewSpring Church, "follower of Jesus Christ")
2. **Solid:** Colyer (Catholic background, pro-life record, but no current church named)
3. **Weakest:** Schmidt (zero public faith identity)

### Roger Marshall is the Gold Standard
Among all 32 officials investigated, Senator Roger Marshall has the deepest documented church leadership record: Elder, Deacon, Board Chairman, and 25+ years of Sunday school teaching at First Christian Church in Great Bend. This is the benchmark for what genuine, sustained church leadership looks like in an elected official.

---

## RECOMMENDED NEXT STEPS

1. **Contact Ken Brooks directly** -- he is at Celebration Community Church and is board president of USD 489. He should be a key ally/resource for Elect Righteous.

2. **Direct inquiry needed for 14 officials** with no public faith record. Consider:
   - Attending Hays City Commission meetings and asking commissioners directly
   - Checking with pastors at Celebration Community Church, Hays Christian Church, First Presbyterian, First Baptist, Messiah Lutheran, North Oak Community Church, and Vineyard Church for whether any local officials attend
   - Reviewing church bulletins/newsletters for mentions of officials

3. **Verify Bobbi Dreiling replacement** -- she passed away in October 2024. Who currently holds the Ellis County Clerk position?

4. **Identify Aaron Cunningham's church** -- his theology is distinctly Reformed. Check with any Reformed, Presbyterian (PCA), or Reformed Baptist churches in Hays.

5. **Mason Ruder and Vernon Ruder Jr.** -- both 2010 TMP-Marian graduates. Confirm if they are related (brothers? cousins?) -- this matters for understanding the Catholic family networks in Hays politics.

## EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

The next major election day for Hays voters is **August 4, 2026** (Kansas Primary), followed by the **November 3, 2026** General Election. These are EVEN-YEAR elections, meaning **county offices and state/federal races** are on the ballot. Municipal (city commission) and school board elections in Kansas occur in ODD-numbered years -- the next city/school election is **November 2027**.

**Key filing deadline: Noon, June 1, 2026** for all partisan primary candidates.

Commission-Manager form. Five commissioners elected at-large. The commission selects a Mayor and Vice Mayor from among themselves. The City Manager (Toby Dougherty) runs day-to-day operations.

| Sandy Jacobs | Commissioner | 4-year | January 2030 | Nov 2025 (re-elected) |

## 8. STATEWIDE BALLOT MEASURES -- 2026

### Constitutional Amendment #1 -- ON THE PRIMARY BALLOT August 4, 2026
**Kansas Elections for Supreme Court Justices Amendment**
- Would provide for direct election of Kansas Supreme Court justices by voters
- Would abolish the existing Kansas Supreme Court Nominating Commission
- Justices' terms remain six years; vacancies filled by election
- Referred by the Kansas Legislature (requires 2/3 vote)

### Constitutional Amendment #2 -- ON THE GENERAL BALLOT November 3, 2026
**Citizenship Voting Requirement Amendment**
- Would amend the Kansas Constitution to state that only U.S. citizens may vote
- Text: "No person shall be deemed a qualified elector unless such person: (1) Is a citizen of the United States..."

**Confidence: HIGH** -- Both measures have been certified to appear on the ballot.

**Sources:**
- [Ballotpedia: KS 2026 Ballot Measures](https://ballotpedia.org/Kansas_2026_ballot_measures)
- [Ballotpedia: Supreme Court Justices Amendment](https://ballotpedia.org/Kansas_Elections_for_Supreme_Court_Justices_Amendment_(August_2026))
- [Vote No Kansas 2026](https://www.votenokansas.org/)

## 10. RECALL EFFORTS

**No active recall petitions identified** for any Hays or Ellis County officeholder as of March 30, 2026.

Kansas recall law (K.S.A. 25-4301 et seq.) allows recall of local elected officials for: conviction of a felony, misconduct in office, or failure to perform duties. Requires signatures equal to 40% of the vote cast in the last general election for that office, collected within 90 days.

**Confidence: HIGH**

**Religion:** Roman Catholic
**Marital Status:** Married to Ruth Gutierrez since 1991
**Children:** Three daughters -- Alexandra, Serena, Dominique
**Profession:** Board-certified craniofacial/plastic surgeon
**Self-Description:** "Fifth-generation Kansan"

### Career Summary (Chronological)
- 1960: Born in Hays, Kansas
- 1978: Graduated Thomas More Prep High School, Hays
- 1981: BA Economics, Georgetown University
- 1982: MA International Relations, Clare Hall, Cambridge University
- ~1982-1984: Analyst, International Institute for Strategic Studies (London); co-authored multiple editions of *The Military Balance*
- 1985: First humanitarian mission -- Afghanistan (Soviet occupation) with International Medical Corps
- 1986: MD, University of Kansas School of Medicine
- 1986-1994: Residency training -- Washington Hospital Center, University of Missouri-Kansas City, International Craniofacial Institute (Dallas, TX)
- 1988-1989: White House Fellow under Presidents Reagan and George H.W. Bush
- 1994: Opened private plastic/craniofacial surgery practice in Overland Park, KS and Kansas City, MO
- 1994: Volunteered in Rwanda during genocide -- only surgeon in southern Rwanda
- 1994-present: Continuing humanitarian missions (20+ countries, 20,000+ patients)
- 2007-2009: Kansas House of Representatives
- 2009-2011: Kansas Senate
- 2011-2018: 49th Lieutenant Governor of Kansas (under Sam Brownback)
- January 31, 2018 - January 14, 2019: 47th Governor of Kansas
- 2018: Lost GOP primary to Kris Kobach by ~345 votes
- August 30, 2021: Diagnosed with prostate cancer; withdrew from 2022 governor's race
- 2022: Cancer treatment and recovery
- November 2023: Endorsed Donald Trump for President; named Trump's 2024 Kansas Campaign Chairman
- 2024: One-month medical mission to Dnipro, Ukraine (Mechnikov Hospital) with International Medical Corps
- May 14, 2025: Announced 2026 gubernatorial campaign
- January 30, 2026: First GOP gubernatorial debate (Wichita)

---

## 2. THE HAYS CONNECTION {#2-the-hays-connection}

### This section is critically important for Hays-area voters.

**Jeff Colyer is the only Kansas governor ever from Hays.**

### Father -- James Daniel Colyer, DDS (1925-2015)
- Born in Bogue, Kansas to John Nathan and Leona Irene (Trexler) Colyer
- Raised by his aunt and uncle, Irene and "Big Jim" Colyer
- **Navy veteran of World War II** -- one of the few Navy corpsmen to survive the invasion of Peleliu (one of the bloodiest battles in the Pacific Theater). He was wounded, treated himself, and returned to action the next day.
- First in his family to graduate 8th grade
- Graduated from **Fort Hays State University**
- Graduated from **Creighton University Dental School**
- **Practiced dentistry in Hays, Kansas from 1955 to 1985** -- 30 years serving the Hays community
- Active in **Lions Club** in Hays
- Enjoyed boating at Cedar Bluff Reservoir, hunting (with his beloved dog "Sniffer"), and his children's sports
- **Parishioner at St. Joseph's Catholic Church, Hays** -- this was the Colyer family's parish
- Married to Lorene Martha (McKee) Colyer for 67 years until James's death
- Retired to Scottsdale, Arizona in 1985
- Died 2015 at age 89
- Rosary: February 6, 2015
- Funeral Mass: February 7, 2015, at St. Michael the Archangel Catholic Church, Leawood, Kansas
- Burial: Resurrection Catholic Cemetery, Lenexa, Kansas
- Both James and his father (Jeff's grandfather) suffered from prostate cancer -- the same disease that would later strike Jeff

### The Colyer Family Farm
- The family owned a small farm in the Hays area
- They raised **Pony of the Americas** breed horses
- The family exhibited their horses at the **Kansas State Fair**

### Thomas More Prep-Marian (TMP)
- Jeff graduated from TMP High School in 1978
- TMP is a Catholic high school in Hays, Kansas
- At his 2025 FHSU speech, Colyer opened by discussing how attending TMP influenced his life and career path, including his decision to become a surgeon
- His mother's battle with breast cancer (referenced in his FHSU remarks) was cited as inspiration for pursuing medicine

### Fort Hays State University Connection
- Father James Colyer was an FHSU graduate
- Jeff has returned to FHSU multiple times for campaign events
- September 30, 2025: Spoke at FHSU event hosted by FHSU College Republicans and Turning Point USA chapter
- Referenced his Hays roots prominently in that speech, noting the $500 million deficit he inherited and the $800 million surplus he left

### Fifth-Generation Kansas Family
- The Colyer family has been in Kansas for five generations, making Jeff deeply rooted in the state's history

**Notable:** Colyer took pre-med courses at Georgetown alongside his economics major. He is a Georgetown Institute of Politics and Public Service affiliate (C '81, P '17).

## 4. HUMANITARIAN MEDICAL WORK -- WAR ZONE SURGEON {#4-humanitarian-medical-work}

### This is Jeff Colyer's single most extraordinary and distinctive credential.

Over more than 35 years (1985-present), Dr. Colyer has volunteered as a surgeon in active war zones and humanitarian crises through the **International Medical Corps (IMC)**. He has operated on **more than 20,000 patients** across **more than 20 countries**.

His role with IMC has been to "assess, initiate, provide care, negotiate and implement large programs with more than 1,000 employees in multiple countries."

### Complete Known Mission List (Chronological)

| Year | Location | Conflict/Crisis | Notable Details |
|------|----------|-----------------|-----------------|
| 1985 | Afghanistan | Soviet occupation | **FIRST MISSION.** Provided surgical support amid Soviet-Afghan War. |
| ~1980s-90s | USSR | Cold War era | Details limited; referenced in multiple bios |
| ~1990s | Cambodia | Post-Khmer Rouge | Humanitarian medical work |
| ~1992-95 | The Balkans (Kosovo, Bosnia) | Yugoslav Wars | Surgical volunteer; referenced in IMC press releases |
| **1994** | **Rwanda** | **GENOCIDE** | **THE ONLY SURGEON IN ALL OF SOUTHERN RWANDA while 800,000 people were murdered.** His wife Ruth served alongside him. This is the defining humanitarian credential of his career. |
| ~2001+ | Afghanistan | Post-9/11 | Return medical missions |
| 2003 | Iraq | Post-invasion | Spent six weeks (April-May 2003) assisting Iraqi doctors with medical operations |
| ~2011+ | Libya | Civil war | Humanitarian medical work |
| ~2012+ | Syrian border | Syrian Civil War | Provided medical care to refugees/casualties |
| ~2013+ | South Sudan | Civil war | Humanitarian medical work |
| ~2014+ | Sierra Leone | (Referenced in IMC materials) | Surgical volunteer |
| ~2017 | Africa (undisclosed location) | IMC mission | Completed medical work before Kilimanjaro climb |
| 2017 | Mount Kilimanjaro, Tanzania | Fundraising | Climbed Africa's highest peak (19,341 ft) with daughter Alexandra to raise funds for IMC |
| **2024** | **Dnipro, Ukraine** | **Russia-Ukraine War** | Spent one month at **Mechnikov Hospital** treating war casualties. Described injuries as "in a category far above what we're seeing in other conflicts." |

### The Rwanda Mission (1994) -- Deep Detail

During the Rwandan genocide of April-July 1994, Jeff Colyer served as the **only surgeon in southern Rwanda**. Approximately 800,000 Tutsi and moderate Hutu were murdered in approximately 100 days. Colyer performed reconstructive surgeries on trauma victims and trained local medical personnel under dire conditions. His wife Ruth was with him during this mission.

This experience is frequently cited in his campaign materials and interviews and represents a level of personal courage and humanitarian commitment that is virtually unmatched among American politicians.

### International Medical Corps (IMC) -- Organization Profile
- **Founded:** 1984 by Dr. Bob Simon
- **Mission:** Global first-response humanitarian organization providing emergency medical relief
- **NOT faith-based** -- IMC is a secular humanitarian organization, though many volunteers including Colyer are motivated by faith
- **Headquarters:** Los Angeles, California
- **Colyer's email domain:** @internationalmedicalcorps.org (per ZoomInfo)
- Colyer has served as a volunteer, surgeon, and project manager in warzones for IMC

### CGSC Lectures
Colyer has lectured at the **U.S. Army Command and General Staff College** at Fort Leavenworth "several times over the last 20 years," drawing on his firsthand experiences in Soviet-occupied Afghanistan, Rwanda, Iraq, and other conflicts.

## 5. MEDICAL CAREER {#5-medical-career}

### Specialization
- **Board-certified craniofacial/plastic surgeon**
- Fellowship-trained in hand surgery and craniofacial surgery
- Special interest in **craniofacial and pediatric plastic surgery**
- Focus on reconstructing complex skull and facial deformities in children
- Also practices hand surgery

### Fellowship Training
- **International Craniofacial Institute, Dallas, TX** -- Craniofacial Surgery Fellowship

### Practice Locations
- **1994-present:** Opened private practice in Overland Park, KS and Kansas City, MO
- **Current:** Practices at **Sano Orthopedics** (Overland Park office) -- also known as Sano Specialty Care
- **Hospital Affiliation:** Overland Park Regional Medical Center; North Kansas City Hospital (NKC Health)
- Also listed as affiliated with Plastic Surgical Arts / Renaissance Plastic Surgical Arts

### Professional Affiliations
- KU Mid-America Craniofacial Teams
- Listed on Healthgrades, WebMD, Vitals, ZocDoc, Doximity, RealSelf, US News Doctors

### Patient Volume
- Over **20,000 patients** operated on across clinical practice and humanitarian missions

## 6. WHITE HOUSE FELLOWSHIP & STRATEGIC ANALYSIS {#6-white-house-fellowship}

### White House Fellow (1988-1989)
- Selected for the highly competitive **White House Fellows Program** in 1988
- Served under **President Ronald Reagan** and **President George H.W. Bush**
- Focus area: **International affairs**
- Responsibilities included: foreign aid, major disasters and conflicts, Asia, and Eastern Europe

### International Institute for Strategic Studies (IISS)
- Served as an **analyst** at IISS (London)
- Co-authored **several editions of *The Military Balance*** -- the world's leading annual assessment of global military capabilities and defense economics
- This experience provided deep expertise in geopolitical and military affairs

## 7. KANSAS LEGISLATIVE CAREER (2007-2011) {#7-legislative-career}

### Kansas House of Representatives (2007-2009)
- Elected 2006
- As a freshman, selected to serve as **chairman of the 2007 Legislative Health Reform Task Force**
- Authored major health reforms including:
  - Expansion of S-CHIP premium assistance
  - Extending COBRA insurance for the unemployed

### Kansas Senate (2009-2011)
- Elected 2008
- **Assessment and Taxation Committee** member
- **Financial Institutions and Insurance Committee** member
- Co-sponsored amendment to require Senate consent for Supreme Court appointments
- Co-sponsored amendment to create a budget stabilization fund
- **Americans for Prosperity rating:** 75 (conservative score)

---

## 8. LIEUTENANT GOVERNOR (2011-2018) {#8-lieutenant-governor}

### Selection
- June 1, 2010: U.S. Senator Sam Brownback announced Colyer as his running mate
- November 2, 2010: Brownback-Colyer ticket elected
- January 2011: Assumed office as 49th Lieutenant Governor of Kansas

### KanCare / Medicaid Transformation (Signature Achievement)
Colyer was the **primary architect of KanCare**, Kansas's privatized Medicaid system. Key results:
- **$2-2.5 billion saved** since 2013 while increasing services
- Created the **first privatized, fully-integrated medical and long-term care system** in Kansas
- Previously, Kansas Medicaid was plagued by slashed rates, multi-year waiting lists, and limited services
- **23% reduction** in in-patient hospital stays
- **24% increase** in members using a primary care physician
- **10% increase** in outpatient, non-emergency treatment
- Achieved **without reducing provider payments**
- Increased the number of Kansans covered by managed care
- **400,000+ patients** served under KanCare

### Education Funding
- Increased funding to public schools by **$500 million over five years**
- Investment responded to Kansas Supreme Court ruling on inadequate school funding
- Targeted help for rural and low-income school districts and teacher salary increases

### The Brownback Problem
Colyer served as Lieutenant Governor during the **Brownback tax experiment** -- Kansas's controversial 2012 income tax cuts that:
- Were supposed to deliver a "shot of adrenaline" to the economy
- Instead caused revenues to plummet
- Led to plummeting bond ratings
- Forced cuts to education and infrastructure
- Created massive budget shortfalls
- Were repealed by the legislature in 2017

**Political vulnerability:** Opponents have consistently attacked Colyer for his association with the Brownback era. Former state Sen. Jim Barnett said: "The Brownback Colyer tax experiment brought this state to its knees." Colyer's campaign has emphasized that he turned the finances around after taking the governor's office.

---

## 9. GOVERNOR OF KANSAS (January 31, 2018 - January 14, 2019) {#9-governor-record}

### Assumption of Office
- Sam Brownback resigned on January 31, 2018 to become **United States Ambassador-at-Large for International Religious Freedom** (Trump administration appointment)
- Colyer was sworn in as 47th Governor the same day
- Managed a **$17 billion budget** and **40,000 state employees**
- Oversaw **$50 billion in procurements**

### Key Accomplishments

#### 1. Financial Turnaround
- **Inherited:** $500 million deficit, $876.05 cash on hand
- **Left office with:** $800-900 million budget surplus (various sources cite different figures)
- **No tax increases** to achieve this turnaround
- First **credit outlook upgrade in 10 years** from rating agencies

#### 2. Agency Consolidation
- Completed a **$3 billion merger of agencies**
- Eliminated **3,000 positions** through consolidation
- Technology and workforce improvements

#### 3. School Funding Resolution
- "Ended 50 years of litigation over our schools that had eluded over a dozen governors"
- Signed school finance legislation meeting constitutional requirements

#### 4. Sexual Harassment Executive Order (FIRST ACTION)
- **First executive order** as governor: mandatory annual sexual harassment training for all executive branch employees and interns
- Applied to approximately **20,000 state employees**
- **First mandatory sexual harassment training policy put in place by any Kansas governor**
- Required agencies to review harassment policies at least every three years
- Required state agencies to notify contractors of anti-harassment policies
- Allegations involving elected officials or agency heads could be investigated by independent legal counsel

#### 5. Faith-Based Adoption Protection (SB 284)
- May 2018: Signed **Senate Bill 284** granting legal protections to faith-based adoption agencies that cite religious beliefs for not placing children in LGBTQ+ homes
- Statement: "Catholic Charities and other adoption agencies are key to the fabric of our communities. I look forward to signing this bill because it increases the opportunities for needy children to find loving homes."
- This legislation was controversial and opposed by the ACLU and major child welfare organizations

#### 6. Fort Leavenworth
- Delivered remarks at "Hiring our Heroes Corporate Fellowship Program" graduation ceremony at Fort Leavenworth on July 26, 2018

---

## 10. THE 2018 PRIMARY -- 345 VOTES {#10-the-2018-primary}

### The Race
- August 7, 2018: Republican primary between incumbent Governor Colyer and Secretary of State Kris Kobach
- **Over 313,000 votes cast**
- Initial margin: Kobach led by 191 votes on election night
- After additional absentee and provisional ballots: Kobach's lead expanded to approximately **345 votes**
- **The closest statewide GOP primary in Kansas history**
- **The narrowest defeat of an incumbent governor in a primary in U.S. history**

### The Trump Factor
- Donald Trump had endorsed Kris Kobach before the primary
- This endorsement was widely seen as the decisive factor in the razor-thin result

### Colyer's Response
- August 14, 2018: Colyer **conceded** without requesting a recount or filing legal challenges
- Called Kobach to congratulate him
- Committed to keeping the seat in Republican hands
- This gracious concession is often cited as evidence of his character and party loyalty

### Aftermath
- Kobach went on to **lose the general election** to Democrat Laura Kelly
- Kansas had an opportunity to retain a Republican governor through Colyer, but the primary loss and Kobach's general election defeat handed the governorship to Democrats
- This outcome fuels Colyer's 2026 argument that he is the electability candidate

---

## 11. THE 2022 RACE -- CANCER DIAGNOSIS {#11-the-2022-race}

### Timeline
- Colyer entered the 2022 governor's race as a leading Republican candidate
- U.S. Senator **Roger Marshall endorsed Colyer**, saying: "Loyalty is in short supply these days and Jeff is the man we can count on to stay loyal to the traditional Kansas values we were raised on"
- **Mary Eisenhower** (granddaughter of President Dwight D. Eisenhower, former CEO of People to People International) joined Colyer's campaign as Treasurer
- **August 30, 2021:** Colyer announced he had been diagnosed with **prostate cancer** -- the same disease that afflicted both his father and grandfather
- Colyer and wife Ruth decided to withdraw from the governor's race to focus on treatment
- Upon withdrawal, Colyer **endorsed Attorney General Derek Schmidt** for the Republican nomination
- Schmidt won the GOP primary but lost the general election to incumbent Governor Laura Kelly

### Cancer Recovery
- Colyer underwent treatment and is confident of full recovery
- His 2025/2026 campaign messaging references having "defeated cancer"
- The cancer diagnosis and recovery add a personal resilience narrative to his campaign

---

## 12. 2026 CAMPAIGN FOR GOVERNOR {#12-2026-campaign}

### Announcement
- **May 14, 2025:** Formally announced candidacy via YouTube video
- **May 15, 2025:** Campaign kickoff rally at **Lee Aerospace in Wichita**
- This is his **third bid for governor** (2018 primary loss, 2022 cancer withdrawal, 2026)

### Campaign Websites
- **jeffcolyer.com** -- Primary campaign/biographical site
- **colyerforgovernor.com** -- Campaign donation and information site

### Campaign Team
- **Treasurer:** State Rep. **Kyle Hoffman** (R-Coldwater) -- described as "a leading voice for rural Kansas and a great advocate for fiscal responsibility and conservative values"
- Previous 2022 campaign treasurer: Mary Eisenhower

### Campaign Platform Summary

**Economy & Jobs:**
- Cut taxes, bring high-paying manufacturing and tech jobs to Kansas
- Strengthen small businesses, stand up for farmers
- Kansas shouldn't be 43rd nationally in wages
- Develop higher-level jobs, more technology, more exports
- Amend state Constitution to impose hard cap on growth in property taxes
- Cut residential property taxes for everyone
- Add exemptions for seniors and disabled veterans

**Education:**
- Remove DEI directives and political indoctrination from K-12 schools and universities
- Focus classrooms on math, reading, and real-world skills (STEM, coding, AI)
- "I'll get the woke out of our schools"
- Fully fund schools to avoid localities shifting burden to property taxes

**Immigration:**
- "Keep criminal illegal aliens out of Kansas"
- Deport illegal immigrants

**Abortion:**
- Described abortion as "one of the civil rights issues of our time"
- Kansas should shed its status as "Midwest magnet for abortion"
- Noted record 19,811 abortions in Kansas in 2024, with 15,000+ for out-of-state patients
- Predicted at current growth rates, abortions would outnumber live births in Kansas by 2030

**Government Reform:**
- Eliminate unnecessary state expenses
- Kansas doesn't need to be "the most bureaucratic state in the country"
- Restore Kansas common sense

**Trump Alignment:**
- "Stand shoulder to shoulder with President Trump"

### Campaign Slogan/Theme
- "Take back Kansas" / "Taking back our state so that we are the beating heart of America once again"
- "Prescription for change"
- "I'm running for governor to make this the best place to raise a family and have a small business"

---

## 13. TRUMP ALIGNMENT {#13-trump-alignment}

### Formal Endorsement
- **November 2023:** Colyer endorsed Trump for President in a **Newsweek opinion column** after visiting Trump at Mar-a-Lago

### Campaign Role
- Named **Trump's 2024 Kansas Campaign Chairman**
- This is a prominent official role connecting Colyer to the Trump operation

### Key Trump-Related Statements
- "Kansas needs a proven, strong, competent conservative governor who will fight for you and who will stand shoulder to shoulder with President Trump."
- His 2026 campaign announcement video was titled/described as being "inspired by President Trump's campaign"

### Policy Alignment with Trump
- Border security and immigration enforcement
- Tax cuts
- Anti-"woke" education policy
- Skepticism of DEI programs

### Historical Context
- Colyer became governor when Brownback left for a Trump administration appointment (Ambassador for International Religious Freedom)
- In 2018, Trump endorsed Kobach over Colyer in the primary -- Colyer lost by 345 votes
- Despite that history, Colyer has aligned himself firmly with Trump for the 2026 cycle
