## 15. FAITH & CHURCH {#15-faith-and-church}

### Religion: Roman Catholic

### Evidence of Catholic Faith
1. **Raised Catholic in Hays** -- attended Thomas More Prep-Marian, a Catholic high school
2. **Family parish in Hays: St. Joseph's Catholic Church** (confirmed via father's obituary)
3. **Father's funeral:** Rosary held February 6, 2015; Funeral Mass at St. Michael the Archangel Catholic Church, Leawood, KS; burial at Resurrection Catholic Cemetery, Lenexa, KS -- all Catholic rites
4. **Signed SB 284** protecting Catholic Charities and other faith-based adoption agencies, with explicit reference to Catholic Charities
5. **Toured Catholic Charities of Wichita** with wife Ruth and daughter Serena (December 2017 tweet) -- "learned first hand how they help families in their time of need"
6. **TMP-Marian influence:** Referenced at FHSU speech as formative to his life direction
7. **Humanitarian work:** While IMC is secular, Colyer's consistent pattern of service to the most vulnerable -- war zones, genocide victims, children with craniofacial deformities -- is consistent with Catholic social teaching on the dignity of human life and preferential option for the poor

### Faith as Campaign Element
- Colyer does not lead with explicitly religious messaging in the way some candidates do
- His faith is expressed more through **action** (humanitarian service, pro-life positions, protecting faith-based organizations) than through verbal testimony
- He has not made prominent public statements about personal prayer life or Scripture, though his Catholic upbringing and schooling are well-documented

## 19. DEBATE PERFORMANCE (January 30, 2026) {#19-debate-performance}

### Event Details
- **Date:** Friday, January 30, 2026
- **Location:** Wichita Marriott, Kansas Republican Party Winter Convention
- **Format:** Six of nine Republican candidates who met participation requirements
- **Participants:** Jeff Colyer, Scott Schwab, Charlotte O'Hara, Ty Masterson (if declared by then), Philip Sarnecki, and others

### Colyer's Performance

**Opening Statement / Key Message:**
> "Kansas needs a proven, strong, competent conservative governor who will fight for you and who will stand shoulder to shoulder with President Trump. This is about winning. This is about taking back our state so that we are the beating heart of America once again."

**On Abortion:**
> "How do we defend innocent life? I think this is one of the civil rights issues of our time. We have a Supreme Court that has found this right to abortion that is nowhere found in that constitution. It's our fastest-growing industry in the state of Kansas."

**On Property Tax Relief:**
> "I will work to cut residential property taxes for everyone, and I'll also add exemptions to make sure seniors and disabled veterans can afford to stay in their homes. This starts with fully funding our schools to avoid localities having to shift the burden and increase property taxes to fill the gap."

**Campaign Vision:**
> "I'm running for governor to make this the best place to raise a family and have a small business."

**Overall Plan:**
- Developing higher paying jobs
- Lowering taxes and initiating a property tax lid
- Promoting education to world class
- Eliminating fraud
- Deporting illegal immigrants
- Restoring Kansas common sense

### Attacks on Colyer
- **Philip Sarnecki** (financial services executive, first-time candidate) criticized longstanding politicians on stage, implicitly targeting Colyer and others, noting Trump carried Kansas three times by double-digits while Kansans twice elected Democrat Laura Kelly

### Key Debate Themes
All six candidates found unity on: abortion opposition, marijuana legalization opposition, judicial bias concerns, and praise for President Trump

## 20. KEY POLICY POSITIONS {#20-policy-positions}

### Abortion
- **Strongly pro-life**
- As governor, supported state constitutional amendment to remove abortion rights protections (failed at ballot in 2022)
- Signed faith-based adoption protection bill (SB 284)
- Describes abortion as "one of the civil rights issues of our time"
- Wants Kansas to stop being an abortion destination for out-of-state patients

### Taxes
- Property tax cap via constitutional amendment
- Cut residential property taxes
- Protect seniors and disabled veterans with exemptions
- "I held the line on taxes, including property taxes" (as governor)
- Kansas ranked 43rd in wages -- wants to improve through better jobs, not just tax cuts

### Education
- Remove DEI and political indoctrination from schools
- Focus on reading, STEM, coding, and artificial intelligence skills
- Fully fund schools through state channels to prevent property tax shifts
- Ended 50 years of school funding litigation as governor
- Increased school funding by $500 million over five years as Lt. Governor

### Immigration
- Deport illegal immigrants
- Keep "criminal illegal aliens" out of Kansas
- Aligned with Trump border policy

### Healthcare
- Architect of KanCare Medicaid reform
- Opposes bureaucratic control of healthcare decisions
- "We need to allow patients and their doctors, not bureaucrats, to determine health care decisions"

### Marijuana
- Opposed to legalization (based on debate position)

### Judiciary
- Co-sponsored amendment requiring Senate consent for Supreme Court appointments (as state senator)
- Concerned about judicial overreach on abortion

### Government Reform
- Agency consolidation
- Eliminate unnecessary state expenses
- Reduce bureaucracy
- Oppose "wokeism" in government ("something that gets rid of any sort of merit, that is a politically inspired outcome")

### Gun Rights
- No prominent statements found in open sources, but general conservative Republican positioning expected

### Critical Race Theory
- Joined other candidates in June 2021 in affirming opposition to CRT in Kansas schools

## 21. VERBATIM QUOTES COLLECTION {#21-verbatim-quotes}

### Campaign / Vision
> "Kansas needs a proven, strong, competent conservative governor who will fight for you and who will stand shoulder to shoulder with President Trump."

> "This is about winning. This is about taking back our state so that we are the beating heart of America once again."

> "I'm running for governor to make this the best place to raise a family and have a small business."

> "I'm Jeff Colyer - Trump's 2024 Kansas Chair - and I'm running for Governor. As a fifth-generation Kansan, a surgeon who's stared down life-and-death in the operating room, defeated cancer, and volunteered in war zones far from home - I've seen firsthand what grit and heart can accomplish."

### On His Record
> "Instead of handing over a $500 million deficit and $800 in the checking account of the state of Kansas, I handed Laura Kelly an $800 million surplus, and we didn't raise taxes to do that."

> "I held the line on taxes, including property taxes. I ended 50 years of litigation over our schools that had eluded over a dozen governors."

> "Matching that support personally shows I'm fully committed to winning this race and delivering results for Kansas again." (on self-funding)

### On Abortion
> "How do we defend innocent life? I think this is one of the civil rights issues of our time."

> "We have a Supreme Court that has found this right to abortion that is nowhere found in that constitution. It's our fastest-growing industry in the state of Kansas."

### On Education
> "I'll get the woke out of our schools."

> Remove DEI "root and branch" from the education system.

### On Property Taxes
> "I will work to cut residential property taxes for everyone, and I'll also add exemptions to make sure seniors and disabled veterans can afford to stay in their homes. This starts with fully funding our schools to avoid localities having to shift the burden and increase property taxes to fill the gap."

### On Faith-Based Adoption
> "Catholic Charities and other adoption agencies are key to the fabric of our communities. I look forward to signing this bill because it increases the opportunities for needy children to find loving homes."

### On Immigration
> "We'll strengthen small businesses, stand up for our farmers and keep criminal illegal aliens out of Kansas."

### On Healthcare
> "We need to allow patients and their doctors, not bureaucrats, to determine health care decisions."

### On Trump Endorsement (Newsweek Column, Nov 2023)
Endorsed Trump stating he would "protect Medicare, lower health care and drug prices, speed development of medical treatments and address the overdose epidemic." Also argued Trump would "close the southern U.S. border with Mexico to drug traffickers" and that America deserved "a president dedicated to securing our borders, stopping the drug traffickers and saving American lives."

### On "Wokeism"
> Defined it as "something that gets rid of any sort of merit, that it is a politically inspired outcome. That's what you're looking for, that's what you're grading people on."

### On Ukraine (2024)
> Regarding injuries he saw in Ukraine: "those injuries are in a category far above what we're seeing in other conflicts."

### On 2019 U.S. Senate Speculation (2019)
> "I appreciate the vast amounts of encouragement I have received over the last few months, though I have made a decision to stay out of the 2020 US Senate race. I remain dedicated to Kansans and will continue to serve in the future."

## 26. STRENGTHS & VULNERABILITIES ASSESSMENT {#26-assessment}

### STRENGTHS

1. **Unmatched humanitarian credentials.** No other candidate in this race -- or virtually any American political race -- can claim to have been the only surgeon in southern Rwanda during a genocide. His 35+ years of war zone medical service across 20+ countries is extraordinary and genuine.

2. **Executive experience.** He is the only candidate who has actually served as Governor of Kansas. He managed a $17 billion budget and 40,000 employees.

3. **Financial turnaround narrative.** Turning a $500 million deficit into a $900 million surplus without raising taxes is a powerful talking point with fiscal conservatives.

4. **Hays roots.** For western Kansas voters specifically, Colyer is one of their own -- born and raised in Hays, TMP graduate, father was a beloved Hays dentist for 30 years, family raised horses on a small farm. He is the only Kansas governor from Hays in state history.

5. **Medical authority.** As a board-certified surgeon, he brings credibility on healthcare policy that no other candidate can match.

6. **Name recognition.** Leads all candidates at 35.1% in Kansas Speaks polling.

7. **Trump alignment.** Serving as Trump's 2024 Kansas Campaign Chair gives him Trump-world credibility in a primary where all candidates are competing for the Trump mantle.

8. **Cancer survivor narrative.** Overcoming prostate cancer adds a personal resilience story.

9. **Family story.** Wife Ruth's impressive scientific career (NIH Genetic Therapy Team), their joint service in Rwanda, and three daughters present a strong family image.

10. **Catholic faith.** Demonstrated through actions (TMP education, parish membership, humanitarian service, protecting Catholic Charities) rather than just words.

### VULNERABILITIES

1. **Brownback association.** Seven years as Brownback's Lieutenant Governor during the disastrous tax experiment is the single biggest political liability. Opponents will continue to tie him to that record.

2. **Third attempt.** This is his third try for the governor's mansion (2018 loss, 2022 withdrawal, 2026). Some voters may see this as inability to close.

3. **2018 Trump endorsement went to Kobach.** In the 2018 primary, Trump endorsed Kobach over Colyer. While Colyer has since aligned with Trump, opponents could use this history.

4. **Overland Park residence.** He grew up in Hays but lives in the Kansas City suburbs. Western Kansas voters may see him as having left.

5. **Self-funding criticism.** The $1.05 million in personal loans, while showing commitment, also invites "millionaire candidate" attacks.

6. **Abortion position vs. Kansas voters.** Kansas voters rejected an abortion amendment in 2022 by a significant margin. Colyer's strong pro-life stance may be out of step with the general electorate (though potentially advantageous in the GOP primary).

7. **"Wokeism" definition weakness.** When pressed to define "wokeism" at FHSU, his answer was vague and criticized by media as lacking substance.

8. **Health questions.** While he says he's recovered from prostate cancer, opponents or voters may quietly wonder about long-term health.

## SOURCE: Kansas-2026-Senate-Insurance-Commissioner-Investigation.md

# DEEP INVESTIGATION: 2026 Kansas U.S. Senate (Democratic Challengers) & Insurance Commissioner Race
## Compiled: March 31, 2026

---

# PART ONE: U.S. SENATE -- DEMOCRATIC PRIMARY (August 4, 2026)

## Race Overview

Eight Democratic candidates are competing for the right to challenge first-term Republican incumbent **Roger Marshall** in deep-red Kansas -- a state that has not elected a Democrat to the U.S. Senate since 1932 (George McGill) and has not elected a Democrat to *this particular seat* since 1913. The primary is August 4, 2026. The general election is November 3, 2026.

A July 2025 hypothetical matchup poll showed **Marshall leading a generic Democrat 58% to 35%**, with 7% undecided. Cook Political Report rates this race **Solid Republican**.

Marshall entered 2026 with a massive financial advantage: **$4.1 million cash on hand** after disclosing $621,400 in Q4 2025 fundraising (69.1% from individual donors), per his January 31, 2026 FEC filing.

The Democratic field is unusually large and features no one with statewide name recognition. No primary polling between the Democratic candidates has been published.

**Republican challenger Chase LaPorte** is also in the GOP primary against Marshall but is not considered a serious threat.

### Key Context for Democrats
Kansas is not as red as it looks on paper. The 2022 abortion referendum (Value Them Both Amendment) was defeated 59%-41%, proving that Kansas voters will cross party lines on specific issues. Gov. Laura Kelly, a Democrat, won two terms. The question is whether any of these Democrats can replicate that crossover appeal at the federal level.

---

## THE CANDIDATES

---

## 1. JASON HART (Wichita)

### The Headline
Former federal prosecutor who quit his job, switched his party affiliation, and entered the race in March 2026 -- making him the **latest entrant** and most unusual story in the field. The most recent major Kansas Reflector/KMUW profile (March 23-25, 2026) focused entirely on him, suggesting significant media interest.

### Full Background
- **Residence**: Wichita, KS
- **Career**: 21+ years in public service as a prosecutor
  - Started practicing law in Dodge City after law school
  - Moved to Shawnee County District Attorney's Office
  - Served as Assistant Attorney General in Kansas
  - Spent **16 years** as an Assistant United States Attorney (AUSA) for the District of Kansas, specializing in **child exploitation and cybercrime cases**
  - Resigned from AUSA position in early March 2026 to run
- **Education**: Law degree from the University of Kansas
- **Party History**: Was registered independent. In February 2026, briefly changed affiliation to Republican intending to primary U.S. Rep. Ron Estes (KS-4th). Learned his friend Katy Tyndell was planning to run as a Democrat in that race. His wife told him: *"I'm not sleeping with a Republican."* He switched to Democrat and filed for U.S. Senate instead.
- **Family**: Married with family. Describes himself as a husband and father.
- **Faith/Values**: Described making the decision after "prayerful and tearful discussions with my wife and family."

### Why He's Running
The January 2026 killing of **Alex Pretti** by federal agents in Minneapolis was the catalyst. As a career federal law enforcement official, Hart said this event -- and the broader direction of the federal government -- compelled him to leave his career and enter politics for the first time.

### Campaign Website & Social Media
- **Website**: [hartforsenate.com](https://hartforsenate.com/)
- Social media accounts not confirmed in available sources

### Campaign Finance
- Hart entered the race in early March 2026. As a very recent entrant, FEC filings may not yet reflect significant fundraising. No specific dollar amounts found in reporting.
- He notably **does not have a campaign manager** as of the March 2026 Kansas Reflector profile.

### Platform
- Frames himself as a nonpartisan law enforcement veteran who served under both Democratic and Republican administrations
- Explicitly **opens arms to Kansas Republicans "lost in the wilderness"** -- positioning himself as a candidate for disillusioned GOP voters
- Emphasis on rule of law, protecting children, cybercrime enforcement
- The "big tent" approach is his primary electability argument

### Key Quotes
- Described making the decision after *"prayerful and tearful discussions with my wife and family"* (Kansas Reflector, March 23, 2026)
- On his party switch: His wife said *"I'm not sleeping with a Republican"* (Kansas Reflector, March 23, 2026)

### Electability Assessment
**Strengths**: The strongest biographical story in the field. A career prosecutor who protected children from predators for 21 years is extraordinarily hard to attack. His party-switching story (independent -> Republican -> Democrat) could genuinely appeal to crossover voters. The "law enforcement Democrat" archetype has worked in red states before.
**Weaknesses**: Entered late (March 2026). No campaign manager. No fundraising infrastructure. No political experience whatsoever. The party-switching could be spun as indecisive.

### Red Flags
- None found. Clean public record consistent with a career federal prosecutor.
- The NRSC financial disclosure complaint (see below) did NOT name Hart, suggesting he filed on time or had not yet triggered the filing requirement.

### Endorsements
- None reported.

---

## 2. CHRISTY CAUBLE DAVIS (Cottonwood Falls)

### The Headline
Fifth-generation Kansan and former Biden USDA Rural Development director who has been running the longest, filed the earliest, and has the deepest rural Kansas credentials in the field. The **first Democrat to declare** for this race (August 2025).

### Full Background
- **Residence**: Cottonwood Falls, KS (Chase County -- deep rural Kansas, population ~900)
- **Born/Raised**: Kansas. Fifth-generation Kansan.
- **Education**:
  - Sedgwick High School
  - B.A., Kansas State University (1997)
  - Graduate degree, Wichita State University (1999)
- **Career**:
  - Preservation planner for the City of Newton
  - Preservation officer, Kansas Historical Society
  - Moved to Chase County in 2013 to become Executive Director of **Symphony in the Flint Hills** (annual outdoor concert event on the Tallgrass Prairie)
  - Board of Directors, Chase County Chamber of Commerce
  - Appointed **Kansas State Director, USDA Rural Development** under President Biden
    - Oversaw **$1.3 billion** of investment in Kansas (businesses, infrastructure, housing, healthcare)
    - Led a nationwide effort to cut red tape and improve federal program delivery
- **Family**: Not detailed in available sources
- **Previous Campaigns**: Ran for Kansas 1st Congressional District in 2020 Democratic primary. **Lost to Kali Barnett**, who received approximately 63% of the vote. Barnett then lost to Tracey Mann (R) in the general.

### Why She's Running
Campaign launch quote: *"It's time for Kansas to have a Senator who shows up."* She positions herself as someone who understands rural Kansas because she lives there and has delivered federal resources there.

### Campaign Website & Social Media
- **Website**: [christydavisforkansas.com](https://www.christydavisforkansas.com/)
- **Facebook**: [Christy Cauble Davis](https://www.facebook.com/christy.davis.710/)

### Campaign Finance
- Filed with the FEC. Specific dollar amounts not found in reporting.
- Named in the **NRSC complaint** (March 11, 2026) for allegedly failing to file a Personal Financial Disclosure Form within 30 days of becoming a candidate.

### Platform
- **Medicaid**: Restore funding; oppose cuts that threaten rural hospitals
- **Education**: Restore funding for special education
- **Affordable Housing**: Restore funding for housing programs
- **Tariffs**: Opposes Trump tariffs, says they cause instability for farmers and rural communities
- **Immigration**: "Fight for immigration reform that provides a pathway to citizenship and ends inhumane policies that terrorize families and unconstitutionally deprive Kansans of due process"
- **Rural Focus**: Her entire campaign is built around rural Kansas credibility

### Key Quotes
- *"It's time for Kansas to have a Senator who shows up."* (Campaign launch, christydavisforkansas.com)
- Said she wants to restore funding for Medicaid, special education and affordable housing programs (KCUR, Dec 30, 2025)

### Electability Assessment
**Strengths**: Deepest rural Kansas credentials. Actually lives in Chase County. The USDA role gives her tangible accomplishments to point to ($1.3B in Kansas investment). Fifth-generation Kansan story is powerful in a state where rootedness matters.
**Weaknesses**: Lost her only previous campaign (2020 KS-1 primary). The USDA role ties her directly to Biden, which is a liability in Kansas. Immigration platform (pathway to citizenship) may be too progressive for Kansas general election voters. The NRSC disclosure complaint, while procedural, gives opponents ammunition.

### Red Flags
- NRSC financial disclosure complaint (March 2026) -- procedural issue, not substantive, but creates a "breaking the law" talking point for opponents.
- 2020 primary loss -- lost significantly (37% to Barnett's 63%).

### Endorsements
- None reported in available sources.

---

## 3. SANDY SPIDEL NEUMANN (Mission)

### The Headline
Retired Ameriprise financial executive with 40 years in business, an economics degree from University of Chicago, and an MBA from Northwestern. The **money candidate** -- has made 120+ donations to Democratic candidates and organizations. Brings corporate-world gravitas but zero political experience.

### Full Background
- **Residence**: Mission, KS (Johnson County -- suburban Kansas City)
- **Born**: Near Topeka. Grew up in Overland Park.
- **Education**:
  - Economics degree, **University of Chicago**
  - MBA, **Northwestern University** (Kellogg School of Management implied)
- **Career**:
  - 40-year career in business
  - 22 years as an executive at **Ameriprise Financial Services**
  - Retired in May 2025
- **Political History**: Has never held public office. Records show she has made **120+ donations to Democratic candidates and organizations**.
- **Family**: Not detailed in available sources.

### Why She's Running
Positioned herself as a businesswoman who will bring financial expertise and tenacity to Washington. Her campaign announcement criticized Roger Marshall directly.

### Campaign Website & Social Media
- **Website**: [sandyforkansas.com](https://sandyforkansas.com/)
- **X/Twitter**: [@speumann](https://x.com/speumann)
- **Instagram**: [@speumann](https://www.instagram.com/speumann/)
- **LinkedIn**: [Sandy Spidel Neumann](https://www.linkedin.com/in/sandy-spidel-neumann-a278536/)
- **FEC Page**: [FEC Candidate S6KS00262](https://www.fec.gov/data/candidate/S6KS00262/)

### Campaign Finance
- Registered with FEC (Candidate ID: S6KS00262). Specific receipt/disbursement totals not extracted from search results. Her FEC page is live at the link above.
- Named in the **NRSC complaint** (March 11, 2026) for allegedly failing to file Personal Financial Disclosure Form on time.

### Platform
- **Lowering costs for families**
- **Fighting for farmers** -- opposes Marshall-endorsed tariffs harmful to agriculture
- **Reproductive freedom**
- **Defending Social Security, Medicare, and the VA**
- **Making kids safer at school**
- **Equal opportunity regardless of economic status**
- **Opposing Medicaid cuts** that threaten rural hospitals

### Key Quotes
- *"In Washington, Sandy will bring that same tenacity to lowering costs for families, fighting for farmers, protecting reproductive freedom, defending Social Security, Medicare and the VA, working to make kids safer at school and ensuring every Kansan -- regardless of economic status -- has the same opportunity she fought for."* (sandyforkansas.com)

### Electability Assessment
**Strengths**: Impressive resume (U of C + Northwestern + 22 years at Ameriprise). Financial expertise is relevant to economic messaging. Johnson County base is where Democratic votes are concentrated. Likely has personal wealth to self-fund.
**Weaknesses**: Zero political experience. Lives in Johnson County, not rural Kansas -- makes "fighting for farmers" claim feel less authentic compared to Davis. 120+ donations to Democrats makes her a clear partisan in a state where crossover appeal is essential. No known endorsements.

### Red Flags
- NRSC financial disclosure complaint (March 2026).
- No political experience at any level.

### Endorsements
- None reported.

---

## 4. ANNE PARELKAR (Overland Park)

### The Headline
Immigration attorney running on fixing the broken immigration system and children's healthcare. First-time candidate. Filed in August 2025, making her one of the earliest entrants alongside Davis and Soetaert.

### Full Background
- **Residence**: Overland Park, KS (Johnson County)
- **Education**:
  - B.A., Lyon College, Batesville, Arkansas (2005)
  - J.D., University of Arkansas at Little Rock (2011)
- **Career**:
  - Immigration attorney
  - Licensed to practice law in Kansas, Arkansas, and Missouri
- **Political History**: Has never run for public office.
- **Family**: Not detailed in available sources.

### Why She's Running
As an immigration attorney, she has a front-row view of the immigration system's dysfunction and wants to bring that expertise to the Senate. Also focused on children's healthcare access.

### Campaign Website & Social Media
- No campaign website found in search results. (May exist but did not surface.)

### Campaign Finance

- Named in the **NRSC complaint** (March 11, 2026) for allegedly failing to file Personal Financial Disclosure Form.

### Platform
- **Immigration Reform**: *"We have a very big problem with immigration in our country right now, in the sense that there's a lot of confusion over it."* Supports reform that is "a solution, not another problem."
- **Children's Healthcare**: Wants to create *"a single consolidated program"* to provide healthcare to people under 18, simplifying coverage and ensuring children have access regardless of family circumstances.
- **Antitrust/Consumer Protection**: Supports stronger antitrust and consumer protection laws.

### Key Quotes
- *"We have a very big problem with immigration in our country right now, in the sense that there's a lot of confusion over it."* (Kansas Reflector, Aug 25, 2025)
- Called for a full investigation of federal immigration enforcement actions (KCUR, Dec 30, 2025)

### Electability Assessment
**Strengths**: Immigration expertise is distinctive and timely. Children's healthcare is universally popular. Licensed in three states suggests serious professional accomplishment.
**Weaknesses**: No campaign website found. No political experience. Immigration is a toxic issue for Democrats in Kansas -- being THE immigration candidate in a red state is a significant liability. Overland Park residence means she competes with Neumann for the same Johnson County base.

### Red Flags

- No visible campaign infrastructure (no website found).

### Endorsements

## 5. ERIK MURRAY (Kansas City, KS)

### The Headline
Kansas City commercial real estate developer behind a nearly **$1 billion** redevelopment project in Wyandotte County. First-time candidate who grew up in KCK, left for USC and a decade in Oakland/San Francisco, then returned in 2023. Has a **significant controversy** flagged by the Washington Free Beacon.

### Full Background
- **Residence**: Kansas City, Kansas (Wyandotte County)
- **Age**: 44 (as of March 2026)
- **Born/Raised**: Kansas City, Kansas. Attended Sumner Academy (magnet high school).
- **Education**: University of Southern California (USC). Met his wife there.
- **Career**:
  - Real estate career, starting in California
  - Moved to Overland Park to raise children
  - Lived in San Francisco Bay Area for approximately 10 years (Oakland)
  - Returned to Kansas City, Kansas in 2023
  - Founded **Eastside Innovation Kansas**
  - Leading the **Midtown Station** redevelopment project at the former Indian Springs Mall site in KCK -- a nearly **$1 billion** development including 2,000 multi-family units, 63 single-family homes, 150 townhomes, affordable housing, childcare center, retail, hotel, and grocery store
- **Family**: Married to Nicole. Lives in Wyandotte County.
- **Political History**: Never held public office. Filed in December 2025.

### Why He's Running
Described the disconnect *"between what capital wants and what community wants"* as his motivation. Said *"politician-created problems"* such as tariffs and tax policies that benefit billionaires *"are tearing apart the fabric of our communities."*

### Campaign Website & Social Media
- **Website**: [erikforkansas.com](https://erikforkansas.com/)
- **Facebook**: [Erik Murray for Kansas](https://www.facebook.com/)

### Campaign Finance
- Filed with FEC. Specific dollar amounts not found.
- Named in the **NRSC complaint** (March 11, 2026) for allegedly failing to file Personal Financial Disclosure Form.

### Platform
- **Small Business**: Lower costs for starting and running small businesses
- **Opportunity Zones**: Supports federal tax incentive programs for investment in economically distressed areas
- **105-County Tour**: Announced a "Heart of America Tour" to visit all 105 Kansas counties
- **Community Development**: Frames his real estate work as community-building, not just profit-seeking

### Key Quotes
- On his motivation: Described the disconnect *"between what capital wants and what community wants"* (Kansas Reflector, March 16, 2026)
- *"Politician-created problems, such as tariffs and tax policies that benefit billionaires, are tearing apart the fabric of our communities."* (KCUR, Dec 30, 2025)

### CONTROVERSY: Elaine Brown / Black Panther Connection
**Source**: Washington Free Beacon (published early 2026)

In late November 2025 -- just days before launching his Senate campaign in December -- Murray appeared on **The Disruption Lab podcast** and spoke at length about his *"transformative experience"* living in Oakland, California for the past 10 years. He credited former Black Panther Party leader **Elaine Brown** with changing *"the wiring"* in his brain.

Elaine Brown led the Black Panther Party from 1974-1977 and has described herself as a *"soldier"* in the fight to bring about a *"socialist revolution"* in the United States -- a fight she says she remains committed to winning. She has recently *"reaffirmed her commitment to topple the 'Empire of the United States.'"*

The Free Beacon framed this as Murray naming *"his political inspiration: a Black Panther 'soldier' working to destroy the American 'Empire.'"*

**Assessment**: This story is almost certainly fatal to Murray's general election viability in Kansas. Whether the podcast comments are taken in or out of context, the attack ads write themselves. In a state that last elected a Democratic senator in 1932, praising a former Black Panther leader as a personal inspiration is disqualifying with the general electorate. It may not even play well in a Democratic primary where electability is the paramount concern.

### Electability Assessment
**Strengths**: The $1 billion development project is the most tangible "job creator" credential in the field. Wyandotte County is a diverse, working-class base. The 105-county tour shows genuine effort.
**Weaknesses**: The Elaine Brown story is a massive liability. Spent a decade in California (Oakland/San Francisco) -- Kansas voters may view him as a California transplant. Recently returned (2023). The development project has had **disputes with the Unified Government of Wyandotte County** over the plan, per KSHB reporting.

### Red Flags
- **Elaine Brown/Black Panther podcast controversy** (Free Beacon, 2026)
- NRSC financial disclosure complaint
- Indian Springs development project had disagreements with local government
- Decade in California is a political liability in Kansas

### Endorsements
- None reported.

---

Former Republican, former Wellington city council member, serial candidate, and the **first openly gay candidate to run for U.S. Senate in Kansas**. Has run for multiple offices under both party labels.

### Full Background
- **Residence**: Wellington, KS (Sumner County -- south-central Kansas)
- **Career**: Former city council member in Wellington (until recently)
- **Political History**:
  - Former Republican

  - First openly gay candidate to run for U.S. Senate in Kansas

- Minimal campaign infrastructure

Current Kansas State Senator (District 19) and former U.S. Naval Intelligence Officer. The **only currently elected official** in the Democratic primary field. Filed in February 2026.

**Strengths**: Only sitting elected official in the field. Military/intelligence background is extremely strong in Kansas (national security, patriotism, discipline). Tufts education shows intellectual caliber. Young and recently elected -- has momentum. State Senate experience, however brief, means he actually has a voting record to run on.
**Weaknesses**: Only been in the state Senate since January 2025 -- barely a year. Running for U.S. Senate from a state Senate seat elected less than two years prior could look overly ambitious. May not have significant fundraising yet.

### Red Flags

## REPUBLICAN PRIMARY

### Roger Marshall (Incumbent)

- **Education**: M.D., University of Kansas School of Medicine (1987)
- **Military**: U.S. Army Reserve (1984-1991)

---

## THE NRSC COMPLAINT (March 11, 2026)

The National Republican Senatorial Committee called on the Senate Select Committee on Ethics to investigate **four** Kansas Democratic Senate candidates for failing to file Personal Financial Disclosure Forms within 30 days of officially becoming a candidate, as required by federal law:

1. **Erik Murray**
2. **Sandy Spidel Neumann**
3. **Christy Davis**
4. **Anne Parelkar**

**Not named**: Jason Hart (entered too recently), Patrick Schmidt, Michael Soetaert.

NRSC Regional Press Secretary Samantha Cantrell: *"By failing to file their personal financial disclosure forms, these four Senate Democrat candidates are not only breaking the law, but deliberately keeping Kansans in the dark."*

**Assessment**: This is a standard opposition research play. Financial disclosure delinquency is common among first-time candidates unfamiliar with federal filing requirements. It is a procedural violation, not evidence of corruption. However, it provides Republicans with a "they broke the law" talking point.

---

## DEMOCRATIC PRIMARY POWER RANKING (Investigator's Assessment)

Based on all available evidence as of March 31, 2026:

| Rank | Candidate | Key Advantage | Key Vulnerability |
|------|-----------|--------------|-------------------|
| 1 | **Jason Hart** | Prosecutor bio + crossover appeal | Late entry, no infrastructure |
| 2 | **Patrick Schmidt** | Only elected official + military | Very brief tenure |
| 3 | **Christy Davis** | Rural credentials + USDA experience | Lost 2020 primary badly |
| 4 | **Sandy Spidel Neumann** | Business resume + likely self-fund capacity | Zero political experience |
| 5 | **Erik Murray** | $1B development project | Elaine Brown controversy |
| 6 | **Anne Parelkar** | Immigration expertise | No visible campaign infrastructure |
| 7 | **Michael Soetaert** | Rural location | Serial losing candidate |

**Note**: This ranking is speculative. With no primary polling, the race is genuinely wide open. Fundraising totals (not yet publicly available for most candidates) will be the most important early indicator.

# PART TWO: KANSAS INSURANCE COMMISSIONER (Open Seat -- November 3, 2026)

## Race Overview

This is an **open seat** race. Current Insurance Commissioner **Vicki Schmidt** (R) is leaving to run for Governor. The Insurance Commissioner is one of only six statewide elected offices in Kansas and directly oversees insurance regulation, consumer protection, healthcare policy enforcement, and the financial solvency of insurance companies operating in the state.

**Why this race matters for rural Kansas**: The Insurance Commissioner has direct authority over health insurance rates, availability of coverage in rural areas, regulation of pharmacy benefit managers (PBMs), crop insurance oversight, and consumer complaint resolution. In a state where rural hospitals are closing and healthcare costs are rising, this office has more direct impact on daily life than most voters realize.

Two candidates are running (one per party -- no primary contests announced):

---

## DANIEL HAWKINS (Republican -- Wichita)

### The Headline
Kansas House Speaker with 30 years in the insurance industry, running on a **"Pro-Life. Pro-Gun. Pro-Trump."** platform -- but now facing intense scrutiny for using his Speaker's power to **block a bipartisan prescription drug cost bill** that would regulate pharmacy benefit managers. The bill eventually passed 104-17 despite his efforts to kill it.

### Full Background
- **Residence**: 9406 Harvest Ln., Wichita, KS 67212
- **Education**:
  - Associate degree in Business, Hutchison Community College (1981)
  - B.S. in Marketing, Emporia State University (1983)
  - Chartered Life Underwriter (CLU) designation (2000)
- **Military**: Staff Sergeant, Kansas Army National Guard (retired 1991)
- **Career**:
  - 30+ years in the insurance business, specializing in **employee benefits**
  - Started in insurance in 1995, helping small businesses and their employees
- **Political Career**:
  - First elected to Kansas House of Representatives in **2012**
  - Became **Speaker of the House in 2023**
  - A rule passed in 2023 limits speakers to two consecutive terms. Hawkins has cited this term limit as part of his reason for running for Insurance Commissioner.
- **Family**: Not detailed in available sources
- **Kansas Legislature page**: [kslegislature.gov](https://www.kslegislature.gov/li/b2025_26/members/rep_hawkins_daniel_1/)

### Campaign Website & Social Media
- **Website**: [hawkinsforinsurance.com](https://www.hawkinsforinsurance.com/)
- **X/Twitter**: [@DanHawkinsKS](https://x.com/danhawkinsks)

### Campaign Finance
- Raised **$417,305 during 2025**, including a $10,000 personal loan
- **~$384,000 cash on hand** at end of 2025
- Source: Sunflower State Journal

### Platform
- Website headline: **"PRO-LIFE. PRO-GUN. PRO-TRUMP."**
- *"Dan has been a strong supporter of President Trump and will serve as a vocal ally for his agenda."*
- Supports "President Trump's America first agenda" and will "prioritize policies that drain the swamp and put Kansans first"
- Focus on: increasing competition, easing marketplace navigation, ensuring people are not wrongly denied coverage
- *"Just like President Trump has made it his mission to make life miserable for foreign cartels, it will be my job as Insurance Commissioner to do the same for any insurance company that does not follow the law."* (hawkinsforinsurance.com)

### THE SB 360 CONTROVERSY (March 2026)

This is the defining issue of Hawkins' candidacy and potentially his greatest vulnerability:

**What happened**: The Kansas Senate passed **Senate Bill 360** with overwhelming bipartisan support. The bill would bring greater state regulation to **pharmacy benefit managers (PBMs)** -- the middlemen (CVS Caremark, Express Scripts, OptumRx, Blue Cross Blue Shield of Kansas) accused of anti-competitive practices, monopolizing the pharmaceutical market, and raising drug costs for consumers.

**What Hawkins did**: As House Speaker, Hawkins used his **unilateral authority** to repeatedly block the bill:
- Ordered SB 360 transferred between the House Insurance Committee and Health Committee **four times** since February 25, 2026
- No action was taken by either committee
- Advocates accused him of "desperately maneuvering to sabotage" the vote
- Kansas Reflector headline (March 22, 2026): *"Kansas House speaker desperately maneuvers to sabotage vote on Senate bill capping drug costs"*

**What happened next**: Kansas House Republicans **defied Hawkins**. The PBM regulatory language was inserted into Senate Bill 20 during a conference committee, and the House passed the measure **104-17** after passionate debate (March 26, 2026). Hawkins was overruled by his own caucus.

**Why this matters for the Insurance Commissioner race**: Hawkins spent 30 years in the insurance industry. PBMs are part of the insurance/healthcare ecosystem. His actions to block consumer-protection legislation -- while running to be the state's top insurance regulator -- create a devastating conflict-of-interest narrative. His opponent has already seized on this.

### Key Quotes
- *"PRO-LIFE. PRO-GUN. PRO-TRUMP."* (hawkinsforinsurance.com)
- *"Just like President Trump has made it his mission to make life miserable for foreign cartels, it will be my job as Insurance Commissioner to do the same for any insurance company that does not follow the law."* (hawkinsforinsurance.com)

### Electability Assessment
**Strengths**: 30 years of insurance industry expertise is directly relevant to the job. $384K cash on hand. Strong Republican base in Kansas. House Speaker title provides name recognition and party infrastructure.
**Weaknesses**: The SB 360 debacle is a gift to his opponent. Being overruled 104-17 by your own caucus is humiliating. The "Pro-Trump" branding may help in a primary but could limit crossover appeal in a general election -- especially after the 2022 abortion referendum showed Kansas voters will cross party lines. The term-limit motivation for running (he's being forced out as Speaker) makes this look like a fallback rather than a calling.

### Red Flags
- **SB 360 blocking**: Used Speaker's power to repeatedly bottle up a bipartisan prescription drug cost bill, while running to be the state's insurance regulator. His own Republican caucus overruled him 104-17.
- **Insurance industry conflict of interest**: 30 years in insurance, now seeking to regulate the industry.
- **PBM lobbying**: CVS Caremark, Express Scripts, OptumRx, and Blue Cross Blue Shield of Kansas lobbied against SB 360 -- the same bill Hawkins tried to kill.

### Endorsements
- None specifically reported, though his Pro-Trump branding implies expected Trump/MAGA endorsement infrastructure.

---

## DINAH SYKES (Democrat -- Lenexa)

### The Headline
Kansas Senate Minority Leader, the **first woman to hold that position** in Kansas history. Former Republican who switched parties in December 2018 as part of a wave of moderate Kansas GOP women leaving the party. Has endorsements from **both a Democratic and Republican former Insurance Commissioner**. Has pledged to accept **zero campaign contributions from the insurance industry**.

### Full Background
- **Residence**: Lenexa, KS (Johnson County)
- **Education**: B.A. in Business Administration, Trevecca Nazarene University (1999) -- *note: Trevecca is a Church of the Nazarene university in Nashville, TN, suggesting a faith background*
- **Career Before Politics**:
  - Ran her own business as a **personal chef**
  - **PTA president**
  - Member, Lenexa Chamber of Commerce
- **Political Career**:
  - Elected to **Kansas State Senate, District 21** in November 2016 -- as a **Republican**
  - **Switched parties to Democrat** on December 19, 2018, along with three other Kansas women legislators:
    - Sen. Barbara Bollier (who later ran for U.S. Senate in 2020)
    - Rep. Joy Koesten
    - Rep. Stephanie Clayton
  - Her reason for switching: *"I am a moderate person who represents a moderate and pragmatic district that expects me to focus on issues and solutions that impact their day-to-day lives. Increasingly, I see the Republican party focusing on issues and approaches that divide our country... being a moderate inside the Republican Party is an increasingly difficult path to take with the trajectory of the party nationally."*
  - Elected **Kansas Senate Minority Leader in 2020** -- first woman in Kansas history to hold this position
  - Has served in the state Senate continuously since 2017

### Why She's Running
To hold insurance companies accountable, lower costs, and protect consumers. She positions herself as the anti-industry candidate against Hawkins' 30-year insurance industry career.

### Campaign Website & Social Media
- **Website**: [dinahsykes.com](https://www.dinahsykes.com/)
- **Facebook**: [Senator Dinah Sykes (@Sykes4KS)](https://www.facebook.com/Sykes4KS/)
- **Kansas Senate Democrats page**: [kssenatedems.org/dinah-sykes](https://www.kssenatedems.org/dinah-sykes)

### Campaign Finance
- Has pledged to **decline any campaign contributions from the insurance industry** -- a direct contrast with Hawkins' insurance industry background
- Specific fundraising totals not found in available reporting

### Platform
- **Lowering costs** for consumers
- **Consumer protection** -- standing up for policyholders
- **Holding "big insurance companies accountable"**
- **Transparency** in insurance policies and rates
- **Fighting unfair practices and discrimination** in insurance
- **Affordable healthcare and childcare**
- **Public education** funding
- **Medicaid expansion**
- **Access to abortion**
- **Protections for survivors** of domestic violence, sexual assault, human trafficking, and stalking
- **Public school funding and early childhood education**

### Legislative Record
- Has served in the Kansas Senate since 2017 (9 years)
- Champion for public school funding, early childhood education
- Advocate for Medicaid expansion
- Protections for survivors of domestic violence, sexual assault, human trafficking, stalking
- Full voting record available at [kslegislature.gov](https://www.kslegislature.gov/li/b2025_26/members/sen_sykes_dinah_1/)

### Endorsements (SIGNIFICANT)
Two former Kansas Insurance Commissioners have endorsed Sykes -- one from each party:

1. **Kathleen Sebelius** (Democrat) -- former Insurance Commissioner, former Kansas Governor, former U.S. Secretary of Health and Human Services:
   *"As long as I've known Dinah, she's stood up for what's right and fought for Kansas families."*

2. **Sandy Praeger** (Republican) -- former Insurance Commissioner:
   *"Kansans want leaders who will listen to them and fight against unfair and discriminatory practices by the industry."* Called Sykes *"a practical leader, focused on garnering results over partisanship."*

**Assessment**: Having BOTH a Democratic and Republican former Insurance Commissioner endorse you is extraordinary. Praeger's endorsement in particular is a powerful signal that Sykes has genuine crossover appeal and that the "moderate Republican" wing of Kansas politics sees her as credible.

### Key Quotes
- On her party switch: *"I am a moderate person who represents a moderate and pragmatic district... being a moderate inside the Republican Party is an increasingly difficult path to take with the trajectory of the party nationally."* (December 2018, multiple sources)
- On her insurance commissioner platform: Focused on *"lowering costs, consumer protection and holding big insurance companies accountable."* (Kansas Reflector, January 2026)

### Electability Assessment
**Strengths**: 9 years in the Kansas Senate. Senate Minority Leader. Former Republican -- speaks directly to moderate/crossover voters. Bipartisan endorsements from two former Insurance Commissioners. The no-insurance-industry-money pledge is a powerful contrast with Hawkins. Hawkins' SB 360 debacle is a gift to her campaign. Johnson County base is the most Democratic-leaning area in Kansas.
**Weaknesses**: Running as a Democrat in a Republican state. The party switch will be attacked as betrayal by Republican voters. Her platform (Medicaid expansion, abortion access) is standard Democratic fare that may limit crossover appeal with conservative voters who might otherwise be open to an insurance reformer. "Personal chef and PTA president" before politics is a thinner pre-political resume than Hawkins' 30 years of insurance expertise.

### Red Flags
- The party switch will be a central Republican attack line.
- Some conservative outlets (BizPac Review, 2018) accused her and other switching legislators of running as Republicans specifically to win in GOP districts and then switching -- calling it a "betrayal of voters."

### Endorsements
- **Kathleen Sebelius** (D) -- former Kansas Governor, HHS Secretary, Insurance Commissioner
- **Sandy Praeger** (R) -- former Insurance Commissioner

---

## INSURANCE COMMISSIONER RACE: HEAD-TO-HEAD COMPARISON

| Factor | HAWKINS (R) | SYKES (D) |
|--------|------------|-----------|
| **Insurance Expertise** | 30 years in industry (CLU designation) | No insurance industry background |
| **Political Experience** | House member since 2012; Speaker since 2023 | State Senator since 2017; Minority Leader since 2021 |
| **Military** | Kansas National Guard (SSgt, retired 1991) | None |
| **Education** | Hutchison CC, Emporia State, CLU | Trevecca Nazarene University |
| **Fundraising** | ~$384K cash on hand (end of 2025) | Unknown; pledged no insurance industry money |
| **Endorsements** | Pro-Trump branding | Sebelius (D) + Praeger (R) -- BIPARTISAN |
| **Key Vulnerability** | SB 360 blocking; insurance industry conflict | Party switch; Democrat in red state |
| **Branding** | "Pro-Life. Pro-Gun. Pro-Trump." | Consumer champion; anti-industry |
| **Party Registration Edge** | Heavy R advantage statewide | Johnson County D base |

### The Central Question
Can Sykes replicate the Laura Kelly / 2022 abortion referendum formula -- winning enough moderate Republicans and independents to overcome Kansas's structural Republican advantage? The Sebelius + Praeger dual endorsement and the SB 360 controversy give her a credible path. But Hawkins has significantly more money and the default partisan advantage.

This race is **genuinely competitive** in a way that the Senate race is not. Insurance Commissioner is a lower-profile office where partisanship matters less and "who will actually protect consumers" matters more. Sykes has a real shot here.

---

## SOURCE: Kris-Kobach-Complete-Dossier.md

# COMPLETE DOSSIER: Kris William Kobach (R)
## Kansas Attorney General -- Seeking Re-Election 2026
## Compiled: March 31, 2026

# SECTION 1: FULL BIOGRAPHY

## Personal Information

- **Full Name**: Kris William Kobach
- **Born**: March 26, 1966 (age 60)
- **Residence**: Farm near Lecompton, Kansas (north of Lawrence), Douglas County
- **Party**: Republican
- **Wife**: Heather Mannschreck Kobach (married June 23, 2001, at St. Michael's Episcopal Church in Kansas City, KS)
- **Children**: Five daughters -- Josephine, Lilly, Charlotte, Reagan, and Molly (all homeschooled)
- **Wife's Background**: B.S. in Biological and Biosystems Engineering, University of Nebraska (2000). Worked as environmental scientist/engineer at Black & Veatch (2000-2008). Operates part-time photography business "Kobagraphy."
- **Church**: Married at St. Michael's Episcopal Church, Kansas City, KS. Reported attendance at Open Door Baptist Church, Kansas City, KS (as of 2018; current status unverified).
- **Property Note**: In 2014, Kobach was cited for using his Lecompton property as a residence when it was only permitted for agricultural use. He subsequently obtained proper residential permits.

Sources:
- [Heather Kobach: 5 Fast Facts](https://heavy.com/news/2018/08/heather-kobach-kris-kobach-wife-kansas/)
- [Kris Kobach - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kris_Kobach)
- [Kris Kobach for AG - Meet Kris](https://kriskobach.com/meet-kris/)

---

## Education

### Harvard University -- B.A. in Government (1988)
- Graduated **summa cum laude**
- **Ranked first in his department**
- This is a Harvard undergraduate degree, NOT Yale as the user initially suggested

### University of Oxford, Brasenose College -- Ph.D. in Politics
- Attended on a **Marshall Scholarship** (one of the most prestigious academic awards for American students to study in the UK)
- Earned a Doctor of Philosophy (Ph.D.) in Politics -- this is confirmed as a full doctorate, not just coursework

### Yale Law School -- J.D. (1995)
- Served as **articles editor** (some sources say "notes development editor") for the **Yale Law Journal**
- Multiple sources conflict on the graduation year -- some say 1992, others 1995. The 1995 date is more consistent with his subsequent clerkship timeline (1995-1996 with Judge Tacha).

**IMPORTANT CORRECTION**: The user asked about "Yale (BA), Oxford (PhD?), Harvard Law (JD)." The actual order is: **Harvard (BA), Oxford (PhD), Yale (JD)**. Kobach's undergraduate degree was from Harvard, not Yale. His law degree was from Yale, not Harvard Law.

Sources:
- [Federalist Society - Kris Kobach Bio](https://fedsoc.org/bio/kris-kobach-1)

# SECTION 2: SECRETARY OF STATE RECORD (2011-2019)

## The SAFE Act and Documentary Proof of Citizenship (DPOC)

In 2011, Kobach persuaded the Kansas Legislature to pass the Kansas Secure and Fair Elections (SAFE) Act, his signature legislation. It required all new voter registrants to present documentary proof of U.S. citizenship (birth certificate, passport, or naturalization papers) before being allowed to register. The law took effect in 2013.

**Impact**: More than **35,000 eligible Kansas voters** were blocked from registering under this law.

**The Trial -- Fish v. Kobach (2018)**:
- Trial hearings ran March 6-19, 2018, before Chief U.S. District Judge Julie A. Robinson
- Kobach personally served as lead attorney defending the law (despite being Secretary of State, not a practicing litigator)
- Judge Robinson **struck down the DPOC law as unconstitutional** on June 18, 2018, finding it violated the National Voter Registration Act and the Equal Protection Clause of the 14th Amendment
- Robinson's 118-page opinion was a point-by-point dismantling of Kobach's arguments
- She found that Kobach could demonstrate only **39 cases of noncitizen voter registration** in Kansas over a nearly 20-year period out of 1.8 million registered voters
- She noted Kobach's "evidence of the iceberg" theory of widespread fraud was not supported by any credible evidence

Sources:
- [Fish v. Kobach - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish_v._Kobach)
- [NPR: Judge Tosses Kansas Proof-of-Citizenship Voter Law](https://www.npr.org/2018/06/19/621304260/judge-tosses-kansas-proof-of-citizenship-voter-law-and-rebukes-sec-of-state-koba)
- [ACLU Kansas - Federal Judge Rules](https://www.aclukansas.org/news/federal-judge-rules-favor-aclu-strikes-down-kobachs-illegal-voter-restrictions/)

---

## Contempt of Court Finding

On **April 18, 2018**, Judge Julie Robinson found Kobach **in contempt of court** for failing to comply with a prior court order requiring him to register voters whose applications were in "suspense" status due to lack of proof of citizenship.

**Sanctions imposed**:
- Ordered to pay **$26,215 in attorney's fees and expenses** ($24,658 in fees + $1,557 in expenses) to the ACLU
- **Ordered to take remedial legal education classes** -- specifically, Kobach was ordered to complete **six hours of continuing legal education on federal or Kansas rules of civil procedure or evidence** (an extraordinary humiliation for someone with degrees from Harvard, Oxford, and Yale)

Additionally, Kobach was sanctioned earlier in the case for attempting to introduce a document (a Homeland Security strategic plan) that he concealed from opposing counsel. The judge found he had tried to **smuggle evidence into the courtroom** that had not been disclosed during discovery.

Sources:
- [ACLU: Court's Ruling Holding Kobach in Contempt](https://www.aclu.org/news/voting-rights/courts-ruling-holding-kobach-contempt-well-deserved)
- [KSHB: Kobach Ordered to Pay $26K for Contempt](https://www.kshb.com/news/state/kansas/judge-orders-kobach-to-pay-more-than-26000-for-contempt)
- [ACLU Kansas: Kansas Drops Kobach Appeal of Contempt](https://aclukansas.org/news/kansas-drops-kris-kobachs-appeal-contempt-ruling-aclu-accepts-20000-legal-fees/)

---

## Presidential Advisory Commission on Election Integrity (2017-2018)

- **Established**: May 11, 2017, by executive order of President Donald Trump
- **Purpose**: Investigate Trump's claim that 3-5 million illegal votes were cast in the 2016 election
- **Chair**: Vice President Mike Pence
- **Vice Chair / Day-to-Day Administrator**: Kris Kobach
- **Disbanded**: January 3, 2018 -- after only 7 months and 2 public meetings

**What happened**:
- Multiple states (both Republican and Democratic) **refused to turn over voter data** to the commission
- Democratic member (Maine Secretary of State Matthew Dunlap) sued the commission for **refusing to share internal documents** with him
- A federal judge ordered the commission to hand over documents to Dunlap
- Those documents revealed that a **draft of the commission's final report had a section on evidence of voter fraud that was "glaringly empty"**
- Dunlap stated the documents showed a **"pre-ordained outcome"** -- the commission appeared designed to reach a conclusion of widespread fraud regardless of evidence
- **The commission found NO evidence of widespread voter fraud**
- Trump disbanded it, blaming states' refusal to cooperate

**Cost to taxpayers**: The commission spent federal funds on operations, travel, and staff for 7 months while producing no report and no findings of fraud.

Sources:
- [Presidential Advisory Commission on Election Integrity - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_Advisory_Commission_on_Election_Integrity)
- [Brennan Center: Disbanded Trump's Voter Fraud Commission](https://www.brennancenter.org/our-work/research-reports/disbanded-trumps-voter-fraud-commission)
- [NPR: Trump Dissolves Controversial Election Commission](https://www.npr.org/2018/01/03/575524512/trump-dissolves-controversial-election-commission)
- [PBS: Report Says Commission Found No Widespread Fraud](https://www.pbs.org/newshour/politics/report-trump-commission-did-not-find-widespread-voter-fraud)
- [Rolling Stone: Kobach and Trump's Spectacular Voter Fraud Failure](https://www.rollingstone.com/politics/politics-features/kris-kobach-donald-trump-voter-fraud-myths-vote-suppression-990300/)

---

## Interstate Crosscheck Voter Purge System

**What it was**: The Interstate Voter Registration Crosscheck Program (IVRC), administered by the Kansas Secretary of State's office under Kobach, aggregated voter registration records from participating states to identify voters who appeared to be registered in more than one state.

**Scale of voter removals**: An estimated **1.1 million voters had their registrations purged** across 30 states before the 2016 election based on Crosscheck data.

**Accuracy problems**:
- The system flagged **7.2 million voters** total
- **Less than one in a million** of those flagged had actually voted twice
- For every double vote prevented, Crosscheck impeded approximately **300 legitimate registrations**
- The system disproportionately impacted minority voters: **1 in 6 Latino voters, 1 in 7 Asian-American voters, and 1 in 9 Black voters** in participating states were flagged
- Common names (e.g., "James Brown," "Maria Garcia") triggered false matches at extremely high rates because the system matched primarily on first name, last name, and date of birth without verifying Social Security numbers

**Collapse of the program**:
- Ten states withdrew from Crosscheck before it was suspended
- In **December 2019**, the program was **suspended indefinitely** as part of an ACLU of Kansas lawsuit settlement
- Security failures were also cited -- voter data was transmitted between states via unencrypted methods

Sources:
- [Interstate Voter Registration Crosscheck Program - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_Voter_Registration_Crosscheck_Program)
- [Common Cause: Crosscheck System Shuttered](https://www.commoncause.org/democracy-wire/crosscheck-system-shuttered-after-wrongly-tagging-legal-voters/)
- [The Fulcrum: Interstate Crosscheck Closed Over Security Failure](https://thefulcrum.us/interstate-crosscheck-program)
- [Greg Palast: Interstate Crosscheck on the Verge of Collapse](https://www.gregpalast.com/interstate-crosscheck-on-the-verge-of-collapse/)
- [Truthout: Kansas Kills Kobach's National Voter Purge System](https://truthout.org/articles/kansas-kills-kris-kobachs-national-voter-purge-system/)

---

## Cost to Kansas Taxpayers from Lost Lawsuits

The Fish v. Kobach case and subsequent appeals resulted in massive taxpayer costs:

- **$1.4 million** paid to the ACLU (attorneys' fees settlement)
- **$475,000** paid to Dentons US LLP (co-counsel fees)
- **Total direct settlement: ~$1.9 million** approved by the Kansas Legislature's Joint Committee on Special Claims Against the State

But it got worse:
- Former AG Derek Schmidt continued appealing Kobach's loss, pushing total legal costs to an estimated **$4 million+**
- This does not include the internal costs of Kansas state employees' time spent on the litigation

Additionally:
- Kobach was personally ordered to pay **$26,215** for his contempt sanction
- Kansas dropped the appeal of the contempt ruling, with the ACLU accepting **$20,000** in legal fees related to the appeal

**Total estimated cost to Kansas taxpayers from Kobach's voter proof-of-citizenship law: $4+ million**

Sources:
- [Kansas Reflector: Kobach, Kansas AG and Legislature to Blame for Voting Law Legal Costs](https://kansasreflector.com/2022/03/24/kobach-kansas-ag-and-legislature-to-blame-for-voting-law-legal-costs-representatives-say/)
- [Lawrence Times: Kansas' Own Million Dollar Man](https://lawrencekstimes.com/2022/10/17/weiss-letter-6m-man/)
- [KCUR: ACLU Says Kobach Owes $52K](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2018-05-08/aclu-says-kobach-owes-52k-in-legal-costs-for-contempt-in-kansas-voting-case)
- [DGA: Derek Schmidt Continues Kobach's Legacy of Costing Taxpayers Millions](https://democraticgovernors.org/updates/icymi-derek-schmidt-continues-kris-kobachs-legacy-of-costing-taxpayers-millions/)

# SECTION 3: ATTORNEY GENERAL RECORD (January 2023-Present)

## Major Lawsuits Filed as AG

### Federal/Multistate Litigation (Anti-Biden Administration)

1. **Biden Parole Program Lawsuit (January 2023)**: Joined 18-state coalition (led by Texas) suing over DHS parole program allowing entry for migrants from Cuba, Haiti, Nicaragua, and Venezuela (30,000/month). Status: Ongoing as of initial filing; program was subsequently modified.

2. **Biden "Amnesty" Program for Spouses (2024)**: Led/joined 16-state coalition challenging program granting legal status to undocumented immigrants married to U.S. citizens. **WON** -- Federal judge in Texas struck down the program in November 2024.

3. **DACA Health Insurance Lawsuit (2024-2025)**: Led 19-state challenge to Biden rule enabling ~200,000 DACA recipients to enroll in ACA marketplace plans. **Won preliminary injunction**. Voluntarily dismissed in December 2025 after Trump rescinded the Biden-era rule.

4. **Title IX Transgender Regulations (May 2024)**: Sued Biden administration over rewrite of Title IX rules to include protections for LGBTQ+ students. Joined by Alaska, Utah, Wyoming. **Won preliminary injunction** (July 2024) blocking implementation nationwide -- declared it a "sweeping victory affecting all 50 states."

5. **Student Loan Forgiveness Lawsuit**: Joined multistate challenge resulting in a **nationwide injunction** from a federal judge in Kansas blocking Biden's student loan forgiveness plan.

6. **Census Apportionment Lawsuit (January 2025)**: Filed with Louisiana, Ohio, and West Virginia AGs to stop Census Bureau from counting undocumented immigrants for congressional reapportionment in 2030.

7. **ESG/Vanguard-BlackRock-State Street Lawsuit**: Joined Texas-led 13-state coalition suing major asset managers over alleged ESG collusion. **Settlement with Vanguard** (February 2026): Vanguard agreed to strict passivity commitments and **$29.5 million payment** to participating states.

### State-Level Litigation

8. **Kansas v. Harper -- Transgender ID/Driver's License Case (July 2023)**: Filed against Kansas Department of Revenue to prohibit transgender people from changing gender markers on driver's licenses. Kobach **lost on appeal** -- Kansas Court of Appeals lifted trial court's injunction (June 2025), finding Kobach "had not shown a substantial likelihood of prevailing" and there was "no evidence beyond mere speculation" of harm. Kansas Supreme Court **denied** Kobach's appeal (September 2025). In January 2026, a judge issued a **symbolic $1 fine** against Kobach for filing a motion in a court without jurisdiction -- the judge said Kobach "should have known better."

9. **SB 244 -- Transgender Bathroom/ID Law (2026)**: After losing in courts, Kobach went to the legislature. SB 244 requires use of bathrooms in government buildings and gender markers on IDs based on sex assigned at birth. Penalties up to **$125,000/day** for government entities that violate. Kobach agreed to pause enforcement until March 26, 2026, while a judge weighed a challenge. A Douglas County judge **denied** plaintiffs' request for a temporary restraining order, allowing the law to remain in effect.

10. **Pfizer COVID Vaccine Lawsuit (June 2024)**: Filed civil suit under Kansas Consumer Protection Act alleging Pfizer misled public about vaccine safety and efficacy. Alleges Pfizer knew of adverse events (myocarditis, pericarditis, failed pregnancies, deaths) and concealed them; claims Pfizer said vaccine prevented transmission when it never studied that. **Won jurisdictional battle** -- federal judge remanded case back to Kansas state court after Pfizer tried to remove it. Case ongoing.

11. **Kelly v. Kobach / SNAP Data Dispute (2025-2026)**: Kobach sued Gov. Kelly in September 2025 for refusing to release SNAP (food assistance) recipient data to the Trump administration. A Shawnee County judge **dismissed** Kobach's lawsuit. Kelly then filed a counter-suit directly with the Kansas Supreme Court alleging Kobach was undermining her constitutional authority. Kansas Supreme Court **dismissed** Kelly's petition on narrow procedural grounds (March 27, 2026). Both sides declared victory. The court's opinion stated the governor may litigate to protect executive interests, and the AG may not enlarge his authority to bar that exercise.

12. **Snapchat Lawsuit**: Sued Snap Inc. alleging deceptive and unconscionable acts harming consumers, particularly teenagers.

13. **THC Smoke Shop Raids (2025-2026)**: Kobach's office directed raids on smoke shops in October 2025. Three shops subsequently sued the state alleging **Fourth Amendment violations** (illegal search and seizure). Defendants include KBI Director Tony Mattivi and AG Kobach. Case pending as of March 2026.

### Consumer Protection Cases

14. **Mercedes-Benz Settlement (December 2025)**: Joined 50-state AG coalition securing **$149 million settlement** for unfair/deceptive trade practices.

15. **Menards Settlement**: Kansas and 9 other states investigated Menards for business practices during COVID-19 pandemic. Settlement required Menards to pay Kansas **$81,570.75**.

16. **All Seasons Lawn, Tree and Landscape LLC**: Filed consumer protection suit against Jeremy Lord and his company for alleged violations.

17. **Missouri Construction Company**: Filed suit against door-to-door construction company for aggressive, deceptive sales tactics targeting elderly residents in Manhattan, KS.

Sources:
- [Kansas AG News Releases](https://www.ag.ks.gov/media-center/news-releases)
- [Kansas Reflector: Kobach AG Record Coverage](https://kansasreflector.com/tag/kris-kobach/)
- [Kansas AG: Vanguard ESG Settlement](https://www.ag.ks.gov/Home/Components/News/News/280/1292)
- [Kansas Reflector: Pfizer Lawsuit](https://kansasreflector.com/2024/06/17/kansas-ag-kobach-accuses-pfizer-of-misleading-vaccine-marketing-in-lawsuit/)
- [Kansas Reflector: Kelly v. Kobach](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/03/27/kansas-governor-attorney-general-both-declare-victory-in-supreme-court-decision-on-executive-power/)
- [Kansas Reflector: Transgender Law](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/03/06/kansas-ag-offers-to-delay-enforcement-of-anti-trans-law-until-march-26-while-judge-weighs-challenge/)
- [Kansas Reflector: THC Raids Lawsuit](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/03/26/kansas-smoke-shops-sue-state-alleging-illegal-search-and-seizure-during-thc-raids/)
- [Kansas Reflector: Gender Marker $1 Fine](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/01/20/kansas-judge-rebukes-ag-kris-kobach-in-gender-marker-case-issues-symbolic-1-fine/)

---

## Fentanyl Enforcement Initiative

One of Kobach's signature AG programs:
- Created the **Joint Fentanyl Impact Team** in 2023
- Deployed the **first fentanyl-detecting K-9 officers** in Kansas (4 dogs trained and certified)
- Seized approximately **25,000 counterfeit oxycodone pills** from a Wichita operation early in the initiative
- Kansas Legislature added **5 FTE positions** to KBI for the team in FY2024, then **30 FTE positions and $6.9 million** in FY2025 for "Fight Against Fentanyl"
- **$8.5 million** in Kansas Fights Addiction grants awarded to 32 organizations (December 2024)
- **$177,000 grant** approved to convert unused news racks into naloxone distribution boxes (August 2025)

Sources:
- [Kansas Reflector: Kobach Fentanyl Initiative](https://kansasreflector.com/2023/07/20/ag-kobach-to-announce-ongoing-initiative-combating-fentanyl-in-kansas-here-are-the-basics/)
- [Kansas AG: Kansas Fights Addiction Grants](https://www.ag.ks.gov/Home/Components/News/News/139/1292)
- [KLRD: Kansas Law Enforcement Fentanyl Response](https://klrd.gov/2024/12/18/kansas-law-enforcement-fentanyl-response/)

---

## Staff and Management Issues

- **Chief Deputy AG Dan Burrows** departed Kansas to join the Trump administration (2025)
- Kobach **fired Morgan & Morgan**, a Florida law firm handling the state's natural gas price-gouging lawsuit, in March 2023. The firm's founder, John Morgan (a prominent Biden donor), alleged the firing was **politically motivated retribution** for Democratic campaign donations. Kobach initially cited "performance" issues but had to backpedal and rebid the contract after legal experts warned the firing could constitute unlawful retaliation, jeopardizing the state's case.
- Reports of broader staffing challenges, but specific data on overall turnover rates was not found in public reporting.

Sources:
- [Above the Law: Kobach Fires Law Firm That Donated to Democrats](https://abovethelaw.com/2023/05/kris-kobach-fires-law-firm-that-donated-to-democrats-clumsily-backpedals-after-realizing-legal-ramifications-of-retaliation/)

---

## Crime Statistics Under Kobach's AG Tenure

Kobach's campaign claims:
- Kansas crime index rate dropped from **27.0 offenses per 1,000 people (2023)** to **23.3 per 1,000 (2024)**
- The 2024 rate was reportedly the **lowest since at least 2003**
- His campaign calls this "the lowest crime rate in 20 years"

**Context**: The AG's office plays a limited direct role in crime reduction. The decrease is part of a broader national trend of declining crime rates from 2022-2024 peaks. Attributing statewide crime drops to the AG is a common political claim by both parties and should be evaluated skeptically.

Sources:
- [Kansas AG: Reelection Announcement](https://kriskobach.com/)
- [Tony's Kansas City: Did Kobach Cut Crime?](https://www.tonyskansascity.com/2025/07/did-kansas-ag-kobach-cut-crime.html)

# SECTION 4: ELECTION HISTORY

## 2022 Attorney General Race (Won)

| Candidate | Votes | Percentage |
|-----------|-------|------------|
| Kris Kobach (R) | 498,869 | 50.8% |
| Chris Mann (D) | 481,506 | 49.1% |

- **Margin**: 17,363 votes (1.7 points) -- the **closest statewide race in Kansas** in the 2022 cycle
- Mann initially refused to concede, citing uncounted mail and provisional ballots
- This was the closest AG race in Kansas in decades
- Note: On the same ballot, Kansas voters **overwhelmingly rejected** a constitutional amendment that would have removed abortion protections (59%-41%), and Gov. Laura Kelly (D) **won reelection** by 3 points. Kobach significantly underperformed the typical Republican statewide margin.

Sources:
- [NBC News: 2022 Kansas AG Results](https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2022-elections/kansas-attorney-general-results/)
- [KCUR: Kobach Squeaks to Political Comeback](https://www.kcur.org/news/2022-11-09/kansas-attorney-general-election-results-2022-kris-kobach-chris-mann)
- [Kansas Reflector: Mann Concedes](https://kansasreflector.com/2022/11/11/mann-surrenders-quest-to-overtake-kobach-in-kansas-race-for-attorney-general/)

---

## 2018 Governor's Race (Lost)

### Republican Primary

| Candidate | Votes | Result |
|-----------|-------|--------|
| Kris Kobach | ~127,000 | Won by ~345 votes |
| Gov. Jeff Colyer | ~126,655 | Conceded without recount |

- The **closest statewide GOP primary in Kansas history**
- Initial margin was just 191 votes on election night, fluctuated during counting
- Colyer conceded on August 14, 2018, when his deficit stood at ~345 votes
- Trump endorsed Kobach via tweet the day before the primary

### General Election

| Candidate | Votes | Percentage |
|-----------|-------|------------|
| Laura Kelly (D) | ~506,000 | 48% |
| Kris Kobach (R) | ~453,000 | 43% |
| Greg Orman (I) | ~73,000 | 7% |

**Why Kobach lost**:
1. **Sam Brownback's shadow**: Kobach was closely associated with former Gov. Sam Brownback's failed "real live experiment" in supply-side economics, which had gutted Kansas schools and services
2. **Independent candidate split**: Greg Orman pulled ~7% as an independent, likely drawing from moderate Republicans who couldn't stomach Kobach
3. **Record voter turnout**: Over 1 million Kansans voted in the governor's race (compared to under 870,000 in 2014). Higher turnout typically benefits Democrats.
4. **Moderate Republican revolt**: Kelly earned endorsements from **every living Republican former governor of Kansas except Brownback**
5. **Kobach's polarizing image**: His national profile on immigration and voter fraud alienated suburban voters in Johnson County, which swung heavily toward Kelly
6. **The contempt finding**: Being held in contempt of court and ordered to take remedial law classes was devastating to his credibility, all happening in the months before the election

Sources:
- [2018 Kansas Gubernatorial Election - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_Kansas_gubernatorial_election)
- [CNN: Kelly Wins Kansas](https://www.cnn.com/2018/11/06/politics/kansas-governor-laura-kelly-democrat/index.html)
- [KCUR: Kelly Beats Kobach](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2018-11-07/kelly-beats-kobach-promises-shell-ditch-partisan-ways-as-governor)
- [NPR: Kobach Wins GOP Primary](https://www.npr.org/2018/08/14/638703832/trump-ally-kris-kobach-wins-primary-for-kansas-governor-as-gop-incumbent-concede)

## Other Election History

- **2010 Secretary of State**: Won with ~60% of the vote
- **2014 Secretary of State**: Won reelection
- **2004 Kansas 3rd Congressional District**: Lost to incumbent Democrat Dennis Moore
- **2000 Kansas State Senate**: Finished third in Republican primary
- **1999 Overland Park City Council**: Won
