# SECTION 5: IMMIGRATION LAW CAREER

## Overview

Before and during his time as Secretary of State, Kobach maintained a lucrative side practice as an immigration enforcement attorney, working primarily for the Immigration Reform Law Institute (IRLI, the legal arm of the Federation for American Immigration Reform/FAIR) and for municipalities seeking to pass anti-immigration ordinances.

## Immigration Ordinances -- Win/Loss Record

### ProPublica's Analysis: **2-6 win-loss record** in federal cases reaching final disposition

| Municipality | What Happened | Result |
|-------------|---------------|--------|
| **Hazleton, PA** | Drafted housing/employment ordinance penalizing landlords and businesses that hired/housed undocumented immigrants | **LOST** -- Third Circuit struck down both provisions as preempted by federal law (July 2013) |
| **Farmers Branch, TX** | Drafted ordinance preventing landlords from renting to undocumented immigrants | **LOST** -- Struck down after years of litigation |
| **Fremont, NE** | Drafted anti-immigration ordinance | **WON** -- One of Kobach's few victories |
| **Valley Park, MO** | Anti-immigration ordinance | **Partial** -- Only a watered-down version survived |
| **Arizona SB 1070** (2010) | Kobach helped draft the "show me your papers" law | **Mostly LOST** -- U.S. Supreme Court struck down 3 of 4 challenged provisions as preempted by federal law; upheld only the "papers" provision with restrictions |

**Financial costs to municipalities**:
- **Farmers Branch, TX**: Owed **$7 million** in legal bills
- **Hazleton, PA**: Took on debt, eventually had to **seek a state bailout** to pay **$1.4 million+** in legal costs. The privately raised defense fund (which had paid Kobach $250,000) ran dry by 2013.
- **None** of the towns where Kobach helped enact anti-immigration ordinances over a 13-year period still have those ordinances on the books.

**Kobach's personal earnings**: Over **$800,000** from immigration-related legal work since 2005, paid by municipalities and anti-immigration advocacy groups, including at least **$150,000** earned while serving as Secretary of State.

## Incomplete Financial Disclosures

ProPublica found that Kobach's Kansas financial disclosure forms began showing **fewer and fewer clients** around the time of his 2014 reelection campaign:
- His 2014 form listed only Fremont, despite receiving over $40,000 from Hazleton and $12,000 from Farmers Branch
- His 2015 form again listed only Fremont, despite receiving $5,500 from Hazleton and $3,650 from Farmers Branch

Sources:
- [ProPublica: Kris Kobach's Lucrative Trail of Courtroom Defeats](https://www.propublica.org/article/kris-kobachs-lucrative-trail-of-courtroom-defeats)
- [SPLC: When Mr. Kobach Comes to Town](https://www.splcenter.org/resources/reports/when-mr-kobach-comes-town-nativist-laws-and-communities-they-damage/)
- [Arizona SB 1070 - Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arizona_SB_1070)

---

# SECTION 6: CAMPAIGN FINANCE

## FEC Fine -- We Build the Wall

- In December 2022, the **Federal Election Commission fined Kobach $30,000** for campaign finance violations during his 2020 U.S. Senate campaign
- The violation: Kobach's campaign rented We Build the Wall's **295,000-person email fundraising list** for just **$2,000** -- far below market rate
- The FEC determined the below-market-rate access constituted an unreported **in-kind corporate contribution** from We Build the Wall
- **Kobach's connection to We Build the Wall**: He served as **General Counsel** and sat on the organization's **Board of Directors/Advisory Board**
- We Build the Wall was the Steve Bannon-linked organization that raised millions for a private border wall. Bannon was later **indicted for fraud** related to the organization (pardoned by Trump), and organizer Brian Kolfage was **sentenced to 51 months in prison** for fraud
- Kobach was not charged with fraud but his close association with a fraudulent organization raises serious questions

## Epstein Files Connection

Kobach's name appeared in the Jeffrey Epstein files released by the House Oversight Committee, but the connection was **indirect and limited**:
- Steve Bannon texted Epstein on May 25, 2019, mentioning Kobach by name in the context of the We Build the Wall project
- Bannon wrote: "can't ; have kobach and kolfage on site -- I'm the chairman but I push those 2 plus the construction guy as national heroes"
- There is **no evidence Kobach ever communicated directly with Epstein**
- The mention was simply Bannon bragging to Epstein about the wall project

## 2026 Campaign Finance

- Filed for reelection January 8, 2026
- Reported **$502,626 cash on hand** -- claimed to be the highest January 1 total ever reported by a Kansas AG candidate
- Specific donor and industry breakdowns for the 2026 cycle are available through the Kansas Public Disclosure Commission (kpdc.kansas.gov) and FollowTheMoney.org

Sources:
- [CNN: Kobach Fined for Campaign Finance Violations](https://www.cnn.com/2022/12/30/politics/kansas-attorney-general-campaign-finance-violations/index.html)
- [Kansas Reflector: Kobach FEC Fine](https://kansasreflector.com/2022/12/31/kobachs-u-s-senate-campaign-we-build-the-wall-hit-by-30000-fine-for-campaign-law-violations/)
- [Yahoo News: Epstein Files and Kobach](https://www.yahoo.com/news/articles/jeffrey-epstein-files-kris-kobach-100825234.html)

# SECTION 7: COMPLETE COURT/SANCTIONS RECORD

## Summary of Sanctions, Contempt, and Judicial Rebukes

| Date | Court/Judge | Action | Details |
|------|------------|--------|---------|
| **April 2018** | Judge Julie Robinson, U.S. District Court, Kansas | **Held in contempt of court** | Failed to comply with order to register voters in DPOC case |
| **April 2018** | Judge Julie Robinson | **$26,215 in sanctions** | Attorney's fees and expenses paid to ACLU |
| **2018** | Judge Julie Robinson | **Ordered to take 6 hours of CLE classes** | Remedial legal education on civil procedure/evidence |
| **2018** | Judge Julie Robinson | **Sanctioned for concealing evidence** | Attempted to introduce undisclosed Homeland Security document at trial |
| **June 2018** | Judge Julie Robinson | **Full loss -- DPOC law struck down** | 118-page opinion dismantling Kobach's case on every major point |
| **January 2026** | Judge Thomas Luedke, Kansas District Court | **Symbolic $1 fine** | Filed motion in court lacking jurisdiction in gender marker case; judge said Kobach "should have known better" |
| **December 2022** | Federal Election Commission | **$30,000 fine** | Illegal in-kind contribution from We Build the Wall during 2020 Senate race |

## Additional Judicial Criticism

- Judge Robinson noted in her 2018 opinion that Kobach's expert witness (political scientist Jesse Richman) had produced "fatally flawed" research
- Judge Robinson wrote that Kobach's trial conduct reflected that he was "unfamiliar with the federal rules" and failed to follow basic discovery requirements
- The ACLU of Kansas has characterized Kobach's litigation pattern as consistently involving "bad lawyering" leading to losses followed by legislative attempts to achieve what courts rejected

# SECTION 8: CONTROVERSIAL STATEMENTS AND QUOTES

## On Voter Fraud
- Claimed Trump's tweet about millions voting illegally was **"absolutely correct"** -- despite producing only 11 cases of voter fraud in Kansas from 18+ years of records when challenged in court
- At trial, could demonstrate only **39 cases of noncitizen voter registration** in Kansas over nearly 20 years out of 1.8 million registered voters

## On Homosexuality (2012)
- At the 2012 Republican National Convention in Tampa, while serving as a Mitt Romney surrogate and debating the GOP platform's marriage equality language, Kobach compared homosexuality to drug abuse and polygamy:
- **Quote**: "Our government routinely judges situations where you might regard people completely affecting themselves... like for example the use of controlled substances, like for example polygamy, that is voluntarily entered into. We condemn those activities even though they are not hurting other people, at least directly."
- He was arguing against an amendment that would have ended the party's support for the Defense of Marriage Act (DOMA)

## On Immigration
- Coined and promoted the concept of **"self-deportation"** -- making conditions so hostile that undocumented immigrants would leave voluntarily
- **Quote**: "If you really want to create a job tomorrow, you can remove an illegal alien today."
- Served as the intellectual architect behind many of the most restrictive immigration enforcement proposals at the state and local level

## On Transgender Issues
- Led a letter to the U.S. Department of Education criticizing proposed rules allowing transgender athletes in girls'/women's sports
- Pushed for legislation requiring government buildings to restrict bathroom access by birth sex, with penalties up to $125,000/day
- After losing the driver's license gender marker case in court, went to the legislature to pass SB 244 to achieve the same goal legislatively -- the ACLU characterized this as a "power grab" and "poor sportsmanship over his recent losses"

## On COVID Vaccines
- Filed a consumer protection lawsuit against Pfizer alleging the company "misled the public that it had a 'safe and effective' COVID-19 vaccine"
- Alleged Pfizer knew of connections to myocarditis, pericarditis, failed pregnancies, and deaths
- Alleged Pfizer worked to "censor speech on social media that questioned Pfizer's claims"

Sources:
- [LGBTQ Nation: Romney Surrogate Compares LGBT People to Drug Users](https://www.lgbtqnation.com/2012/08/top-romney-surrogate-compares-lgbt-people-to-drug-users-polygamists/)
- [GLAAD: Kris Kobach](https://glaad.org/gap/kris-kobach/)
- [ACLU Kansas: AG Kobach Power Grab](https://www.aclukansas.org/press-releases/aclu-of-kansas-responds-to-ag-kobachs-power-grab-and-effort-to-change-law-after-losses/)
- [ProPublica: How the Case for Voter Fraud Was Tested](https://www.propublica.org/article/kris-kobach-voter-fraud-kansas-trial)
- [America's Voice: Who is Kris Kobach](https://americasvoice.org/blog/kris-kobach/)

# SECTION 9: 2026 RACE -- KOBACH vs. MANN REMATCH

## Kobach's 2026 Campaign

- **Filed**: January 8, 2026
- **Cash on hand**: $502,626 (as of January 1, 2026)
- **Campaign message**: Low crime rates, anti-Biden lawsuits, immigration enforcement partnership with Trump, fentanyl enforcement, ESG/Vanguard settlement
- **Primary**: August 4, 2026 (no announced Republican challengers)
- **General**: November 3, 2026

## Chris Mann (D) -- Challenger

- **Announced**: July 30, 2025
- **Background**:
  - Lawrence, Kansas resident
  - Former **police officer** -- became a cop at age 21 during his junior year of college
  - In 2002, at age 25, was **hit by a drunk driver during a traffic stop**, forcing him to retire from law enforcement
  - After retirement from police work, attended and graduated from **law school**
  - Worked as a **prosecutor in Wyandotte County**
  - Served at the **Kansas Securities Commission**
  - Opened his own **private law firm** in Lawrence in 2016
  - **National Chairman of Mothers Against Drunk Driving (MADD)** -- served on the national board since 2014, advocated for Kansas's vehicle ignition lock law for DUI offenders
  - Has never held elective office
- **Family**: Wife Ashley is a surgeon practicing in Olathe
- **Campaign Treasurer**: Jill Docking (2014 Democratic candidate for lieutenant governor)
- **Platform**: "Defend the rule of law, protect our rights, protect our families and make Kansas a safer place to live." Emphasizes reorienting the AG's office toward **basics of law enforcement** rather than partisan federal lawsuits.
- **2022 performance**: Lost to Kobach by only 1.6 points (481,506 votes to 498,869) -- the closest statewide race in Kansas that cycle

**Key dynamics for 2026**:
- Mann nearly won in 2022 despite low name recognition and Kobach's built-in advantage as a Republican in Kansas
- The 2022 abortion referendum showed Kansas voters are more moderate than the state's Republican leadership
- Kobach's record as AG gives Mann significantly more ammunition than he had in 2022
- Trump will not be on the 2026 ballot, which could affect Republican turnout

Sources:
- [Kansas Reflector: Kansas AG Election 2026 May Repeat 2022](https://kansasreflector.com/2025/07/30/kansas-election-for-attorney-general-in-2026-may-become-a-repeat-of-2022-showdown/)
- [Chris Mann for Kansas](https://chrismannforkansas.com/)
- [WIBW: Mann Announces Second Bid](https://www.wibw.com/2025/07/30/democrat-chris-mann-announces-second-bid-kansas-ag/)
- [Emporia News: 2026 Race](https://emporianews.com/2026-kansas-attorney-general-race-could-mirror-2022-as-chris-mann-announces-candidacy-against-kris-kobach/)

# SECTION 10: RED FLAGS

## Legal Competence Concerns
1. **Held in contempt of federal court** (2018) for violating a judge's order
2. **Ordered to take remedial law classes** -- a Harvard/Oxford/Yale-educated lawyer ordered to learn basic rules of civil procedure
3. **Sanctioned for concealing evidence** at trial
4. **$30,000 FEC fine** for illegal campaign contribution
5. **Symbolic $1 fine** from Kansas judge in 2026 for filing in wrong jurisdiction
6. **2-6 win-loss record** on immigration ordinance cases that cost cities millions
7. Consistent pattern of judicial rebukes -- multiple judges across jurisdictions have criticized his legal work

## Financial Concerns
8. **$4+ million cost to Kansas taxpayers** from DPOC litigation and appeals
9. **$800,000+ in personal income** from immigration consulting while elected officials -- with **incomplete financial disclosures** that failed to list all paying clients
10. Cities that hired him (Hazleton, Farmers Branch) were left with millions in legal bills -- one had to seek a state bailout
11. Association with **We Build the Wall**, a fraudulently run organization (Bannon pardoned, Kolfage sentenced to prison)

## Pattern of Losing Then Legislating
12. After courts reject his legal arguments, he goes to the legislature to pass laws achieving the same goals -- documented in the driver's license gender marker case and bathroom bills
13. The ACLU calls this a "power grab" pattern

## Voter Suppression Record
14. **35,000+ eligible Kansas voters** blocked from registering under his DPOC law
15. **1.1 million voters purged** across 30 states by Interstate Crosscheck, with massive racial disparities
16. Led a presidential commission that found **zero evidence** of the widespread fraud it was created to investigate, then was disbanded

## Political Retaliation Allegation
17. Fired Morgan & Morgan law firm from the natural gas price-gouging case, allegedly because the firm's founder donated to Democrats -- had to backtrack after legal experts warned of retaliation liability

---

# SECTION 11: GREEN FLAGS

## Legitimate Accomplishments

1. **Fentanyl enforcement**: Built a genuinely operational program with K-9 units, $6.9 million in legislative funding, seized thousands of counterfeit pills, distributed naloxone
2. **Kansas Fights Addiction grants**: $8.5 million distributed to 32 organizations for substance use disorder treatment
3. **Pfizer lawsuit**: Regardless of one's view of COVID vaccines, filing a consumer protection case alleging a pharmaceutical company misled the public is within the AG's traditional consumer protection role. He won the jurisdictional battle to keep it in state court.
4. **ESG/Vanguard settlement**: Secured tangible reforms and $29.5 million in payments to participating states
5. **Mercedes-Benz settlement**: Part of 50-state coalition securing $149 million
6. **Crime statistics**: Kansas crime rate did decline during his tenure (though attribution is debatable)
7. **Title IX injunction**: Won a nationwide preliminary injunction on Biden's Title IX rewrite -- a major legal victory regardless of one's policy position
8. **Biden amnesty program struck down**: Federal judge sided with Kobach's coalition
9. **Student loan forgiveness blocked**: Part of successful multistate litigation
10. **Murder conviction**: Secured conviction of Steven Couch Jr. for a 2011 cold case murder (sentenced to life)
11. **Academic credentials**: The Harvard/Oxford/Yale pedigree is genuinely exceptional, even if his courtroom performance hasn't always matched it

## Bipartisan Actions
12. Consumer protection lawsuits against local contractors and deceptive businesses are traditional, non-partisan AG functions
13. The fentanyl and addiction treatment work is broadly supported across the political spectrum

# SECTION 14: OVERALL ASSESSMENT

## The Kobach Paradox

Kris Kobach presents a genuine paradox. He holds elite academic credentials from three of the world's most prestigious universities (Harvard, Oxford, Yale). He has been a law professor, a White House Fellow, and counsel to the U.S. Attorney General. On paper, he should be one of the most formidable lawyers in state government.

And yet, the record shows a consistent pattern of **overreach followed by courtroom failure**:
- He drafted immigration ordinances that were struck down across the country, leaving cities bankrupt
- He passed a voter proof-of-citizenship law that was struck down, costing Kansas $4+ million
- He was held in contempt of court and ordered to take remedial law classes
- He led a presidential commission that found nothing and was disbanded
- He administered a voter crosscheck system that purged 1.1 million legitimate voters with a false positive rate exceeding 99.9999%
- He lost a governor's race in a deep-red state

As AG, his record is more mixed. He has secured genuine consumer protection settlements, built a functional fentanyl enforcement program, and won significant federal injunctions against Biden administration policies. But he has also continued the pattern of overreach -- losing the gender marker case in court, then going to the legislature; directing smoke shop raids now facing Fourth Amendment challenges; and engaging in an unprecedented power struggle with the Governor.

## The 2026 Race

Kobach won by only 1.6 points in 2022 in a state where Republicans typically win statewide by 10+ points. The 2022 abortion referendum revealed a Kansas electorate far more moderate than its Republican establishment. Chris Mann is a credible challenger with a compelling personal story (former cop hit by a drunk driver, national MADD chairman).

Kobach's advantages: incumbency, $502,626 cash on hand, Trump alignment in a red state, tangible AG accomplishments to point to (fentanyl program, federal litigation wins).

Kobach's vulnerabilities: razor-thin 2022 margin, extensive record of courtroom losses and judicial sanctions, the Morgan & Morgan firing, ongoing THC raid lawsuit, the cost of his SOS-era litigation to taxpayers, and the fact that his most prominent work as AG (anti-Biden lawsuits, anti-transgender litigation) may not resonate with the moderate suburban voters who determine close Kansas races.

## SOURCE: KS-01-2026-challengers-investigation.md

# KS-01 2026: Comprehensive Investigation of All Challengers to Rep. Tracey Mann

**Investigation Date**: March 30, 2026
**Investigator**: Internet Investigator (Claude Agent)
**Classification**: DEEP SCRUB -- All Candidates, All Parties

---

## RACE OVERVIEW

**District**: Kansas 1st Congressional District (the "Big First")
**Incumbent**: Rep. Tracey Mann (R), in office since 2021, won three terms with ~70% of the vote each time
**Cook PVI**: R+16 (64th most Republican district nationally)
**Primary Date**: August 4, 2026
**General Election**: November 3, 2026
**Historical Context**: Only ONE Democrat has ever won this seat -- Howard Miller, in 1952. Republicans have held it for 150 of the last 150+ years.
**District Geography**: Covers 60+ counties spanning over half the state. Includes Manhattan, Salina, Dodge City, Garden City, Hays, McPherson, Hutchinson, and (since 2022 redistricting) Lawrence.

### ALL FILED CANDIDATES (per FEC and Ballotpedia as of March 2026):

| Candidate | Party | Status | FEC ID |
|-----------|-------|--------|--------|
| Tracey Mann | Republican (incumbent) | Running in GOP primary | H0KS01123 |
| Colin McRoberts | Democrat | Running in Dem primary | H6KS01195 |
| Lauren Reinhold | Democrat | Running in Dem primary | Not yet confirmed |
| Craig Musser | United Kansas Party (Independent) | Filed for general election | Filed Feb 14, 2026 |

**No Republican primary challenger to Mann has been identified.**
**No Libertarian candidate has been identified.**

## CANDIDATE 1: COLIN McROBERTS (Democrat)

### Identity & Vital Information

- **Full Legal Name**: Kenneth Colin McRoberts
- **Residence**: Lawrence, Kansas (Douglas County)
- **Occupation**: Associate Teaching Professor of Law, University of Kansas School of Business
- **Party**: Democrat (notably, was NOT registered as a Democrat for years prior to running)
- **Campaign Filed**: September 17, 2025
- **FEC Candidate ID**: H6KS01195
- **FEC Committee**: Colin for Kansas (C00919860)

### Education

- **B.A. in International Studies**, Trinity University, San Antonio, TX (2001)
- **J.D. (Law Degree)**, Harvard Law School (2004)

### Career Timeline

1. **Steptoe & Johnson LLP** -- Commercial litigator after Harvard Law. Practiced commercial litigation, secured multimillion-dollar wins for clients. Fought in courtroom to protect family businesses from fraud.
2. **Vasher McRoberts LLC** -- Founded his own consulting firm focused on negotiation and communication analysis. Advised major corporations, unions, diplomatic teams, government institutions worldwide. Worked with Fortune 500 businesses, diplomats, and military special forces in dozens of countries.
3. **University of Kansas School of Business** -- Associate Teaching Professor of Law. Teaches business law, business fundamentals, and a course on the origin and spread of conspiracy theories. Award-winning professor.
4. **University of Missouri-Kansas City** -- Also teaches negotiation to MBA students.
5. **Author & Researcher** -- Published in Aeon Magazine and Wired. Writes the blog "Violent Metaphors." Published chapter "A Symbol for Hope: Superman's Battle with the KKK as a Model for Effective Cultural Engagement with Conspiracy Theories" in *The Lizard People Don't Want You to Read This* (McFarland, 2025). Working on book titled *The Good Fight* about how irrational ideas capture rational people.
6. **ConspiraSea Cruise (2016)** -- Attended a seminar-at-sea for conspiracy theorists as research for his book. Ran a GoFundMe to fund attendance. Blogged extensively about it. Interviewed by Skeptical Inquirer, Token Skeptic podcast, and featured on Kansas Public Radio.
7. **Licensed with State Bar of Texas** (Kenneth Colin McRoberts).

### Family

- Married with children (specific names not publicly available)
- "Was not born in Kansas, but chose to move there with his wife to teach and start their family"
- Has lived in Lawrence, Kansas for a significant period

### Why He Is Running

McRoberts was directly inspired by Sen. Roger Marshall's contentious town hall in Oakley, Kansas on March 1, 2025. He drove four and a half hours from Lawrence to Oakley to hear what Marshall would say about Health Secretary Robert F. Kennedy Jr. and vaccines. He ended up taking one of the videos that went viral when Marshall was booed by constituents and left the event abruptly.

### Campaign Platform & Positions

**On Tariffs & Agriculture:**
- Return tariff power to Congress (away from executive branch)
- Legislate a small business exemption to tariffs allowing family farms to import items with no reasonable domestic substitute at reasonable cost
- Open foreign markets for American crops

**On USAID:**
- Restore U.S. Agency for International Development and its mission of buying American crops to prevent famine overseas

**On Social Programs:**
- Protect Social Security and Medicare

**On Government Accountability:**
- Defend rights of workers and teachers
- Restore Congressional oversight on trade

**On Executive Overreach:**
- Cited what he describes as illegal actions including tariffs, federalized troop deployments, ICE arrests of U.S. citizens, arrests over speech, and firing federal employees during a shutdown

### Verbatim Quotes (with Sources)

> "The long odds are exactly why this fight is so important. Gerrymandering and partisanship have kept our incumbent politicians safe even as they give up on representing Kansans in order to serve national donors and powerbrokers. This campaign is about giving Kansans the power to choose a better deal."
-- Campaign announcement, September 17, 2025 (colinforkansas.com; KWCH)

> "He does not care what that vote does. He doesn't care what it does to his neighbors. He doesn't care what it does to the rest of Kansas. He doesn't care what it does to the rest of the world, as long as it serves his interests, makes the party happy, gets him more qualified to one day go to the Senate or take some other easy, easy, no-fight election."
-- On Tracey Mann, Kansas Reflector, January 5, 2026

> "I think that's been going on for a long time, an intentional strategy to use the east against the west, and maybe to a lesser extent, the west against the east, to drive these wedges for the benefit of party politics. And I will not and cannot play that game. We're all neighbors. The 1st District is much more alike than it is different."
-- Kansas Reflector, January 5, 2026

> "The first district is red in a red state. This is not going to be an easy race, it's not going to be a cheap race, it's not going to be a short race, but it's possible to win in a way it hasn't been before."
-- Kansas Democracy Fest in Hays (Hays Post)

> "I'm running not as a politician, but as a businessman and negotiator."
-- Kansas Democracy Fest in Hays (Hays Post)

### Social Media & Online Presence

- **Campaign Website**: [colinforkansas.com](https://colinforkansas.com/)
- **Instagram**: [@colinforkansas](https://www.instagram.com/colinforkansas/)
- **Facebook**: [facebook.com/colinforkansas](https://www.facebook.com/colinforkansas)
- **Bluesky**: [@colinmcroberts.bsky.social](https://bsky.app/profile/colinmcroberts.bsky.social)
- **LinkedIn**: [linkedin.com/in/colin-mcroberts-5781291](https://www.linkedin.com/in/colin-mcroberts-5781291/)
- **Personal/Consulting Website**: [colin-mcroberts.com](https://www.colin-mcroberts.com/)
- **KU Faculty Page**: [business.ku.edu/people/colin-mcroberts](https://business.ku.edu/people/colin-mcroberts)
- **Rate My Professors**: [ratemyprofessors.com/professor/2506562](https://www.ratemyprofessors.com/professor/2506562)
- **Take Back Congress Profile**: [take-bac-congress.us/team/colin-mcroberts](https://www.take-bac-congress.us/team/colin-mcroberts)

### Campaign Finance

- **FEC Candidate ID**: H6KS01195
- **Committee**: Colin for Kansas (C00919860)
- **Note**: Specific fundraising totals not available from search results. Most recent FEC filing covers July 1 - December 31, 2025. Full financial data available at [fec.gov/data/candidate/H6KS01195](https://www.fec.gov/data/candidate/H6KS01195/) and [fec.gov/data/committee/C00919860](https://www.fec.gov/data/committee/C00919860/).

### Endorsements & Affiliations

- Listed with **Take Back Congress** (a Democratic candidate recruitment organization)
- Attended and spoke at **Kansas Democracy Fest** in Hays (Kansas Democratic Party event)

### News Coverage

1. KWCH, Sept 17, 2025: "Colin McRoberts files for 1st Congressional District seat"
2. Kansas Reflector, Jan 5, 2026: "Lawrence Democrats take aim at Kansas Republican's congressional seat"
3. Lawrence Journal-World, Jan 7, 2026: "Lawrence Democrats take aim at Mann's congressional seat"
4. Hays Post: "Kansas Democrats wrap up Democracy Fest in Hays"
5. US Resist News, Feb 4, 2026: "2026 Democratic Primary Preview Series: Kansas (Brief #10)"

### Red Flags / Controversies

- **Not a lifelong Democrat**: He openly acknowledged he "wasn't registered as a Democrat for years." This could be used against him in a primary or general election.
- **Lives in Lawrence**: While Lawrence is technically in KS-01 (since 2022 redistricting), it is the most liberal city in the district and culturally distinct from western Kansas. This is a vulnerability -- opponents can paint him as an eastern Kansas liberal running in a western Kansas district.
- **Harvard Law + conspiracy theory research**: While impressive credentials, in a deep-red R+16 district, the "elite coastal education + studying conspiracy theories" combination could be weaponized in attack ads.
- **No prior political experience**: First-time candidate. Has never held elected office.
- **No court records or criminal history found** in searches.

### Assessment

McRoberts is the more polished and better-resourced of the two Democratic candidates. He has a real professional pedigree (Harvard Law, international consulting, university professor), a clear campaign message centered on negotiation and deal-making, and came to the race with a viral moment (the Marshall town hall video). He is running a "businessman, not politician" campaign in a district where that frame has appeal. His weakness is that he lives in Lawrence, has no roots in western Kansas, and is running in a district where a Democrat hasn't won since 1952. The Cook PVI of R+16 means he would need roughly a 16-point swing from the national environment to even be competitive, which is historically unprecedented for this district.

---

## CANDIDATE 2: LAUREN REINHOLD (Democrat)

### Identity & Vital Information

- **Full Name**: Lauren Elizabeth Reinhold
- **Date of Birth**: October 2, 1970 (age 55)
- **Residence**: Lawrence, Kansas (Douglas County)
- **Occupation**: Attorney (28 years experience), former federal employee (Social Security Administration)
- **Party**: Democrat
- **Religion**: Christian (per public records)
- **FEC Filing Status**: Campaign active; specific FEC candidate ID not confirmed in search results. Committee details available at [fec.gov/data/elections/house/KS/01/2026](https://www.fec.gov/data/elections/house/KS/01/2026/).

### Education

- **J.D.**, University of Kansas School of Law (attended starting 1993)
- Undergraduate education: Not confirmed in search results

### Career Timeline

1. **Attorney/Owner, Reinhold Law Office, LLC** -- Private practice in Lawrence, Kansas
2. **Staff Attorney, University of Kansas Legal Services for Students** -- Legal aid for KU students
3. **Managing Attorney, Carter Law Firm** -- Iowa
4. **Attorney-Adviser, Social Security Administration** -- Federal employment, worked on disability cases and administrative law
5. **Federal Union Officer** -- Worked in human resources advocating for federal employees
6. **Federal Administrative Law Judge** (per some references, though this may overlap with attorney-adviser role)
7. **Volunteer/Board Member, Kansas Lawyers Assistance Program (KALAP)** -- Lawyer wellness organization

### Personal Background

- Lived in Topeka until age 6, then moved to St. Louis
- Returned to Kansas in 1993 to attend KU Law School
- Stayed in Kansas to raise a family
- Currently resides in Lawrence
- Married (husband's name not public)
- Related to/associated with: Kent M. Clasen, Martin Reinhold

### Why She Is Running

Reinhold was directly catalyzed by the DOGE purge of federal employees. She was working at the Social Security Administration when she received the email from DOGE urging federal employees to quit in exchange for pay through September (late January 2026). She initially resisted, then decided that if they fire her, she could run for Congress. She eventually accepted the buyout offer and is now running full-time.

### Campaign Platform & Positions

**On Government Services:**
- "I really care that the American people get the government they deserve, that we get the governmental services we need and deserve to make our lives better."

**On Healthcare:**
- "Healthcare you can count on" is a central campaign pillar
- Criticized broken promises on healthcare

**On Wages & Economy:**
- "Wages you can raise a family on"

**On Protecting Kansas:**
- "If anyone in Washington wants to push policies that hurt our farmers, our hospitals, our workers, or our towns, they'll have to go through me first."

**On Tracey Mann:**
- Reinhold accuses Mann of "spending his life enriching and protecting the wealthy," ignoring constituents, refusing to take real stances on foreign policy or federal overreach, and voting to cut funding for health and safety

### Verbatim Quotes (with Sources)

> "I was a proud public servant. When DOGE pushed hardworking employees like me out the door, I decided if Washington won't fight for people, then I will."
-- Campaign announcement (laurenforkansas.com)

> "I could run for Congress and try to fight this mess they've made of the federal government. Fight back and restore what the American people need."
-- Kansas Reflector, January 5, 2026

> "It's not about me. It's not about, oh, poor Lauren lost her job to DOGE. I really care that the American people get the government they deserve, that we get the governmental services we need and deserve to make our lives better."
-- Kansas Reflector, January 5, 2026

> "If anyone in Washington wants to push policies that hurt our farmers, our hospitals, our workers, or our towns, they'll have to go through me first."
-- Campaign website (laurenforkansas.com)

> "I was told they would fix health care."
-- Campaign messaging (various)

### Social Media & Online Presence

- **Campaign Website**: [laurenforkansas.com](https://www.laurenforkansas.com)
- **LinkedIn**: [linkedin.com/in/laurenreinhold](https://www.linkedin.com/in/laurenreinhold/)
- **Facebook Video**: Spoke at Douglas County Democrats meeting about exploratory campaign ([facebook.com/dgcodems](https://www.facebook.com/dgcodems/videos/2299093513898616/))
- **No Twitter/X, Instagram, or Bluesky accounts found** in searches

### Campaign Finance

- FEC committee details not confirmed via search results. Check [fec.gov/data/elections/house/KS/01/2026](https://www.fec.gov/data/elections/house/KS/01/2026/) for most current filings.

### Campaign Activity

- Traveled across the Big First before announcing -- stopped in Hays, Dodge City, Salina, Hutchinson, and "dozens of rural towns"
- Spoke at the Friendship Center in Salina (746 Commanche Ave), December 2025
- Spoke at Douglas County Democrats meeting about exploratory campaign
- Running a "go-everywhere" grassroots campaign

### How She Differs from McRoberts

| Factor | McRoberts | Reinhold |
|--------|-----------|----------|
| Trigger for running | Marshall town hall (March 2025) | DOGE purge (Jan 2026) |
| Professional identity | Harvard lawyer, professor, negotiator | 28-year practicing attorney, federal employee |
| Campaign pitch | "Businessman and negotiator" | "I fought for workers, I'll fight for you" |
| Core issue | Tariffs, executive overreach, trade | Government services, healthcare, DOGE |
| Filing date | September 2025 | Late 2025/early 2026 |
| Age | Not public | 55 |
| Tone | Analytical, policy-focused | Personal, emotional, worker-advocate |

### News Coverage

1. Kansas Reflector, Jan 5, 2026: "Lawrence Democrats take aim at Kansas Republican's congressional seat"
2. Lawrence Journal-World, Jan 7, 2026: "Lawrence Democrats take aim at Mann's congressional seat"
3. Salina Post: "Reinhold, 1st Congressional District candidate to speak in Salina"
4. KCN Online, Jan 5, 2026: "Two Lawrence Dems Seek 1st District Seat"

### Red Flags / Controversies

- **Also lives in Lawrence**: Same geographic vulnerability as McRoberts. Both Democrats are from the same city, which is the most liberal enclave in an otherwise deeply conservative district.
- **DOGE narrative could cut both ways**: While "fired federal employee fights back" plays well with Democrats, in R+16 KS-01, many voters may sympathize with DOGE's mission to cut government. Her origin story could actually hurt her with the general electorate.
- **Later entry**: Filed months after McRoberts, giving her less time to build name recognition and fundraise.
- **MyLife.com notation**: One public records site notes "Has Court or Arrest Records" but this could refer to anything from a traffic ticket to professional court appearances as an attorney. This needs further investigation before drawing conclusions.
- **No statewide or national profile**: Zero previous political experience.

### Assessment

Reinhold has a compelling personal story -- a federal worker displaced by DOGE who channeled her anger into a congressional run. Her 28 years of legal experience and time as a federal union officer give her deep institutional knowledge. However, she entered later than McRoberts, has less apparent fundraising infrastructure, less visible social media presence, and faces the same fundamental math problem: KS-01 is R+16. In the Democratic primary, her worker-advocate, DOGE-survivor message may resonate with primary voters who are energized by anti-Trump sentiment. Whether that's enough to beat McRoberts in the primary depends heavily on fundraising and ground game.

---

## CANDIDATE 3: CRAIG MUSSER (United Kansas Party / Independent)

### Identity & Vital Information

- **Full Name**: Craig A. Musser
- **Residence**: 570 SE 50 Road, Ellinwood, KS 67526 (Barton County)
- **Occupation**: Manager, Environment, Health & Safety at PureField Ingredients (Russell, KS)
- **Party**: United Kansas Party (officially recognized as Kansas's 5th political party in May 2024)
- **Campaign Filed**: February 14, 2026 (FEC Form 2)
- **FEC Committee**: Craig Musser for Congress
- **Running in**: General election (November 3, 2026) -- does NOT go through a primary

### Education

- **B.S.**, Bucknell University (Lewisburg, PA)
- **B.S.**, Shippensburg University of Pennsylvania
- **M.S. in SSEM / Occupational Safety / Safety Leadership**, Eastern Kentucky University
- **M.B.A.**, Frostburg State University (Maryland)

### Career Timeline

1. **Process Engineer, Merck & Co.** -- Pharmaceutical manufacturing
2. **Maintenance Engineer & Process Engineer, Ply Gem** -- Building products manufacturing
3. **Safety Project Engineer, Specialty Granules**
4. **Manager, Maintenance, Agy** -- Glass fiber manufacturer
5. **Manager, Maintenance, Optima Chemical Group**
6. **Director, Health For Kansas Manufacturing, Jacam Catalyst** -- Oilfield chemicals (Sterling, KS)
7. **Manager, Environment, Health & Safety, PureField Ingredients** -- Current role. PureField is a wheat protein (vital wheat gluten) and biofuels manufacturer in Russell, Kansas. Senator Jerry Moran has visited the facility.

### Personal Background

- Located in the Wichita, Kansas Metropolitan Area (per LinkedIn) but lives in Ellinwood, KS
- Ellinwood is a small town (population ~2,000) in Barton County, deeply within the KS-01 district
- **He actually lives in the heart of the Big First**, unlike both Democratic candidates who are in Lawrence
- Engineering and safety management background spanning pharmaceutical, chemical, glass, and agricultural industries
- Originally from the eastern United States (educated in Pennsylvania, Maryland, Kentucky)

### Why He Is Running

Musser is running under the banner of the United Kansas Party, a newly formed (2024) cross-partisan party. He is positioning himself as an alternative to both the Republican and Democratic parties.

### About the United Kansas Party

- **Founded**: 2024 by Jack Curtis
- **Official Recognition**: May 24, 2024, by Kansas Secretary of State Scott Schwab after collecting 35,152 petition signatures
- **Kansas's 5th recognized political party**
- **Core Strategy**: Advocates for "fusion voting" -- nominating candidates from existing parties on the United Kansas ballot line
- **Platform**: Cross-partisan, centrist. Focuses on voter choice, strong schools, affordable housing, accessible healthcare, accountable leadership
- **Website**: [unitedkansas.com](https://unitedkansas.com/)
- **Facebook**: [facebook.com/unitedksparty](https://www.facebook.com/unitedksparty/)
- **Prior Candidates (2024)**: Nominated 3 candidates for Kansas House and Senate races
- **Legal Activity**: Filed lawsuits challenging Kansas law forbidding multi-party nominations (Kansas Reflector, July 12, 2024)

### Campaign Platform & Positions

**On Representation:**
- "Kansans deserve a representative who serves them -- not donors, party bosses or Washington insiders."

**On Women's Rights:**
- "Every Kansan, particularly women whose rights are being eroded by the incumbent party, has the right to self-determination and freedom from government intrusion into their personal lives."

**On Tax & Healthcare:**
- Will "bring discipline to fixing the tax code and healthcare system that are failing too many Kansans."

**On Education:**
- "Every student deserves access to a quality education."

**On Governance Philosophy:**
- "Effective governance is not about ideology -- it's about listening and delivering outcomes."

### Verbatim Quotes (with Sources)

> "Kansans deserve a representative who serves them - not donors, party bosses or Washington insiders. I'm running to be that representative."
-- Campaign announcement (Hays Post, Great Bend Post)

> "Effective governance is not about ideology -- it's about listening and delivering outcomes."
-- Campaign announcement (Hays Post, Great Bend Post)

### Social Media & Online Presence

- **No personal campaign website found** in searches
- **LinkedIn**: [linkedin.com/in/craig-musser-82880838](https://www.linkedin.com/in/craig-musser-82880838/)
- **United Kansas Party**: [unitedkansas.com/candidates](https://unitedkansas.com/candidates)
- **No Twitter/X, Instagram, Facebook, or Bluesky campaign accounts found**

### Campaign Finance

- Filed FEC Form 2 (Statement of Candidacy) on February 14, 2026
- Committee: "Craig Musser for Congress"
- No financial reports found in search results -- this is a very new filing and may not yet have substantive fundraising data
- Check [fec.gov](https://www.fec.gov/data/) for updates

### News Coverage

1. Hays Post: "Kansas First Congressional District has a new candidate"
2. Great Bend Post: "Kansas First Congressional District has a new candidate"
3. NewsBreak (via JC Post): "Kansas First Congressional District has a new candidate"

### Red Flags / Controversies

- **Extremely limited campaign infrastructure**: No campaign website, no social media campaign accounts, minimal news coverage. This is a bare-bones operation.
- **New party, unproven**: United Kansas Party was only recognized in 2024 and has never won a race. Fusion voting strategy is untested in Kansas.
- **Not from Kansas originally**: Educated entirely in eastern states (PA, MD, KY). Has worked in Kansas at Jacam and PureField, so he does have Kansas industrial experience.
- **No court records, criminal history, or controversies found**.

### Assessment

Craig Musser is the most enigmatic candidate in the race. He has the strongest geographic credentials of any challenger (he actually lives in the rural heart of KS-01, in Ellinwood), and his industrial/manufacturing background is the most aligned with the district's working-class character. But he has virtually no campaign infrastructure -- no website, no social media, no visible fundraising. The United Kansas Party is a new and unproven vehicle. His platform includes a reference to women's rights and self-determination that would be notable and potentially strategic in a post-Dobbs Kansas (where voters overwhelmingly rejected an anti-abortion amendment in 2022). However, without money, media, and organization, he is essentially a placeholder candidate at this stage.

### Other Third-Party Candidates

- **Committee**: Mann for Congress (C00460659)
- **OpenSecrets Profile**: [opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/tracey-mann/summary?cid=N00030743](https://www.opensecrets.org/members-of-congress/tracey-mann/summary?cid=N00030743)
- **Last three elections**: Won with approximately 70% of the vote each time
- **Specific 2026 fundraising totals**: Not extracted from search results; check FEC/OpenSecrets links above

## COMPARATIVE ANALYSIS

### Strengths by Candidate

| Factor | McRoberts | Reinhold | Musser |
|--------|-----------|----------|--------|
| Professional credentials | HIGHEST (Harvard Law, international consulting) | HIGH (28 years law, federal service) | MODERATE (engineering, MBA, safety management) |
| Campaign infrastructure | MOST DEVELOPED (website, social media, endorsements) | DEVELOPING (website, some events) | MINIMAL (FEC filing only) |
| Geographic fit with KS-01 | WEAK (Lawrence) | WEAK (Lawrence) | STRONG (Ellinwood, rural Barton County) |
| Compelling narrative | MODERATE (professor turned activist) | STRONG (DOGE survivor, worker advocate) | WEAK (limited public narrative) |
| Name recognition | LOW-MODERATE (some press coverage) | LOW (limited press) | NEGLIGIBLE |
| Party infrastructure | MODERATE (Democratic Party) | MODERATE (Democratic Party) | VERY LOW (brand-new party) |
| Cultural fit with KS-01 | LOW (academic, liberal Lawrence) | LOW-MODERATE (worker identity helps) | MODERATE (industrial, rural) |

### The Fundamental Math Problem

Kansas 1st is R+16. Tracey Mann wins with ~70%. For any challenger to win:

- A Democrat would need roughly every Democratic vote PLUS a massive crossover of Republican/independent voters
- The 2022 Kansas abortion vote showed rural Kansans can break with the GOP on specific issues, but that hasn't translated to candidate elections
- The Lawrence redistricting adds Democratic votes but also adds cultural friction with western Kansas voters
- Both Democrats are from Lawrence, which is a significant liability in a district where Lawrence is viewed with suspicion by many rural voters

### Most Likely Outcome

Based on all available evidence, **Tracey Mann wins re-election easily.** The most competitive scenario would be if national conditions deteriorate dramatically for Republicans AND one of the Democrats runs a near-perfect campaign. Even then, the structural disadvantage is enormous. The Democratic primary between McRoberts and Reinhold will be the only competitive element of this race. McRoberts appears better positioned to win the primary based on earlier entry, more developed campaign infrastructure, and broader platform. Musser's candidacy is significant mainly as a test case for the United Kansas Party brand.

---

## SOURCE: plain-english-voter-guide.md

# PLAIN ENGLISH VOTER GUIDE: 2026 KANSAS ELECTIONS
### Written for Hays voters who want the truth, not the spin
#### Last Updated: March 31, 2026

---

# PART ONE: THE TWO BALLOT MEASURES

These are constitutional amendments. They change the Kansas Constitution itself. You vote YES or NO. There is no candidate -- just the question.

---

## AMENDMENT 1: Should Kansas Voters Elect Supreme Court Justices?

**On your ballot: August 4, 2026 (PRIMARY election -- not November)**

---

### What This Amendment Would Do

Right now, when there is an opening on the Kansas Supreme Court, a 9-person commission (5 lawyers elected by other lawyers, 4 non-lawyers picked by the governor) reviews the applicants, picks 3 finalists, and sends those names to the governor. The governor picks one. Then every 6 years, you get to vote YES or NO on keeping that justice (a "retention vote").

This amendment would scrap that entire system. Instead, you would vote for Supreme Court justices the same way you vote for governor or senator -- in regular elections. Seven justices would be phased in through elections in 2028, 2030, and 2032. The 9-person nominating commission would be abolished permanently.

**The catch nobody is talking about:** The amendment does NOT say whether these elections would be partisan (Republican vs. Democrat) or nonpartisan. It does NOT say how campaigns would be financed. It does NOT say what the nomination process would look like. ALL of those details would be decided later by the Kansas Legislature -- which is controlled by a Republican supermajority. As retired Kansas Supreme Court Justice Carol Beier put it: "It is exceedingly vague. It will be decided by the Legislature. Do you trust them?"

---

### Why This Exists -- The Real History

This fight did not come out of nowhere. There are three things that made Kansas Republicans angry enough to put this on the ballot:

**1. The Abortion Ruling (2019):** The Kansas Supreme Court ruled 6-1 that the Kansas Constitution protects a right to "personal autonomy," including the right to decide whether to continue a pregnancy. This made Kansas one of the strongest states for abortion rights -- decided by appointed justices, not elected ones.

**2. The School Funding Wars (2005-2024):** For nearly 20 years, the Kansas Supreme Court told the Legislature it was not funding public schools adequately. The court repeatedly ordered lawmakers to spend more money on education. Conservative legislators were furious about being told how to spend taxpayer money by judges they did not elect.

**3. Kobach's Losses in Court:** Attorney General Kris Kobach has had multiple laws struck down by Kansas courts, including his proof-of-citizenship voter registration law.

Kansas Reflector explicitly headlined their coverage: "Kansas Senate adopts plan to elect Supreme Court justices, a step toward overturning abortion rights."

**The 1958 origin story:** Kansas adopted its current system after one of the most embarrassing scandals in state history. In 1956-57, Governor Fred Hall lost his reelection bid, his friend the Chief Justice conveniently resigned, Hall himself resigned with 11 days left in office, and his Lieutenant Governor (who had to be pulled out of a hospital by a Highway Patrolman) was briefly elevated to Governor just long enough to appoint Hall to the Supreme Court. Kansans were so disgusted by this backroom deal that they voted to create the nominating commission system in 1958. It has been in place for 67 years.

---

### Why Supporters Want This

**Their core argument:** The people should choose their judges. Period. Democracy means voting.

Attorney General Kris Kobach: "People, not only lawyers in smoke-filled back rooms, should have a voice in selecting Kansas Supreme Court justices."

Americans for Prosperity-Kansas (Koch-funded conservative group): "The current process involves a commission of trial attorneys selecting nominees behind closed doors with no input from Kansans or their elected legislators."

Kobach has cited polling showing 74% of Kansans support directly electing Supreme Court justices. **However:** That polling came from Kobach's own office, and the way you ask the question matters enormously. "Should you get to vote for judges?" always polls well. "Should judges have to raise millions from special interests to win partisan campaigns?" polls very differently. No independent public polling on this specific amendment has been released.

**Who voted for it in the Legislature:** The amendment passed the Kansas Senate 27-13 and the House 84-40. It required a two-thirds supermajority in both chambers. 93% of Republicans voted YES. Democrats almost unanimously voted NO. It passed by the absolute minimum number of votes -- if ONE more legislator in either chamber had voted no, it would not be on your ballot.

---

### Why Opponents Fight This

**Their core argument:** This will turn Kansas courts into political war zones funded by out-of-state billionaires.

Micah Kubic, ACLU of Kansas: "Partisan elections quickly become fights between out-of-state, big money interests. These elections become less about the voters and constituents of the state and more an opportunity for out-of-state big money interests to wage war against one another."

Retired Justice Carol Beier: "Opening the process up to expensive popular elections financed by special interests was contrary to the idea of an independent judiciary."

Teresa Woody, Kansas Appleseed: "It would be impossible for elections of Supreme Court justices to be anything other than partisan brawls."

Rep. Rui Xu (D-Westwood): "Republicans are mad that our Supreme Court wanted us to fully fund school and not ban abortions so now they want to change the Supreme Court."

**Organizations opposing:** Kansas Bar Association, ACLU of Kansas, American Federation of Teachers-Kansas, Kansas Appleseed Center for Law and Justice, Kansas Association of School Boards, Kansas Women Attorneys Association, Planned Parenthood Great Plains Votes, VoteNoKansas.org, Stand Up Blue Valley.

---

### What You Need to Know -- The Facts That Cut Through the Spin

**FACT 1: This is on the August PRIMARY ballot, not November.** Primary turnout in Kansas is typically 20-25%, compared to 50-60% in November. Republican voters dominate primary turnout because they have more contested races. Putting it on the primary ballot is widely seen as a strategy to pass it with a smaller, more conservative electorate. The exact same strategy was used for the 2022 abortion amendment -- and it backfired spectacularly when turnout surged to nearly 50% and the amendment was crushed 59-41.

**FACT 2: The amendment is deliberately vague.** It says justices will be elected but leaves every important detail -- partisan vs. nonpartisan, campaign finance rules, nomination process -- to the Legislature. The Legislature has a Republican supermajority.

**FACT 3: Other states that elect judges have seen massive spending.** Wisconsin's 2025 Supreme Court race cost $144.5 million for a single seat. Elon Musk alone spent over $25 million on one side. North Carolina elected a conservative court majority, and those new justices immediately reheard and reversed decisions on redistricting and voting rights that had been issued just months earlier.

**FACT 4: The opposition has raised nearly $2 million.** The pro-side has dark money backing (see below).

**FACT 5: Kansas is the ONLY state that uses a bar-controlled commission** where lawyers elected by other lawyers hold the majority. Supporters call this elitist. Opponents call it a feature, not a bug -- it keeps judges qualified and independent.

---

### Who Is Behind It -- Follow the Money

**Pro-Amendment (YES):**
- **Kansans for Democracy** -- a 501(c)(4) nonprofit that is NOT required to disclose its donors -- booked approximately $802,000 in television ads running from July 7 through August 4. The Sunflower State Journal reports this group has "a conservative connection." This is textbook dark money: nearly $1 million in ads and the public cannot find out who is paying for them.
- **Americans for Prosperity-Kansas** (funded by the Koch network)
- **Kansas Chamber United for Business**
- **Kansas Policy Institute** (conservative think tank)

**Anti-Amendment (NO):**
- The opposition campaign (VoteNoKansas.org and allies) has raised nearly $2 million according to Sunflower State Journal reporting.
- Kansas Bar Association, ACLU, teacher unions, school board associations, and others listed above.

---

### What Happened Elsewhere -- Real Examples

**Wisconsin (2025):** One Supreme Court seat. $144.5 million spent. Elon Musk spent $25 million+ on one candidate. Illinois Governor JB Pritzker and George Soros funded the other side. It became a national proxy war over abortion, Trump, and redistricting -- not about Kansas-style local concerns. The losing candidate's supporters included $4.3 million from Wisconsin Manufacturers and Commerce, $4 million from Fair Courts America (tied to conservative megadonor Richard Uihlein), and $3.2 million from Americans for Prosperity (Koch). This is what Kansas could look like.

**North Carolina (2022):** After partisan elections flipped the court's majority to conservative, the new justices took the extraordinary step of rehearing and reversing several predecessor decisions on redistricting and voting rights -- decisions issued just months earlier. Opponents say this is exactly what would happen in Kansas with abortion rights.

**Pennsylvania:** Supreme Court races have become multi-million-dollar partisan battles with spending increasing every cycle.

**The academic evidence:** Research in the Journal of Public Economics found that judges selected through nonpartisan processes produce higher-quality work than judges chosen in partisan elections. The Brennan Center for Justice documented that campaign spending and special interest influence in state supreme court elections has increased dramatically nationwide.

---
---

## AMENDMENT 2: Should the Kansas Constitution Say "Only Citizens" Can Vote?

**On your ballot: November 3, 2026 (GENERAL election)**

---

### What This Amendment Would Do

Right now, the Kansas Constitution says: "Every citizen of the United States who has attained the age of eighteen years and who resides in the voting area in which he or she seeks to vote shall be deemed a qualified elector."

This amendment would change it to: "No person shall be deemed a qualified elector unless such person: (1) Is a citizen of the United States..."

In plain English: The current Constitution says "every citizen CAN vote." The amendment would change it to "ONLY citizens can vote." Same idea, different framing -- from welcoming language to restricting language.

---

### What This Actually Changes Legally

**Honest answer: Almost nothing. Right now.**

It is ALREADY illegal for non-citizens to vote in Kansas. It has been illegal under both Kansas state law and federal law for as long as Kansas has been a state. This amendment does not create any new rule. It restates what is already the law using stronger, exclusionary language.

The ballot question itself says as much: "This amendment would clarify that only a person who is a citizen of the United States is eligible to vote in this state."

---

### Is Non-Citizen Voting Actually a Problem in Kansas?

**No. The evidence is overwhelming.**

When Kris Kobach was Secretary of State, he championed the Kansas SAFE Act (2011), which required documentary proof of citizenship (birth certificate or passport) to register to vote. The ACLU sued. The case went to federal court. Here is what the court found:

- Over nearly 20 years, Kansas officials confirmed only **39 non-citizens** on the voter rolls (many due to administrative error at the DMV, not intentional fraud)
- Meanwhile, Kobach's law **blocked 31,089 eligible American citizens** from registering to vote
- That is a ratio of roughly 1 non-citizen for every 797 blocked citizens

Federal Judge Julie Robinson's conclusion: **"There is no iceberg; only an icicle, largely created by confusion and administrative error."**

The law was struck down as unconstitutional. The 10th Circuit Court of Appeals upheld the ruling. The U.S. Supreme Court declined to hear the case.

---

### Why Supporters Want This

Their argument is straightforward: Voting should be exclusively for citizens, and the Constitution should say so clearly and forcefully. They point out that similar amendments passed in all 8 states where they appeared on the 2024 ballot, often with 65-80% of the vote. It is a matter of principle, even if non-citizen voting is not currently a problem.

The amendment passed the Kansas House 90-28 and the Senate 37-3. Unlike the judicial amendment, this had meaningful bipartisan support -- 9 House Democrats voted YES.

---

### Why Opponents Fight This

**ACLU of Kansas:** "The language in HCR 5004 could be weaponized to justify a return to restrictive voter registration laws, as it explicitly conditions voter eligibility on U.S. citizenship, despite no evidence of noncitizen voting in Kansas elections."

**Loud Light Civic Action:** "This amendment does nothing to strengthen our Constitution, it appears to do nothing at all legally, yet it will cause confusion, inflame tensions, and distract from important conversations."

The concern is not about what the amendment does today. It is about what it enables tomorrow. Specifically:

1. **Proof-of-citizenship revival:** The exclusionary language could give Kansas constitutional ammunition to re-enact a proof-of-citizenship requirement for voter registration -- the same kind of law that blocked 31,000+ citizens last time.
2. **Additional ID barriers:** Could justify requiring additional documentation beyond what is currently needed to register.
3. **Chilling effect:** The framing could discourage naturalized citizens from voting out of confusion or fear.

---

### What You Need to Know

**FACT 1: Non-citizen voting is already illegal.** This amendment does not make anything new illegal.

**FACT 2: The evidence of non-citizen voting in Kansas is nearly nonexistent.** Federal courts examined 20 years of data and found 39 cases, mostly from administrative error.

**FACT 3: Every state that has voted on this has passed it.** From 2018-2025, voters approved all 15 similar ballot measures nationwide. This will almost certainly pass in Kansas.

**FACT 4: The real debate is about the future.** Supporters see it as locking in a principle. Opponents see it as laying groundwork for restrictive voter registration laws.

**FACT 5: The Kobach connection.** As Attorney General, Kobach still pursues voter fraud cases. In November 2025, Kobach and Secretary of State Schwab announced charges in a voter fraud case. The question is whether this amendment becomes a tool for future proof-of-citizenship legislation.

---

### The 8 States That Passed Similar Measures in 2024

| State | Result |
|-------|--------|
| Idaho | Approved (large margin) |
| Iowa | Approved (76% YES) |
| Kentucky | Approved |
| Missouri | Approved |
| North Carolina | Approved |
| Oklahoma | Approved |
| South Carolina | Approved |
| Wisconsin | Approved (66% YES) |

**Prior states:** Alabama, Colorado, Florida, Louisiana, North Dakota, and Ohio had already passed similar measures before 2024.

---
---

# PART TWO: EVERY RACE ON YOUR BALLOT -- WHAT IT IS ABOUT AND WHY IT MATTERS

---

## Kansas Governor
**Primary: August 4, 2026 | General: November 3, 2026**

### What Does the Governor Actually Do?

The governor is the most powerful person in Kansas state government. They sign or veto every bill the Legislature passes. They appoint the heads of nearly every state department and agency. They submit the state budget. They command the Kansas National Guard. In emergencies, they have near-absolute power over state resources. They serve a 4-year term and can serve a maximum of two consecutive terms.

### Why Does This Open Seat Matter?

Governor Laura Kelly (Democrat) is term-limited and cannot run again. This is the first open governor's race in Kansas since 2018. Open seats are rare and always attract crowded fields because there is no incumbent advantage. The winner will shape Kansas policy on taxes, education funding, Medicaid expansion, abortion access, and how the state responds to federal government changes for the next 4 years.

Kansas has a history of electing moderate governors even though the Legislature is heavily Republican. Kelly won twice as a Democrat. Before her, Republican Sam Brownback's aggressive tax cuts nearly bankrupted the state. The question for 2026 is whether Kansas voters pick a governor who will check the Legislature's power or one who will rubber-stamp it.

**Republican primary (crowded):** Former Governor Jeff Colyer (plastic surgeon, served 2018-19), Secretary of State Scott Schwab, Senate President Ty Masterson, Insurance Commissioner Vicki Schmidt, Charlotte O'Hara (former Johnson County commissioner), Stacy Rogers (Wichita businesswoman), and others.

**Democratic primary:** Senator Ethan Corson (Fairway attorney, emphasizes bipartisan deal-making, helped eliminate the grocery sales tax), Senator Cindy Holscher (Overland Park, farm-raised, led repeal of Brownback tax cuts, founded Bipartisan Women's Caucus).

---

## U.S. Senate: Roger Marshall vs. Challengers
**Primary: August 4, 2026 | General: November 3, 2026**

### What Does Marshall Actually Do for Kansas?

Senator Roger Marshall is a physician from Great Bend who has represented Kansas in the U.S. Senate since 2021 (before that, he was the KS-01 congressman). In the Senate, he sits on committees dealing with agriculture, health, and the budget. He has focused on rural hospital funding, farm policy, and -- most recently -- is a founding member of the Senate DOGE Caucus working with Elon Musk's Department of Government Efficiency to cut federal spending. He voted with Trump's positions 98% of the time. He voted against certifying the 2020 presidential election results.

He worked to move USAID's Food for Peace program under the Department of Agriculture -- directly relevant to Kansas farmers. He has introduced legislation to codify DOGE spending cuts.

### Why Do 8 Democrats Think They Can Beat Him?

Kansas has not elected a Democrat to the U.S. Senate since 1932. That is not a typo. Ninety-four years. So why are 8 Democrats running?

Two reasons: First, the 2022 abortion vote proved that Kansas voters will cross party lines on the right issue. If DOGE cuts hit Kansas hard -- closing rural VA clinics, cutting farm subsidies, eliminating Social Security Administration offices in small towns -- there could be an opening. Second, Marshall's close alignment with Trump and Musk is a bet that could pay off or backfire depending on how Kansans feel about federal government cuts by November.

**Notable Democratic challengers:**
- **Jason Hart** -- former federal prosecutor who served under both Democratic and Republican officials
- **Christy Davis** -- former Kansas director for USDA rural development under Biden
- **Anne Parelkar** -- immigration attorney

**The honest assessment:** This seat is rated Solid Republican. An upset would be historic. But 2022 showed that "impossible" is a word Kansas voters do not always respect.

---

## U.S. House KS-01 (Big First): Tracey Mann
**Primary: August 4, 2026 | General: November 3, 2026**

### Why Is This Seat So Safe for Republicans?

Kansas's 1st Congressional District covers the entire western two-thirds of the state -- from the Nebraska border to the Oklahoma border, from the Colorado line almost to Topeka. It is the second-largest congressional district east of the Mississippi. It is overwhelmingly rural, agricultural, and Republican. Mann won reelection in 2024 with 69% of the vote. No Democrat has won this seat since the 1990s.

### What Does Mann Actually Do in Congress?

Mann serves on the House Agriculture Committee and chairs the Subcommittee on Livestock, Dairy, and Poultry. For western Kansas, this is the most important committee assignment possible. He has spent his time fighting for Farm Bill provisions: strengthening crop insurance, raising reference prices for ARC and PLC programs (which protect farmers when commodity prices drop), increasing funding for agricultural export programs (MAP and FMD), and pushing to set the estate tax exemption at $30 million per couple so family farms can pass to the next generation without being sold to pay taxes. He was named a "Friend of Farm Bureau" by the American Farm Bureau Federation.

In plain English: Mann's job is keeping western Kansas agriculture funded and protected at the federal level.

**Democratic challengers:**
- **Colin McRoberts** -- University of Kansas business school professor, inspired to run after attending Marshall's contentious town hall in Oakley
- **Lauren Reinhold** -- former Social Security Administration employee who was laid off in the DOGE federal workforce reductions

**The honest assessment:** This is a long-shot race for Democrats. But the DOGE layoffs of federal employees in rural Kansas could create unusual dynamics.

---

## Kansas Attorney General: Kobach vs. Mann (Rematch)
**Primary: August 4, 2026 | General: November 3, 2026**

### What Does the Attorney General Actually Do?

The AG is Kansas's top law enforcement officer. They prosecute major crimes that cross county lines, defend the state in lawsuits, issue legal opinions that guide state agencies, enforce consumer protection laws, go after fraud, and represent Kansas in cases at the U.S. Supreme Court. The AG's office shapes how aggressively Kansas enforces everything from environmental laws to election rules.

### Why Was the 2022 Race So Close?

Kris Kobach (Republican) beat Chris Mann (Democrat) by only 15,000 votes out of 1 million cast -- a 1.6% margin, the closest statewide race that year. Kobach is one of the most polarizing figures in Kansas politics. He is a lightning rod on immigration, voting laws, and abortion. Some voters see him as a principled conservative warrior; others see him as someone who picks high-profile fights and loses in court.

This is a direct rematch. Mann is a Lawrence attorney and former police officer turned prosecutor. He focuses on "basics of law enforcement" -- DUI prevention, victims' rights, public safety. His pitch: the AG's office should protect Kansans, not chase national headlines.

Kobach's campaign says Kansas crime has dropped to a 20-year low under his leadership. Mann says the AG should focus on the basics and "defend the rule of law."

**Why this matters:** The AG interprets and enforces Kansas laws on abortion, voting, immigration, and government transparency. Whoever holds this office shapes which laws get enforced aggressively and which ones gather dust.

---

## Kansas Secretary of State
**Primary: August 4, 2026 | General: November 3, 2026**

### Why Is This the Most Consequential Race Nobody Is Watching?

The Secretary of State runs Kansas elections. They decide how voter registration works, what IDs are required, how ballots are counted, whether mail-in voting is easy or hard, and how election complaints are handled. In a time when election integrity is a national flashpoint, this office has enormous power over how -- and whether -- Kansans vote.

Incumbent Scott Schwab (Republican) is leaving to run for governor.

### What Would Pat Proctor Change?

Pat Proctor is a Republican state representative from Leavenworth who chairs the House Elections Committee. He is a retired Army officer with a doctorate in history. Here is what matters about his record:

Proctor has been one of the Legislature's strongest advocates for election law changes inspired by President Trump's claims about the 2020 election. As Elections Committee chair, he has championed bills to:
- **Repeal the 3-day grace period** for mailed ballots to arrive after Election Day
- **Ban ranked-choice voting** in Kansas
- **Ban foreign nationals** from contributing to constitutional amendment campaigns
- **Limit the Kansas Governmental Ethics Commission's** power to investigate campaign finance violations

If elected Secretary of State, he would go from writing the election rules to enforcing them.

**Other candidates:**
- **Ken Rahjes** (Republican) -- state representative from the 110th district
- **Jennifer Day** (Democrat) -- former state representative
- **Sam Lane** (Democrat)

**Why this matters for Hays:** The Secretary of State decides how easy or hard it is for every person in Ellis County to register, vote by mail, and have their vote counted. This office touches every single election on your ballot.

---

## Kansas Insurance Commissioner
**Primary: August 4, 2026 | General: November 3, 2026**

### Why Does This Matter for Rural Kansas Healthcare Costs?

The Insurance Commissioner regulates every insurance company doing business in Kansas -- health insurance, car insurance, homeowners insurance, crop insurance, all of it. They review rate increases, make sure companies can actually pay claims, handle consumer complaints, and license insurance agents. In rural Kansas, where hospital closures and limited healthcare options are a growing crisis, the Insurance Commissioner's decisions on what health plans are available and what they can charge directly affect your family's bottom line.

### The Candidates

**Dan Hawkins (Republican):** Current Kansas House Speaker, 30 years in the insurance business, runs his own insurance agency. His campaign website leads with "PRO-LIFE. PRO-GUN. PRO-TRUMP." As House Speaker, he proposed cutting $200 million from the state budget, including targeting Medicaid for cuts. He receives commissions from six insurance companies. His campaign treasurer is Mary Jean Eisenhower (granddaughter of President Eisenhower).

**Dinah Sykes (Democrat):** Kansas Senate Minority Leader from Lenexa. She has pledged to accept zero campaign contributions from the insurance industry. Her platform focuses on lowering healthcare costs, consumer protection, and holding insurance companies accountable. She is a longtime advocate for Medicaid expansion. She has been endorsed by former Insurance Commissioner and Governor Kathleen Sebelius (Democrat) and former Insurance Commissioner Sandy Praeger (Republican).

**Why this matters for Hays:** When your health insurance premium goes up, when a hospital closes, when an insurance company denies a claim -- the Insurance Commissioner is the person who is supposed to be in your corner. The question is whether you want that person to come from the insurance industry or from outside it.

---

## Kansas House District 111: Barb Wasinger (Hays)
**Primary: August 4, 2026 | General: November 3, 2026**

### What Has Barb Wasinger Actually Done for Hays?

Barb Wasinger (Republican) has represented District 111 since 2019. Before the Legislature, she served 8 years as a Hays City Commissioner (including two stints as Mayor) and 6 years as an Ellis County Commissioner -- the first woman to hold that county position.

In the Legislature, she serves on the **Appropriations Committee** (controls the state budget), **Commerce, Labor and Economic Development**, **Financial Institutions and Rural Development**, and chairs the **Committee on General Government Budget** and the **Joint Committee on Administrative Rules and Regulations**.

Her most notable concrete accomplishment for Hays: she coordinated a visit with state and federal officials to address Ellis County infrastructure needs, which resulted in **$1 million in state funding** and **$6.5 million from a federal BUILD grant**.

She has won three consecutive elections (2020, 2022, 2024), each time defeating a challenger.

**What to watch:** As of March 31, 2026, no challenger has been announced for the August primary or November general. The filing deadline is June 1. Wasinger is running for reelection.

---

## State Board of Education District 5
**Filing deadline: June 1, 2026 | Primary: August 4, 2026 | General: November 3, 2026**

### What Does the State Board of Education Actually Control?

The Kansas State Board of Education is one of the most powerful and least understood bodies in state government. It has 10 elected members (one from each district) and has constitutional authority over:

- **Curriculum standards** -- what Kansas kids learn in math, science, reading, writing, and social studies (yes, including what gets taught about evolution, history, and sex education)
- **School accreditation** -- whether schools meet state standards
- **Teacher licensing** -- who is qualified to teach in Kansas
- **Special education** -- programs for disabled, homebound, and exceptional students
- **Career and technical education** -- approval of all vocational programs
- **School nutrition** -- food service and child care food programs
- **School district organization** -- how districts are structured
- **Budget requests** -- the Board requested over $105 million in enhancements for FY2026

District 5 covers western Kansas, including Hays. The current member is **Cathy Hopkins** (Republican), elected in 2022. Her seat is up in 2026.

**Why this matters:** The Board of Education has been a battleground over science standards (evolution vs. intelligent design), sex education, school library books, and transgender student policies. In recent years, conservative and moderate factions have fought for control. The 2026 elections could shift the balance of power on the board.

**As of March 31, 2026, no candidates have filed for District 5.** The filing deadline is June 1. Watch this space -- candidates often file at the last minute.

---
---

# QUICK REFERENCE: BOTH AMENDMENTS SIDE BY SIDE

| | Supreme Court Amendment (Aug 4) | Citizenship Voting Amendment (Nov 3) |
|---|---|---|
| **In one sentence** | Changes how KS Supreme Court justices get their jobs -- from commission-appointed to elected | Changes "every citizen can vote" to "only citizens can vote" in the state constitution |
| **Real-world impact** | Massive -- restructures the judiciary | Minimal -- restates existing law |
| **Controversy** | Extremely high | Low |
| **Partisan divide** | 93% Republican support, near-zero Democratic support | Bipartisan (9 Democrats voted YES) |
| **Dark money** | Yes ($802K+ from undisclosed donors pro-YES) | None documented |
| **Likely outcome** | Uncertain -- could go either way | Almost certain to pass |
| **When you vote** | August 4 PRIMARY (low turnout favors supporters) | November 3 general (higher turnout) |

---

# HOW TO VOTE

**Registration deadline:** Check with the Ellis County Clerk's office or visit https://www.kdor.ks.gov/Apps/VoterReg/

**August 4 primary:** You MUST be registered with a party (Republican or Democrat) to vote in that party's primary races. However, ALL registered voters -- including unaffiliated voters -- can vote on the constitutional amendment.

**November 3 general:** All registered voters can vote on all races and the citizenship amendment.

**Where to vote in Hays:** Contact the Ellis County Clerk at (785) 628-9410 or check https://myvoteinfo.voteks.org/
