## 1. FULL BIOGRAPHY

### Personal Information
- **Full Name:** Roger Wayne Marshall
- **Born:** August 9, 1960
- **Birthplace:** El Dorado, Butler County, Kansas
- **Age (as of investigation):** 65
- **Party:** Republican
- **Religion:** Nondenominational Christian (First Christian Church, Disciples of Christ, Great Bend)
- **Residence (Official):** A 1,120 sq ft cabin on a dirt road in western Kansas (near Great Bend area), on a 300+ acre ranch/property owned by a family-controlled corporation

### Family
- **Wife:** Laina Marshall -- married 40+ years
- **Children (4):** Lauren, Victor, Matt, Cal
- **Grandchildren:** 4

### Education
| Year | Institution | Degree/Notes |
|------|-----------|--------------|
| ~1978-1980 | Butler Community College (El Dorado, KS) | Associate's Degree (1980) |
| 1980-1982 | Kansas State University | B.S. in Biochemistry (1982); member of Beta Theta Pi fraternity |
| 1983-1987 | University of Kansas School of Medicine | Doctor of Medicine (M.D.), 1987 |
| ~1987-1991 | Bayfront Medical Center, St. Petersburg, FL | OB/GYN Residency |

### Military Service
- **Branch:** United States Army Reserve
- **Years:** 1984-1991 (7 years)
- **Rank Achieved:** Captain (O-3)

### Background Summary
Marshall is a 5th-generation Kansas farm kid from Butler County. He was the first in his family to attend college. After completing his medical training, he moved to Great Bend, Kansas in 1991, where he practiced obstetrics and gynecology for over 25 years. He delivered more than **5,000 babies** during his career. He entered politics in 2016 by defeating incumbent Rep. Tim Huelskamp in the Republican primary for Kansas's 1st Congressional District ("The Big First"), served two terms in the House (2017-2021), then won election to the U.S. Senate in 2020.

---

## 2. FAITH & CHURCH INVOLVEMENT

### Church Membership
- **Church:** First Christian Church, Great Bend, Kansas (Disciples of Christ denomination)
- **Duration:** 25+ years of active involvement

### Leadership Roles at First Christian Church
- **Elder** -- Served for years in this governing/spiritual leadership role
- **Deacon** -- Service role in the congregation
- **Board Chairman** -- Led the church's governing board
- **Sunday School Teacher** -- He and wife Laina taught Sunday school together for **over 25 years**

### Faith Statements (Verbatim)
- "I don't wear my faith on my shirt sleeve, but in my heart."
- "I have tried to read the Bible every day since I was 10 years of age, so a lot of the wisdom I've been given comes from reading the Bible."
- "Every decision I make, I always have to be true to my faith."
- "My faith is a pillar of my life, and the life of my family, and it is our strength."
- "So I truly, truly hope this nation can remember our Judeo-Christian values that we were founded on, that we could always be, indeed, 'One nation under God.'"

### Conversion Story
Marshall states he was raised in a Christian home and "fully accepted Jesus Christ as his Lord and Savior at a **Fellowship of Christian Athletes** event in high school." He has committed to daily Bible readings since age 10.

### Faith in Legislative Work
- Has referenced his Christian faith and Judeo-Christian values in Senate floor speeches
- His pro-life stance is directly connected to his faith and his experience delivering 5,000+ babies
- His first bill as a U.S. Senator was pro-life legislation protecting the unborn
- Supported the "Value Them Both" Kansas constitutional amendment on abortion in 2022
- After the amendment's defeat, he said: "While I don't have an answer, I do know that God works all things for good for those who trust him."

### Assessment
Marshall's faith appears deeply personal and longstanding -- not performative. 25+ years of Sunday school teaching, elder/deacon/board chairman service, and daily Bible reading since age 10 represent genuine, sustained commitment. His pro-life positions are rooted in both his faith and his medical career delivering thousands of babies.

### "A Doctor's Note" Newsletter
Marshall publishes a weekly email newsletter called **"A Doctor's Note"** through his Senate office website (marshall.senate.gov). Content includes:
- Legislative updates and priorities
- Events across Kansas
- Healthcare policy commentary
- Political commentary

**Criticism:** The Kansas City Star editorial board criticized the newsletter as being used primarily to attack Democrats (Biden/Harris) rather than to help Kansans, calling it partisan rather than informative.

### Social Media Tone & Content
- **Frequent topics:** Healthcare reform, agriculture/Farm Bill, border security, pro-life issues, Second Amendment, fiscal conservatism, faith references
- **Tone:** Combative on partisan issues, folksy/relatable on Kansas-specific topics, uses "Doc" persona frequently
- **Notable incident:** Facebook removed a COVID-19 post by Marshall in September 2020 for misinformation

## 4. COMPLETE VOTING RECORD

### January 6 Electoral Certification (January 6-7, 2021)

**VOTED TO OBJECT to certification in BOTH Arizona AND Pennsylvania.**

- **Arizona objection:** Voted YES to sustain objection. Senate rejected 6-93.
- **Pennsylvania objection:** Voted YES to sustain objection. Senate rejected 7-92.
- Marshall was one of only **8 Republican senators** to vote against certification in both states.
- On January 2, 2021, he joined 10 other GOP senators/senators-elect announcing plans to block certification.
- He called it "a decision from my heart" and said he was "concerned then and I still am today that six states broke their own laws or their own constitution."
- **Later asked about it:** Told CNN he was "so ready to move on" and defended it as "a decision based upon the facts that I knew at that point in time."
- **Voted AGAINST** creating an independent commission to investigate the January 6 Capitol attack (May 28, 2021).

### Abortion / Life Issues
- **Pro-life scorecard: 100%** -- Voted pro-life on every single recorded vote (20/20 as House member, continued in Senate)
- **National Pro-Life Scorecard (SBA Pro-Life America):** Perfect score
- **Planned Parenthood Action Fund:** 0% rating
- Co-sponsored and voted for the **Born-Alive Abortion Survivors Protection Act**
- Co-sponsored and voted for the **Pain-Capable Unborn Child Protection Act** (protecting unborn at 20 weeks)
- Co-sponsored the **Protecting Pain-Capable Unborn Children from Late-Term Abortions Act** (Fall 2022)
- His **first bill as a U.S. Senator** was pro-life legislation
- Voted multiple times against using tax dollars for abortion
- Opposes taxpayer funding of abortion providers
- Supported Kansas "Value Them Both" amendment (defeated by voters August 2022)
- Has said he **opposes abortion including in cases of rape and incest**
- Called for **overturning Roe v. Wade** in 2020 (achieved via Dobbs in 2022)

### Gun / Second Amendment Votes
- **Voted AGAINST** the Bipartisan Safer Communities Act (June 2022) -- the gun reform bill that passed after Uvalde
- Called red flag laws provisions a "gun-grabbing scheme" that "violate the Second Amendment" and are "begging to be abused"
- Both Kansas senators (Marshall and Moran) voted against the bipartisan gun safety bill
- **Introduced pro-2A legislation:**
  - Home Defense and Competitive Shooting (HDCS) Act -- end prohibition-era regulations on short-barreled rifles
  - Fire Arms Safety Act -- tax credit for firearms safety courses or purchasing gun safes
  - Firearms Interstate Commerce Reform Act (FICRA) -- modernize interstate firearms transactions
  - ATF Transparency Act -- speed up application processes for gun owners
  - Modern Firearms Safety Act (with Sen. Risch) -- prohibit states from enforcing handgun rosters
  - SHORT Act (with Sen. Rick Scott) -- related to short-barreled rifle regulations

### Immigration / Border Security
- **Hardline border hawk** -- consistently votes for stricter border enforcement
- Supported finishing the border wall, ending catch-and-release
- Fought to maintain **Title 42** -- called it "the only tool in the toolkit"
- Traveled to Brownsville, Texas with Sens. Cruz, Budd, Hoeven before Title 42 expired
- Supported **H.R. 2, the Secure the Border Act**
- Called Biden's border policy an "open borders agenda" that "exposed states to invasion"
- Called for more border patrol agents and ending "abuse of asylum"

### Agriculture / Farm Bill
- Serves on Senate Agriculture Committee -- a pillar of his identity
- Supports Farm Bill framework that "puts Farm back in the Farm Bill"
- Pushed for 15% average increase in statutory reference prices for all commodities
- Fought against using Conservation Title to phase out livestock production
- Introduced "Product of the USA" label legislation for beef (born, raised, processed in US)
- Reintroduced bill to support livestock producers
- Opposes federal control over cattle markets
- Introduced bill to protect family farms from "burdensome government overreach"
- Prioritized trade and food aid in Farm Bill hearings
- **Key issue for Kansas:** State is top-3 in cattle, cattle on feed, and cattle slaughter

### Healthcare
- Has said: "I came to Congress to fix the cost of health care"
- Called Obamacare a "miserable failure" -- said premiums doubled and average family deductible is $7,000-$9,000
- Supported repealing/replacing ACA as House member (voted YES on American Health Care Act, 2017)
- **Voted AGAINST** extending ACA subsidies -- expects them to expire, acknowledges "some people's premiums are going to go up"
- Proposed alternative: redirect ACA subsidies from insurance companies into Health Savings Accounts for patients
- Supports health ministry plans and association healthcare plans as alternatives
- Champions "Make America Healthy Again" (MAHA) initiative -- shift from "sick care" to "health care" model, address chronic diseases
- Promised healthcare vote before end of 2025

### Ukraine / Foreign Aid
- **Early on (2022):** Strongly supported Russia sanctions, called for "maximum pressure" on Putin
- Endorsed the **NYET Act** (Never Yielding Europe's Territory) to stop Nord Stream 2 and sanction Russian banks
- Said Ukraine "doesn't need words, they need action" in February 2022
- **BUT voted AGAINST the $95 billion foreign aid package** (Ukraine + Israel aid) in 2024
- Was one of only **15 Republican senators** to vote against $60 billion for Ukraine
- Argued border security should be prioritized before foreign aid -- called Ukraine funding "another blank check"
- This split him from Kansas colleague Sen. Jerry Moran, who voted FOR the aid

### Budget / Debt Ceiling / Spending
- **Fiscal hawk position** -- votes against spending bills he considers excessive
- Voted against continuing resolutions that don't include border security funding
- Attempted to trigger automatic spending cuts by extending a CR through September
- Was among only **9 Republicans** to vote against a funding bill in one instance
- Said the US is "$34 trillion in debt, paying a trillion dollars on interest alone"
- Calls for "meaningful cuts to out-of-control spending to save future generations"
- Opposed stopgap bills without spending reform

### Bipartisan Votes
- **Ensuring Innovation Act** -- bipartisan bill with Sens. Cassidy (R) and Smith (D), signed into law
- Voted for bipartisan resolution objecting to UN Security Council Resolution 2334 (on Israel)
- Proposed bipartisan ACA credit extension (1 year) before transitioning to HSA-style accounts
- Generally few bipartisan crossover votes -- **voted with Trump positions 98% of the time**

### Overall Voting Metrics
- **Missed votes:** 72 of 2,362 roll call votes (3.0%) -- near median for current senators
- **Heritage Action Lifetime Score:** 82%
  - 117th Congress (2021-2022): 94%
  - 118th Congress (2023-2024): 89%
- **Trump alignment:** 98%

## 5. THE FAUCI "MORON" INCIDENT & OTHER CONFRONTATIONS

### The Fauci Hot Mic Incident (January 11, 2022)

**What happened:** During a Senate HELP Committee hearing on COVID, Marshall questioned Dr. Anthony Fauci about his salary ($434,000/year in 2020) and financial disclosures, and whether Fauci would submit a financial disclosure including investments to Congress and the public. Fauci responded that his financial records were already publicly available.

**The hot mic moment:** When Marshall was cut off and another senator began questioning, Fauci's microphone caught him saying **"What a moron"** and **"Jesus Christ"** in exasperation.

**Video:** Yes -- the clip went viral, viewed nearly 3 million times.

**Marshall's response:** Tweeted: "Calling me a moron during a Senate hearing may have alleviated the stress of the least trusted bureaucrat in America, but it didn't take away from the facts. We need the truth Dr. Fauci!"

**Legislative response:** Marshall introduced the **FAUCI Act** (Financial Accountability for Uniquely Compensated Individuals) to require public posting of financial disclosures for high-ranking government officials on the Office of Government Ethics website.

**Follow-up:** Marshall obtained and published Fauci's previously unpublished financial disclosures from NIH, claimed Fauci had been misleading about their public availability. (Note: Fact-checkers found Fauci's disclosures were technically publicly available via FOIA request, but were not posted online.)

### The Oakley Town Hall Walkout (March 1, 2025)

**What happened:** Marshall held a town hall at a hospital in Oakley, Kansas (Logan County -- 85% Trump in 2024). Expected 20-30 people; the crowd was so large they had to move to a larger space.

**The confrontation:** Constituents immediately began peppering Marshall with angry questions about DOGE cuts, the Ukraine conflict, hollowing of federal agencies, and rural healthcare. The crowd booed and shouted.

**The exit:** Marshall left approximately 20 minutes early, reportedly calling the audience "rude" and saying "God bless America" as he bolted for the door. He was **called a "coward"** as he departed. He stated he had "two more commitments today."

**Marshall's response:** His chief of staff claimed "Democrat operatives that couldn't place Oakley, Kansas on a map before today sabotaged a local town hall." Marshall later called attendees "paid Democratic operatives."

**Public pushback:** Kansas residents who attended pushed back hard, saying they were real constituents concerned about agriculture funding cuts and federal worker layoffs. One Kansas Reflector columnist wrote: "If he proves it, I'll eat a copy of Project 2025."

### CNN Confrontations (2025-2026)
- **Iran nuclear comments:** CNN's Kaitlan Collins confronted Marshall about his claim that Iran wouldn't pose a nuclear threat for years. Marshall admitted on air: **"Look, I was wrong."**
- **Trump AI video:** Collins asked Marshall about a controversial AI video Trump posted; Marshall deflected.

## 7. BILLS SPONSORED & LEGISLATIVE ACHIEVEMENTS

### Bills Signed Into Law

#### The Ensuring Innovation Act (Signed April 23, 2021)
- **Co-sponsors:** Sens. Bill Cassidy (R-LA) and Tina Smith (D-MN)
- **What it does:** Codifies FDA's "active moiety" approach to granting New Chemical Entity (NCE) exclusivity, closing loopholes that allowed drug companies to claim false innovations to extend exclusivity and delay cheaper generics
- **Significance:** Marshall's first bill signed into law; he was the only freshman Senate Republican to achieve this at that time
- **Passed Senate:** March 10, 2021, by unanimous consent

### Major Bills Introduced (Not Yet Signed Into Law)

#### Healthcare & COVID
- **FAUCI Act** -- Require public posting of financial disclosures for top government officials
- **Viral Gain of Function Research Moratorium Act** -- Moratorium on federal grants for gain-of-function research
- **Chinese Communist Party Accountability Act** -- Sanctions on Chinese health officials tied to COVID outbreak
- **National BioSecurity Improvement Act** -- Protect national security from dangerous pathogen research
- **Biologics Market Transparency Act (S.4302)** -- Give physicians drug shortage information
- **REAL Health Providers Act** -- Healthcare transparency
- **Surprise Medical Bills legislation** (with Sen. Bennet) -- Strengthen protections against surprise billing
- **Whole Milk for Healthy Kids Act of 2025** -- Allow whole milk in school lunches
- **21st Century WIC Act of 2026** -- Modernize WIC program
- **Healthy Start Reauthorization Act of 2026**

#### Agriculture
- **"Product of the USA" label legislation** -- Require beef to be born, raised, and processed in US for label
- **Livestock producer support bill** (reintroduced)
- **Family farm protection bill** -- Against "burdensome government overreach"
- Multiple Farm Bill provisions as Agriculture Committee member

#### Second Amendment
- **Home Defense and Competitive Shooting (HDCS) Act**
- **Fire Arms Safety Act** -- Tax credits for safety courses
- **ATF Transparency Act**
- **Modern Firearms Safety Act** (with Sen. Risch) -- Ban handgun rosters
- **SHORT Act** (with Sen. Rick Scott)
- **Firearms Interstate Commerce Reform Act (FICRA)** (with Sen. Cramer)

#### Healthcare Reform (2025-2026)
- Proposed ACA alternative redirecting subsidies to HSAs
- "Make America Healthy Again" initiative framework
- Promised comprehensive healthcare bill by end of 2025

## 8. THE 2026 CHALLENGERS

### Republican Primary Challenger

#### Chase LaPorte
- **From:** Lenexa, Kansas
- **Born:** Carthage, Missouri
- **Military:** U.S. Army, 2005-2013
- **Education:** Associate's degree, Cowley County Community College (2017)
- **Career:** Business administrator
- **Website:** Not identified in research
- **Assessment:** Long-shot challenger with minimal profile. Marshall has Trump's endorsement and massive financial advantage. LaPorte lacks significant campaign infrastructure.

### Democratic Primary Candidates (8 Total)

#### 1. Jason Hart -- LEADING CONTENDER
- **Website:** hartforsenate.com
- **Background:** Former Assistant U.S. Attorney, District of Kansas, specializing in child exploitation and cybercrime prosecution. 21+ years serving Kansans.
- **Notable:** Quit his federal prosecutor job and switched party affiliation to run (entered race March 2026)
- **From:** Kansas
- **Platform:** Reduce costs for working families, support small businesses, corporate tax accountability, Congressional oversight against executive overreach, regulate Big Tech, immigration and trade reform
- **Strength:** "Law and order" credibility as a federal prosecutor; appeal to moderates and disaffected Republicans

- **Website:** patrickforkansas.com
- **Background:** Kansas State Senator, 19th District (since 2025). Former U.S. Navy Intelligence Officer -- served on USS RONALD REAGAN, deployed as Fleet Intelligence Watch Officer and targeting analyst with Joint Special Operations Task Force Arabian Peninsula. Stationed at Office of Naval Intelligence in D.C. during January 6 attack.
- **From:** Lawrence area
- **Won:** State Senate seat defeating Tyler Wible in November 2024 general
- **Strength:** Military credentials, elected office experience, witnessed January 6 firsthand

#### 3. Christy Cauble Davis
- **Website:** christydavisforkansas.com
- **Background:** Former Kansas Director for USDA Rural Development under President Biden. Oversaw major investments in businesses, infrastructure, housing, and healthcare across Kansas. Led nationwide effort to cut federal red tape.
- **From:** Cottonwood Falls, Kansas
- **Education:** Kansas State University (B.A., 1997), Wichita State University (graduate degree, 1999), Sedgwick High School
- **Platform:** Restore funding for healthcare and education, immigration reform, address rural economic concerns from tariffs
- **Strength:** Deep rural Kansas roots, USDA/agriculture credibility

#### 4. Sandy Spidel Neumann
- **Website:** sandyforkansas.com
- **Background:** Retired after 22+ years as executive at Ameriprise Financial Services. 40-year business career.
- **From:** Mission, Kansas (Johnson County)
- **Education:** B.A. Economics, University of Chicago; MBA, Northwestern University
- **Platform:** Opposes Marshall-endorsed tariffs harmful to farmers, opposes Medicaid cuts that threaten rural hospitals, supports reinstating Medicaid funding, extending ACA subsidies, keeping government out of women's healthcare, fighting pharma on drug prices
- **Strength:** Business/financial credibility, education pedigree

#### 5. Erik Murray
- **Website:** erikforkansas.com
- **Background:** Kansas City, Kansas entrepreneur and commercial real estate developer. Leading the $1 billion "Midtown Station" redevelopment of the former Indian Springs Mall site in KCK -- 1,500+ new homes, retail, 30-acre solar microgrid.
- **From:** Kansas City, Kansas
- **Platform:** Lower costs for starting/running small businesses, entrepreneurship focus
- **VULNERABILITY:** Spoke on a podcast about being inspired by former Black Panther leader Elaine Brown during his years in Oakland, CA. The Washington Free Beacon reported he named a "Black Panther 'Soldier' Working to Destroy the American 'Empire'" as his political inspiration. This will be opposition research ammunition.

#### 6. Anne Parelkar
- **Website:** anneforkansas.com
- **Background:** Immigration attorney licensed in Kansas, Arkansas, and Missouri. First-time candidate.
- **From:** Overland Park, Kansas
- **Education:** Lyon College, Batesville, AR (2005); University of Arkansas at Little Rock (J.D., 2011)
- **Raised:** Presbyterian, Pine Bluff, Arkansas
- **Platform:** Consolidated children's healthcare program (replace Medicaid/CHIP patchwork), stronger antitrust and consumer protection laws, immigration reform
- **Strength:** Immigration policy expertise; unique voice in field

- **Website:** ActBlue donation page (secure.actblue.com/donate/michael-soetaert)

- **Background:** Art gallery owner, former Wellington city council member. **Perennial candidate** -- previously ran for KS-01 House (2020), Kansas State Senate District 32 (2024, lost primary)

## 9. KS-01 CONGRESSIONAL RECORD (2017-2021)

### How He Got to Congress
- In 2016, Marshall -- a political newcomer -- challenged 3-term incumbent Rep. Tim Huelskamp in the Republican primary for Kansas's 1st Congressional District
- **Key issue:** Huelskamp had lost his seat on the House Agriculture Committee, the first time in a century no Kansan was on that panel. This enraged Kansas agricultural groups who backed Marshall.
- **Primary result:** Marshall 56% vs Huelskamp 44% (August 2, 2016)
- **General election 2016:** Marshall 65.9% -- no Democrat filed
- **Re-election 2018:** Marshall won handily

### Key Actions as House Member
- Joined the **GOP Doctors Caucus** -- put himself at center of ACA repeal effort
- **Voted YES** on the American Health Care Act of 2017 (ACA repeal attempt)
- Served on **House Agriculture Committee** -- key for representing the Big First
- **October 23, 2019: SCIF Storming** -- Marshall was part of the group of 15-30 House Republicans led by Rep. Matt Gaetz who stormed a confidential House Intelligence Committee hearing during the first Trump impeachment inquiry
  - Marshall called the impeachment inquiry a "sham"
  - Said "the people of Kansas are sick and tired of these impeachment hearings"
  - Said of Adam Schiff: "He left, he just got up and left. He doesn't have the guts to tell us why we can't come in the room"
  - The incident involved bringing cell phones into a SCIF (Sensitive Compartmented Information Facility), a national security concern
- Focused on healthcare and agriculture legislation
- Voted in line with Trump positions at an extremely high rate

## 11. COVID-19 POSITIONS

### Vaccine Stance
- **Supports the vaccine as effective** -- led a public service campaign with Republican doctors to boost COVID-19 vaccine participation
- Stated: "I do think the vaccines work"
- **BUT strongly opposes all vaccine mandates** -- calls it a personal choice between individuals and their doctors
- Led opposition to Biden's CMS vaccine mandate for healthcare workers
- Introduced resolution of disapproval under Congressional Review Act to halt the mandate
- Wrote op-ed: "Biden's COVID vaccine mandate treats our heroes like felons"
- Celebrated SCOTUS decision blocking OSHA vaccine mandate

### Mask Stance
- **Opposes mask mandates**
- Stated: "I'm not convinced the masks really work at all"
- Said: "I just think that we're kidding ourselves if kids wearing masks helps. It probably even makes it worse."
- Routinely campaigned among crowds in 2020 without wearing a mask

### Ivermectin
- **Personally recommended ivermectin** to a loved one with COVID symptoms
- Reported that within an hour of taking it, their asthma symptoms settled down, with recovery after a second dose
- Called for "Warp Speed for COVID therapeutics"
- His advocacy of ivermectin for COVID drew criticism as it lacked evidence of effectiveness

### Gain-of-Function Research
- Introduced the **Viral Gain of Function Research Moratorium Act**
- Introduced the **Chinese Communist Party Accountability Act** targeting Chinese health officials
- Introduced the **National BioSecurity Improvement Act**

### Facebook Removal
- Facebook removed a COVID-19 post by Marshall in September 2020 for violating misinformation policies

### RFK Jr. Connection
- Reporting in 2025-2026 noted Marshall "echoes RFK Jr.'s vaccine nonsense," drawing concern about aligning with anti-vaccine messaging

### Summary Assessment
Marshall occupies a position common among Republican physician-politicians: he personally supports vaccines but aggressively fights mandates, opposes masks, promoted unproven treatments, and pushed conspiracy-adjacent theories about COVID origins. His credibility as a doctor makes his anti-mandate/anti-mask positions more influential.

## 19. VULNERABILITIES & CONTROVERSIES SUMMARY

### For a General Election Opponent
1. **January 6 Electoral Objection** -- Voted to overturn election results in two states, one of only 8 Republican senators to do so
2. **Oakley Town Hall Walkout** -- Fled his own constituents, called them "paid Democratic operatives" when they were rural Kansans in Trump country
3. **Florida Property / Residency Questions** -- $1.2M Sarasota house vs. tiny Kansas cabin; $4,900+ in taxpayer-funded flights to Sarasota; raises "does he even live in Kansas?" questions
4. **COVID Positions** -- Anti-mask, ivermectin promotion, Facebook post removed for misinformation, despite being a physician
5. **ACA Subsidies Expiration** -- Voted to let subsidies expire, acknowledging premiums will go up for some
6. **Ukraine Aid Vote** -- Voted against supporting Ukraine after initially supporting sanctions on Russia
7. **SCIF Storming** -- Participated in the 2019 breach of a secure facility during impeachment hearings
8. **98% Trump Alignment** -- In a state that voted for Trump but also rejected the abortion amendment, lockstep alignment could alienate suburban moderates
9. **Gun Vote** -- Voted against bipartisan gun safety bill after Uvalde school shooting
10. **"What a moron" incident** -- While it plays well with his base, it highlights combative approach over substance

### For a Primary Opponent
- Very few vulnerabilities from the right; Heritage Action 89-94%, pro-life 100%, NRA-aligned, Trump-endorsed
- Possible angles: the Florida property (not a "real Kansan"), Heritage score drop in 115th Congress, initial lower Heritage rating

### For Faith-Based Voter Guide Assessment
**Strengths from a Judeo-Christian values perspective:**
- 25+ years of genuine church leadership (elder, deacon, board chair, Sunday school teacher)
- Daily Bible reader since age 10
- Fellowship of Christian Athletes conversion
- 100% pro-life voting record backed by personal experience delivering 5,000+ babies
- References faith consistently in public statements
- Strong traditional family (40+ year marriage, 4 children, 4 grandchildren)

**Concerns from a Judeo-Christian values perspective:**
- Electoral objection and SCIF storming raise integrity/rule-of-law questions
- Oakley walkout and "paid operatives" claim raise honesty/accountability concerns
- Florida property/taxpayer flight expenses raise stewardship questions
- COVID ivermectin promotion and anti-mask stance despite medical training raises questions about truthfulness
- 98% partisan alignment may suggest tribalism over principled governance

# PART I: US SENATE CHALLENGERS (2026 Primary - August 4, 2026)

---

## 1. JASON HART (D) -- Wichita

### Basic Profile
- **Party:** Democrat (switched from Independent to Republican in February 2026, then switched to Democrat in March 2026)
- **Location:** Wichita, Kansas
- **Occupation:** Former Assistant U.S. Attorney, District of Kansas (resigned March 2026)
- **Campaign Website:** [hartforsenate.com](https://hartforsenate.com/)
- **Self-Description:** "Straight, white, Christian man"
- **FEC Filing:** Registered candidate for 2026 Kansas Senate race

### Biography & Career
- **Education:** Juris Doctor, University of Kansas School of Law
- **Career Timeline:**
  1. Practiced law in Dodge City, Kansas (early career, several years)
  2. Shawnee County District Attorney's Office
  3. Kansas Attorney General's Office -- Assistant Attorney General
  4. U.S. Attorney's Office, District of Kansas -- Assistant U.S. Attorney (~16 years, serving under both Democratic and Republican-appointed U.S. Attorneys)
- **Specialty:** Child exploitation, child abuse, and child pornography prosecution. 21+ years total prosecuting these cases across multiple offices.
- **Boss at resignation:** U.S. Attorney Ryan Kriegshauser
- **Notable cases prosecuted:** Multiple federal child pornography indictments and convictions, including a Kansas man sentenced to 480 months (40 years) for production of child pornography

### The Party Switch Story
This is the defining narrative of Hart's candidacy:
1. Hart was registered as an **Independent** for most of his career
2. In **February 2026**, he switched to **Republican** -- intending to primary U.S. Rep. Ron Estes in Kansas' 4th Congressional District
3. His wife told him: **"I'm not sleeping with a Republican"**
4. He then discovered his friend **Katy Tyndell** was planning to run as a Democrat in that same race -- didn't want to compete with her
5. In **early March 2026**, he quit his job as AUSA, switched to **Democrat**, and entered the U.S. Senate race
6. He described the **January killing of Alex Pretti by federal agents in Minneapolis** as the catalyzing event that pushed him from law enforcement into politics

### Campaign Positions
- **Tariffs:** Opposes current tariff policies, says "Kansas families are paying the price for unfair tariffs"
- **Corporate taxes:** Wants corporations to "pay their fair share" and close loopholes
- **Small business:** Supports reducing costs for working families and small businesses
- **Immigration:** Has spoken about immigration policy (details from Kansas Democrats immigration forum)
- **Running without a campaign manager:** Has deliberately chosen not to hire one, stating: "I'm not sure that a campaign manager, though, would help me out, because what I have observed is the campaign manager is the handler that kind of tries to prevent you from being your authentic self."

### Key Quote -- "Electability" Argument
Hart has made a controversial argument for his candidacy, defending his assertion that he is the best Democratic candidate because he is "a straight, white, Christian man" -- essentially arguing electability in deep-red Kansas requires a candidate who matches the state's demographics. This has drawn both support (pragmatism) and criticism (identity-based argument) within the Democratic primary field.

### Family
- **Wife:** Name not publicly confirmed; known only through the "I'm not sleeping with a Republican" quote
- **Children:** At least one child (referenced in Kansas Reflector article -- child's head of school is Laura Kelly's daughter's best friend)

### Church/Faith
- **Self-identifies as Christian.** No specific denomination or church identified in public records.

### Social Media
- **Campaign website:** [hartforsenate.com](https://hartforsenate.com/)
- No verified Twitter, Instagram, or Facebook campaign accounts found in search results

### Assessment
Hart is the most unconventional candidate in the Democratic primary. A career federal prosecutor who switched parties twice in one month, running on a blunt "electability" argument centered on his identity as a straight white Christian male in Kansas. His wife's quip has become his most quoted line. His lack of political experience or campaign infrastructure is either refreshingly authentic or dangerously unprepared -- depends on the voter. His 21-year record prosecuting child predators is his strongest credential.

### Sources
- [Kansas Reflector: Hart opens arms to Republicans](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/03/23/democratic-candidate-in-u-s-senate-race-opens-arms-to-kansas-republicans-lost-in-the-wilderness/)
- [KMUW: Hart coverage](https://www.kmuw.org/government/2026-03-25/democratic-candidate-in-u-s-senate-race-opens-arms-to-kansas-republicans-lost-in-the-wilderness)
- [KCUR: Guide to candidates](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2025-12-30/whos-running-to-represent-kansas-in-the-u-s-senate-in-2026-heres-a-guide-to-the-candidates)
- [Avvo: Jason Hart profile](https://www.avvo.com/attorneys/67202-ks-jason-hart-1922169.html)
- [DOJ: Cases prosecuted by Hart](https://www.justice.gov/usao-ks/pr/kansas-man-sentenced-480-months-production-child-porn)
- [hartforsenate.com](https://hartforsenate.com/)

## 2. PATRICK SCHMIDT (D) -- Lawrence/Topeka

### Basic Profile
- **Party:** Democrat
- **Age:** ~35 (graduated Tufts 2013)
- **Location:** Topeka, Kansas (represents KS Senate District 19 -- parts of Lawrence/Douglas County + Lecompton)
- **Current Office:** Kansas State Senator, District 19 (sworn in January 13, 2025)
- **Campaign Website:** [patrickforkansas.com](https://patrickforkansas.com/)
- **Facebook:** [patrickforkansas](https://www.facebook.com/patrickforkansas/)

### Biography & Education
- **Born:** Overland Park, Kansas
- **6th-generation Kansan** -- family includes six generations of farmers, miners, and teachers
- **Parents:** Both public school teachers; mother worked retail as second job, father did custom harvesting with family business and later tutoring
- **High School:** Grew up in Overland Park area
- **Bachelor's degree:** Tufts University, 2013
- **Convisero Mentor** -- participated in political mentorship program

### Military Service
- **Commissioned:** U.S. Navy Intelligence Officer after Tufts graduation
- **Ship:** USS Ronald Reagan (CVN-76) -- served on the battle group's intelligence team
- **Mission:** Defending U.S. interests from China and Russia in the Pacific
- **Pentagon:** Worked at the Pentagon (specific role not detailed)
- **Transition:** Recently moved to Naval Reserve and returned to Kansas with wife

### Political Career
- **2022:** First political run -- U.S. House of Representatives, Kansas 2nd Congressional District, challenging Republican incumbent Jake LaTurner. Lost in general election.
- **Motivation:** The January 6, 2021 Capitol attack motivated his entry into politics
- **2024:** Won Kansas State Senate District 19, defeating Republican Tyler Wible in the general election
- **2025-2026:** Serving as state senator while running for U.S. Senate

### State Senate Record (2025-2026)
- **Property Tax Champion:** Made property taxes his top issue; broke with party lines to support a proposed state constitutional amendment capping annual property value increases for tax purposes
- **SR 1706:** Sponsored a resolution condemning the pardons and commutations of sentences for those involved in the January 6 Capitol attack
- **Budget:** Active in Senate budget debates; participated in discussions about state funding allocation
- **Self-described approach:** "Trying to stop bad stuff" while pressing for property tax relief (Kansas Reflector profile, March 2025)

### Family
- **Wife:** Megan Walden -- returned to Kansas together after his Naval Reserve transition
- **Resides:** Topeka, Kansas

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified** in public records. No church affiliation found.

### Campaign Positions
- Property tax relief (core issue)
- Rural healthcare access
- Public education funding
- Veterans' issues

### Social Media
- **Website:** [patrickforkansas.com](https://patrickforkansas.com/)
- **Facebook:** [patrickforkansas](https://www.facebook.com/patrickforkansas/)
- **KS Legislature page:** [kslegislature.gov](https://www.kslegislature.gov/li/b2025_26/members/sen_schmidt_patrick_1/)

### Assessment
Schmidt is the only Democratic candidate currently holding elected office, which gives him a legislative record to run on (or defend). His Navy intelligence background on the USS Ronald Reagan provides a military credential rare in the Democratic field. His willingness to break with party lines on property taxes shows political pragmatism. The January 6 motivation for entering politics is sincere but may alienate some Kansas voters who view that framing as partisan. He is arguably the strongest institutional candidate in the Democratic primary.

## 3. CHRISTY CAUBLE DAVIS (D) -- Cottonwood Falls

### Basic Profile
- **Party:** Democrat
- **Location:** Cottonwood Falls, Kansas (Chase County)
- **Occupation:** Business owner (Davis Preservation, LLC) + former USDA Rural Development State Director for Kansas
- **Campaign Website:** [christydavisforkansas.com](https://www.christydavisforkansas.com/)
- **Facebook:** [Christy Cauble Davis](https://www.facebook.com/christy.davis.710/)
- **LinkedIn:** [Christy Davis - Davis Preservation](https://www.linkedin.com/in/christy-davis-19286b224/)

### Biography & Education
- **Born:** Sedgwick, Kansas
- **5th-generation Kansan**
- **High School:** Sedgwick High School
- **Bachelor's degree:** Kansas State University, 1997
- **Graduate degree:** Wichita State University, 1999

### Career Timeline
1. **City of Newton** -- Preservation Planner
2. **Kansas Historical Society** -- Preservation Officer
3. **Symphony in the Flint Hills** -- Executive Director (2013-2019). Moved to Chase County for this role.
4. **Davis Preservation, LLC** -- Owner (ongoing)
5. **USDA Rural Development** -- Kansas State Director (Biden administration appointment, announced June 23, 2022). Oversaw $1.3 billion in Kansas investment across businesses, infrastructure, housing, and healthcare.
6. **Kansas Downtown Development Association** -- Legislative Chair
7. **Chase County Chamber of Commerce** -- Board member

### Family & Community
- **Husband:** Luke Davis
- **Son:** Jack
- In 2016, Christy and Luke **adopted a historic building in Cottonwood Falls** and transformed it into an award-winning laundromat ("Clean History" -- featured in American Coin-Op magazine)
- In 2019, the couple **rehabilitated a historic bank building** to create new housing and a bookstore
- Both projects demonstrate their commitment to rural community revitalization

### Campaign Positions
- Expanding access to rural healthcare
- Funding strong public schools
- Immigration reform that works for families and agriculture
- Rebuilding reasonable economic policies
- Restoring accountability in Washington
- **Core message:** "It's time for Kansas to have a Senator who shows up."

### Campaign Finance
- FEC-registered candidate (FEC ID: H0KS01214)
- Under NRSC scrutiny: The National Republican Senatorial Committee called for an ethics investigation into Davis (along with Murray, Spidel Neumann, and Parelkar) for allegedly failing to submit financial disclosures within required timeframe

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified** in public records. No church affiliation found.

### Assessment
Davis has the deepest rural Kansas credentials in the Democratic primary. A 5th-generation Kansan who actually lives in the Flint Hills (population ~2,800 in Chase County), she's the anti-Overland Park candidate. Her USDA appointment under Biden gives her federal experience and a $1.3 billion Kansas investment talking point. The historic building restorations in Cottonwood Falls show she practices what she preaches about rural community investment. Her vulnerability is being tied to the Biden administration in a state Trump won by 14+ points.

- **Threads:** [@speumann](https://www.threads.com/@speumann)

- **Born:** Near Topeka, Kansas
- **Raised:** Overland Park, Johnson County
- **High School:** Shawnee Mission North -- standout student and athlete
- **Girls Nation:** Represented Kansas at Girls Nation (American Legion program), where she first declared her dream to serve in the U.S. Senate
- **University of Chicago** -- Economics degree
- **Northwestern University (Kellogg School of Management)** -- MBA (completed while working full-time at Ameriprise)
- Returned to Kansas in summer 2025 after decades away

### Career
- **Ameriprise Financial Services** -- 22 years as an executive (culmination of 40-year business career)
- Retired May 2025
- **First time running for office**

### Campaign Positions
- Opposes tariffs harmful to Kansas farmers

- Fighting for farmers
- Protecting reproductive freedom
- Defending Social Security, Medicare, and the VA
- Making kids safer at school

- **FEC ID:** S6KS00262
- Under NRSC scrutiny for alleged late financial disclosure filing

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified** in public records.

### Assessment
Spidel Neumann brings the strongest corporate resume in the field -- 22 years as an Ameriprise executive with a UChicago/Kellogg pedigree. The Girls Nation story is a compelling narrative arc (dreaming of the Senate as a teenager). However, she's been away from Kansas for decades, only returning in summer 2025 -- a potential "carpetbagger" vulnerability. She's never held elected office. Her Johnson County base is the Democratic stronghold in Kansas, but that also means she'll compete with Murray and Parelkar for those same metro voters.

## 5. ERIK MURRAY (D) -- Kansas City, KS

### Basic Profile
- **Party:** Democrat
- **Location:** Kansas City, Kansas (Wyandotte County)
- **Occupation:** CEO/Managing Partner, Eastside Innovation LLC (commercial real estate development)
- **Campaign Website:** [erikforkansas.com](https://erikforkansas.com/)
- **Facebook:** [@erik.murray.820582](https://www.facebook.com/erik.murray.820582/)
- **Instagram:** [@erik4ks](https://www.instagram.com/erik4ks/)
- **LinkedIn:** [Erik Murray, SIOR, CCIM](https://www.linkedin.com/in/erikmurraysior)

### Biography & Education
- **Born:** KU Medical Center, Kansas City, KS
- **Raised:** Kansas City, KS
- **Childhood faith:** Attended **Fellowship Christian Church** with his grandmother; also attended **St. Patrick's Catholic School**
- **High School:** Sumner Academy of Arts and Science, Class of 2000 (magnet school in KCK)
- **College:** University of Southern California (USC), graduated 2004, BA in Disease Prevention from USC's Medical School
- **Professional designations:** CCIM (Certified Commercial Investment Member) and SIOR (Society of Industrial and Office Realtors), both earned 2009 -- places him in top 1% of commercial real estate professionals internationally

### Career Timeline
1. **Commercial real estate brokerage** -- 20-year career spanning investment, brokerage, and development
2. **Oak Impact Group** (Oakland, CA, 2016) -- Founded venture capital investment firm intersecting real estate and social impact. Among the first to bring FDIC-insured banking real estate lending into the cannabis industry.
3. **Returned to Kansas** in 2023 with family
4. **Eastside Innovation LLC** (Kansas City, KS, 2023) -- Founded to bring clean energy to low-income communities in KCK
5. **Indian Springs Mall redevelopment** -- Leading a **nearly $1 billion redevelopment project** at the site of the former Indian Springs Mall in Kansas City, KS

### Family
- **Wife:** Nicole (met at USC)
- **Children:** Four kids; two still at home attending Sumner Academy
- Lives in Wyandotte County

### THE BLACK PANTHER QUOTE -- Full Context
This is Murray's biggest vulnerability. Here is the full story:

**What happened:** On a late November 2025 appearance on **The Disruption Lab podcast** (just days before entering the Senate race on December 3, 2025), Murray said:

> "Go spend a decade, you know, having lunch with Elaine Brown, who's one of the original founders of the Black Panther[s]. It'll change some wiring in your brain."

**Who is Elaine Brown:** Former chairman of the Black Panther Party (1974-1977). Self-described "soldier" working to bring about a "socialist revolution" in the United States. Has recently reaffirmed her commitment to topple the "Empire of the United States." Currently 81 years old, living in Oakland, where she builds affordable housing (79 units of supportive housing in West Oakland). The Oakland City Council is considering naming an intersection after her.

**The Washington Free Beacon reported this** under the headline: "Kansas Senate Candidate Names His Political Inspiration: A Black Panther 'Soldier' Working To Destroy the American 'Empire.'" The Free Beacon noted Murray's ties to Brown "may be a tough sell in deep-red Kansas, which last elected a Democratic senator in 1932."

**The nuance:** Murray didn't call Brown his "political inspiration" -- he cited her as someone who changed his perspective during a decade in Oakland. Brown's current work is legitimate affordable housing development. But in a Kansas general election, the "had lunch with a Black Panther founder" line is oppo research gold for any Republican opponent.

**Murray's defense (from campaign materials):** He frames his Oakland experience as broadening, not radicalizing. His campaign emphasizes he was born in KCK, returned to Kansas, and wants to bring the "disconnect between what capital wants and what community wants" insight home.

### Campaign Finance
- Under NRSC scrutiny for alleged late financial disclosure filing
- Campaign attributed delays to complications during federal government shutdown affecting FEC systems

### Campaign Positions
- Lowering costs for starting and running small businesses
- Supports Opportunity Zones program (tax incentives for investment in distressed areas)
- Healthcare accessibility
- Touring all 105 Kansas counties ("Heart of America tour")
- First time running for office

### Church/Faith
- **Fellowship Christian Church** (childhood, attended with grandmother)
- **St. Patrick's Catholic School** (education)
- Current church affiliation not confirmed.

### Assessment
Murray is the most complex candidate in the field. A KCK native with legitimate deep roots (Sumner Academy multigenerational), elite real estate credentials (CCIM/SIOR), and a nearly $1 billion redevelopment project in his hometown. But the decade in Oakland, the cannabis industry work, and especially the Elaine Brown quote create a massive vulnerability in Kansas. He's essentially running on the narrative that leaving Kansas and coming back made him better -- a risky pitch in a state that values people who stayed. The Free Beacon hit piece was the first real opposition research deployed against any Democratic candidate in this race.

### Sources
- [Free Beacon: Black Panther inspiration](https://freebeacon.com/democrats/kansas-senate-candidate-names-his-political-inspiration-a-black-panther-soldier-working-to-destroy-the-american-empire/)
- [Kansas Reflector: Murray campaign profile](https://kansasreflector.com/2026/03/16/kansas-city-entrepreneur-prioritizes-passion-decency-in-campaign-for-u-s-senate/)
- [AfroTech: Oak Impact Group](https://afrotech.com/erik-murray-oakland-impact-group)
- [erikforkansas.com/meet-erik](https://erikforkansas.com/meet-erik/)

## 6. ANNE PARELKAR (D) -- Overland Park

### Basic Profile
- **Party:** Democrat
- **Location:** Overland Park, Kansas (since 2017)
- **Occupation:** Immigration attorney
- **Campaign Website:** [anneforkansas.com](https://www.anneforkansas.com/)
- **LinkedIn:** [Anne Lea Parelkar](https://www.linkedin.com/in/anne-lea-parelkar-83095659/)

### Biography & Education
- **Born:** Pine Bluff, Arkansas
- **Raised:** White Hall, Arkansas
- **High School:** White Hall High School, Class of 2001
- **College:** Lyon College, Batesville, Arkansas -- BA in History, Political Science minor, Secondary Education concentration
- **Law School:** William H. Bowen School of Law, University of Arkansas at Little Rock -- graduated 2011, passed Arkansas Bar Exam
- **Bar admissions:** Arkansas, Missouri, Kansas
- **Specialty:** Immigration law

### Career
- Licensed immigration attorney practicing in Kansas, Arkansas, and Missouri
- Member of AILA (American Immigration Lawyers Association)
- **First time running for office**

### Origin Story
Parelkar traveled across Kansas in March (2025) to a town hall in western Kansas to confront U.S. Sen. Roger Marshall -- and that experience motivated her to run for his seat.

### Family
- **Husband:** Nikhil Parelkar -- married shortly after passing the Arkansas bar; they moved to Kansas together
- Lived in Overland Park since 2017

### Campaign Positions
- Immigration reform (core issue, professional expertise)
- Children's healthcare: Proposes a "single consolidated program" for health care for people under 18, replacing the patchwork of Medicaid, CHIP, and other programs
- Antitrust and consumer protection: Stronger laws to protect consumers
- First-time candidate bringing professional expertise to broken federal systems

### Campaign Finance
- Under NRSC scrutiny for alleged late financial disclosure filing

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified** in public records.

### Assessment
Parelkar is the only immigration attorney in the field, giving her unique professional credibility on an issue that dominates Kansas politics. However, she's not from Kansas -- born and raised in Arkansas, moved to Kansas through marriage. In a field where "5th-generation Kansan" and "6th-generation Kansan" are common descriptors, her transplant status is a weakness. Her children's healthcare consolidation proposal is the most specific policy proposal from any Democratic candidate. The Overland Park base puts her in the same Johnson County lane as Spidel Neumann and Murray.

## 7. MICHAEL SOETAERT (D) -- Wellington

### Basic Profile
- **Party:** Democrat
- **Location:** Wellington, Kansas (Sumner County)
- **Occupation:** Not clearly stated (political activist/serial candidate)
- **Campaign Websites:** Multiple -- [replacejerrymoran.org](https://replacejerrymoran.org/), [mike4kansas.org](https://mike4kansas.org/), [mikeforkansas.net](https://mikeforkansas.net/), [mikeforkansas.my.canva.site](https://mikeforkansas.my.canva.site/)
- **Facebook:** [michael.soetaert1](https://www.facebook.com/michael.soetaert1/)
- **ActBlue:** [michael-soetaert](https://secure.actblue.com/donate/michael-soetaert)
- **Historic distinction:** First openly gay candidate to run for U.S. Senate in Kansas

### Biography
- **Born:** Wellington, Kansas
- **Family Heritage:** Direct descendant of Constant Soetaert; knew great-grandfather Charles as a child. The Soetaert family includes former Wellington Mayor Tony Soetaert.
- **Adoption:** Given up for adoption at birth into a "right wing, fundamentalist, Roman Catholic family" (pre-Roe v. Wade)
- **Father's career:** Vice President of Coca-Cola Mid-America; previously part of NASA Mission Control for the first 16 Apollo missions
- **Self-identifies as Christian**

### Serial Candidacy Record
This is the defining characteristic -- Soetaert has run for office repeatedly:
| Year | Office | Result |
|------|--------|--------|
| 2019 | Council Grove City Council, Ward 3 | Unknown |
| 2020 | U.S. House, Kansas 1st District | Lost primary |
| 2022 | U.S. Senate, Kansas | Lost primary |
| 2024 | Kansas State Senate, District 32 | Lost |
| 2024 | President of the United States | Did not advance |
| 2025 | Wellington City Council | Won (962 votes) |
| 2025 | Resigned from Wellington City Council (Dec 12) after 2 meetings |
| 2026 | U.S. Senate, Kansas | Current race |

### Wellington City Council Resignation
- **Elected:** November 2025 (962 votes; Tim Hay got 1,322, Mary Lucas 1,191)
- **Inducted:** December 3, 2025
- **Resigned:** December 12, 2025 -- submitted resignation, accepted 5-0 with one abstention on December 16
- **Had served:** Two meetings before resigning to run for U.S. Senate
- **Jerry Elmore Jr.** was appointed to fill his vacant seat

### Campaign Positions
- LGBTQ+ rights champion: Supports the Equality Act and the Respect for Marriage Act
- First openly gay Kansas Senate candidate -- frames candidacy around representation

### Church/Faith
- **Raised Roman Catholic** (adoptive family described as "right wing, fundamentalist, Roman Catholic")
- **Self-identifies as Christian**
- Current church affiliation not confirmed

### Assessment
Soetaert is a serial candidate with no viable path to the nomination. He has run for six different offices across seven years, winning only a Wellington city council seat that he resigned from after two meetings. The pattern of running, losing, and running again for progressively higher offices -- while simultaneously being unable to hold the one office he won -- is disqualifying for most voters. His historic significance as the first openly gay Kansas Senate candidate is genuine. But this is his fourth attempt at federal office. His multiple campaign websites (at least four different domains) suggest organizational chaos.

### Sources
- [Ballotpedia: Michael Soetaert](https://ballotpedia.org/Michael_Soetaert)
- [Vote Smart: Soetaert biography](https://justfacts.votesmart.org/candidate/biography/192430/michael-soetaert)
- [City of Wellington: Resignation press release](https://www.cityofwellington.net/newsview.aspx?nid=6940)
- [Sumner NewsCow: Council resignation](https://www.sumnernewscow.com/wellington-city-council-accepts-michael-mike-soetaerts-resignation-at-tuesdays-meeting/)

## 8. CHASE LaPORTE (R) -- Primarying Marshall

### Basic Profile
- **Party:** Republican
- **Location:** Kansas (originally Carthage, Missouri)
- **Occupation:** Business administrator
- **Campaign Website:** [laporte4ksgov.com](https://www.laporte4ksgov.com/) (this appears to be a gubernatorial site -- no dedicated Senate website found)
- **FEC Filing:** [FEC Candidate H6KS03258](https://www.fec.gov/data/candidate/H6KS03258/)
- **Community affiliations:** Shriners, American Legion, VFW

### Biography
- **Born:** Carthage, Missouri
- **U.S. Army:** Served 2005-2013 (8 years active duty)
- **Education:** Associate degree, Cowley County Community College, 2017
- **Career:** Business administrator (details limited)

### Serial Candidacy
Like Soetaert on the Democratic side, LaPorte has run for multiple offices:
- **U.S. House, Kansas 3rd Congressional District** (previous cycle)
- **Kansas Governor** (previous/current cycle -- has a gubernatorial campaign website)
- **U.S. Senate** (2026 -- challenging Roger Marshall in the Republican primary)

### Campaign Positions
- Reducing government spending and inflation
- Term limits (cites George Washington)
- Smaller government (cites Ronald Reagan)
- Limited campaign materials available

### Assessment
LaPorte is not a serious threat to Roger Marshall. He's a perennial candidate with limited resources, no dedicated Senate campaign website (his web presence is for a gubernatorial campaign), an associate degree from a community college, and a thin public record. Marshall will win this primary without breaking a sweat. LaPorte's value in the race is as a protest vote vehicle for any Republicans dissatisfied with Marshall -- but that number in Kansas is negligible.

### Sources
- [Ballotpedia: Chase LaPorte](https://ballotpedia.org/Chase_LaPorte)
- [FEC: LaPorte filing](https://www.fec.gov/data/candidate/H6KS03258/)
- [KCUR: Guide to candidates](https://www.kcur.org/politics-elections-and-government/2025-12-30/whos-running-to-represent-kansas-in-the-u-s-senate-in-2026-heres-a-guide-to-the-candidates)
- [OpenCampaign: LaPorte positions](https://www.opencampaign.com/politicians-in-united-states/197957/chase-laporte/issue-positions)

## 9. ALAINA CUNNINGHAM -- Vice Mayor, Hays City Commission

### Full Profile (Updated from previous report)

### Relationship to Aaron Cunningham (County Attorney)
**INVESTIGATION STATUS: Strong circumstantial evidence of spousal relationship, but NOT confirmed in any public record.**

Evidence for:
- Alaina stated she "moved to Hays to start a career for her husband" (2010)
- Aaron Cunningham is a Hays-based attorney (graduated Hays High 2012, K-State, Washburn Law 2019)
- Both share the Cunningham surname and serve in Hays public offices
- The timing is compatible if there is a modest age gap (she arrived 2010; he graduated HS 2012 -- she would be mid-to-late 20s, he 17-18)

Evidence against:
- No public record, news article, wedding announcement, or social media post confirms the relationship
- An "about.me" profile for Aaron lists Manhattan and Hays associations but doesn't mention Alaina
- Alaina's maiden name appears to be Nesmith (public records suggest "Alaina D Nesmith" from Hays)

**Bottom line:** They may be married, but it could also be coincidence. A county marriage record search would resolve this definitively. If they are married, it means the City Vice Mayor and the County Attorney are spouses -- a notable power dynamic in a community of 21,000.

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified** in any public record searched. No church membership, no faith statements found. The Salina Diocese Catholic Register PDF appeared in search results for her name, but the connection (if any) could not be confirmed.

### Community Involvement
- HaysMed Foundation: Board member 8+ years, elected President unanimously
- Downtown Hays Development Corporation Board (past)
- Hays High Academic Booster Club (current)
- O'Loughlin Elementary PTA (past officer -- all three children attended)
- 13+ years living in Hays

### Assessment
Cunningham remains the least publicly visible commissioner. Her primary public identity is through healthcare (HaysMed nurse) and community boards rather than political activity. The potential spousal connection to the County Attorney is the most interesting unanswered question in Hays local government.

## 10. SHAUN MUSIL -- Commissioner (~12 years)

### Full Profile (Updated from previous report)
- **Age:** 53
- **Lived in Hays:** 30 years
- **Spouse:** Heather Musil -- instructor in FHSU Department of Teacher Education (previously Hays Middle School teacher)
- **Day Job:** Account Representative, Nex-Tech (managed IT, cybersecurity, physical security, communications)
- **Previous career:** District Sales Manager, Coca-Cola Enterprises (oversaw western Kansas routes, achieved double-digit growth)
- **Business:** Former co-owner, Paisley Pear Wine Bar, Bistro & Market (opened July 2017, sold to Matt and Tiffany October 2024)
- **Facebook (Official):** [musilcomish](https://www.facebook.com/musilcomish/)
- **LinkedIn:** [Shaun Musil](https://www.linkedin.com/in/shaun-musil-26539490/)
- **City Page:** [haysusa.com/273/Shaun-Musil](https://haysusa.com/273/Shaun-Musil)

### COVID Vandalism (Full Context)
During 2020, as Mayor Musil led the city through COVID mask mandate debates:
- **Voted FOR the mask ordinance** (3-1 vote; Ruder sole dissenter)
- His family's **three vehicles were vandalized** overnight -- he woke up to find the damage
- Received **personal threats** against himself and his family
- His own business (Paisley Pear) was **shut down by the governor's emergency order**
- **All five Musil family members contracted COVID** during the pandemic
- His quote afterward: He was "scared to death" making those decisions but "the people came out of the woodwork thanking us"
- Described the experience: "True government means disagreeing and working things out"

### Paisley Pear Timeline
- **July 2017:** Shaun and Heather purchased from Jocelyn Brungardt; added wine bar component
- **2020:** Shut down by governor's emergency COVID order
- **August 2024:** Named FHSU Tiger Nation Partner of the Year
- **April 2024:** Listed for sale (announced as wanting to "prioritize time with loved ones")
- **October 2024:** Sold to Matt and Tiffany; grand reopening under new ownership

### Wife Heather Musil & FHSU Connection
- Heather Musil is an instructor in the **FHSU Department of Teacher Education** at Fort Hays State University
- Previously taught at Hays Middle School
- This is the FHSU connection -- it's through his wife, not directly through Shaun

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified** in any public record searched. No church membership or faith-related statements found despite extensive search. The surname "Musil" is common in the Catholic Volga German communities of western Kansas (Hays has deep Catholic/Volga German heritage), but this is inference, not evidence.

### Assessment (Updated)
Musil is entering his final years on the commission with deep institutional memory. The COVID vandalism story is the most dramatic personal narrative of any local official in Hays. Having sold the Paisley Pear, he's now free of the business interest that created potential conflict-of-interest questions on downtown development votes. His re-election in 2025 to a four-year term (through 2029) was emphatic community endorsement.

## 11. SANDY JACOBS -- Commissioner (~8 years), Former Mayor

### Full Profile (Confirmed from previous report)
- **Age:** 75
- **Husband:** Danny Jacobs (both over 65)
- **Lifetime Hays resident**
- **Retired from:** Sunflower Bank (Executive Vice President) and Heartland Community Foundation (Executive Director, 5 years, retired ~Dec 31, 2020)
- **Email:** sandyj1950@gmail.com
- **Facebook:** [Sandy Jacobs - Hays City Commission](https://www.facebook.com/people/Sandy-Jacobs-Hays-City-Commission/100063604999773/)
- **City Page:** [haysusa.com/270/Sandy-Jacobs](https://haysusa.com/270/Sandy-Jacobs)

### Three-Time Mayor
- **Mayor 2021:** Succeeded Musil after COVID term
- **Mayor September 2024-January 2026:** Elected by commission
- **Previous stint:** First served as mayor during her initial years on the commission (exact year unconfirmed -- may be counted as third time)
- NOTE: Reorganization in January 2026 named Mason Ruder as Mayor and Alaina Cunningham as Vice Mayor; Jacobs stepped down from the mayor role but remains a commissioner.

### Vine Street Champion (Key Infrastructure Legacy)
- **Core promise:** Ran for office partly on fixing Vine Street (the main commercial corridor in Hays)
- **North Vine Corridor:** Major reconstruction project with KDOT. Came in $3.5M over budget. 18 months of construction. "Substantially completed." Included roundabouts.
- **South Vine reconstruction:** $3.5M project (separate from north Vine)
- **37th Street roundabout:** Jacobs' signature project. Restaurants near the roundabout saw **10-20% sales increases** after installation.
- **Quote:** "This is the best design -- in my opinion -- that has been brought forward."

### Heartland Community Foundation Legacy
Led "substantial growth" across Ellis, Rooks, and Trego counties during her 5-year tenure as ED. The foundation remains a cornerstone of regional philanthropy:
- [Heartland Community Foundation](https://heartlandcommunityfoundation.org/)
- Raised $410,145 for Ellis, Rooks, and Trego counties in a single campaign year

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified** in any public record searched. No church membership found. Like Musil, the Jacobs surname is common in the western Kansas community but no specific affiliation confirmed.

### Assessment
At 75, Jacobs is the commission's elder stateswoman with the deepest roots in Hays finance and philanthropy. Her Sunflower Bank career (EVP) and Heartland Foundation leadership give her the strongest economic development credentials on the commission. The Vine Street roundabout project -- backed by hard data on restaurant sales increases -- is a tangible legacy. She and Danny are emblematic of the "establishment Hays" power structure: banking, nonprofit, civic service.

The BYOB self-defense classes and Alzheimer's fundraiser show genuine community investment. His pet licensing reform initiative (reducing bureaucratic fees that collect only $14K/year) signals a practical, libertarian-leaning approach to government. He replaced the progressive Reese Barrick, shifting the commission's center of gravity.

## 13. TOBY DOUGHERTY -- City Manager (Since 2007)

### Full Profile (Updated)
- **Title:** City Manager, City of Hays (appointed August 1, 2007)
- **Hometown:** Lucas, Kansas (small town ~1 hour from Hays)
- **In Hays since:** 2005 (started as Assistant City Manager March 2005)
- **Total Hays government service:** 21 years
- **Education:** University of Kansas -- B.A. Political Science + Public Service/Civic Leadership; KU Certified Public Manager program
- **Previous job:** City Administrator, Gallatin, Missouri
- **Previous career:** Transportation industry (12 years)
- **Email:** tdougherty@haysusa.com
- **City Page:** [haysusa.com/directory.aspx?eid=6](https://www.haysusa.com/directory.aspx?eid=6)

### Salary
- **2022 salary (last available on OpenPayrolls):** $186,284 -- highest-paid employee in the City of Hays
- **2025-2026 salary:** Not publicly available through search; would require Kansas Open Gov database query or public records request. Given his 21-year tenure and typical annual adjustments, likely in the **$195,000-$210,000 range** (estimate only).

### R9 Ranch Pipeline -- The Defining Project
- **Cost:** $144.9 million (up from $75-80M estimate ~5 years ago)
- **Distance:** 65-90 mile pipeline from R9 Ranch wellfield (Edwards County) to Hays/Russell
- **Water rights:** 8,000 acre-feet on 6,700 acres (purchased by city in 1995)
- **Legal battle:** WaterPACK (agricultural irrigators) has fought the water transfer through courts. Kansas Supreme Court heard oral arguments December 2025.
- **Dougherty quote:** "The opponents in this have succeeded in weaponizing the legal and judicial system against Hays and Russell."
- **Funding:** $15.8M Build Kansas grant (April 2025); pursuing $50M FEMA BRIC grant
- **Status (March 2026):** Pipeline design wrapping up; right-of-way permits being sought; expected to bid early 2026

### Strong Towns Pioneer
Dougherty was one of the early city managers nationally to adopt Strong Towns fiscal analysis methodology:
- Featured on the Strong Towns Podcast (2015 + follow-up)
- Created "A Stronger Hays" fiscal analysis document
- Key insight: "New growth -- typically seen as an asset -- could be a liability" if infrastructure maintenance costs exceed revenue generated

### Family/Personal
- **Not identified** in public records. No spouse, children, church, or personal details found despite extensive search. Dougherty maintains an exceptionally private personal life for someone who has been a public figure for 21 years. His public persona is entirely professional.

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified.** Zero results across multiple search strategies.

### Assessment
Dougherty is the most consequential unelected official in western Kansas. His 21-year tenure managing a city whose water supply is existentially threatened has made him effectively irreplaceable. The R9 Ranch pipeline is a generational infrastructure project -- $144.9M for a city of 21,000 is extraordinary. His Strong Towns methodology makes him unusually sophisticated for a small-city manager. The cost doubling of the R9 project is his biggest vulnerability, but no one has seriously challenged it because everyone knows the alternative (no water) is unthinkable. His personal privacy is remarkable -- in 21 years, there's essentially nothing public about his personal life.

### Sources
- [Strong Towns: Toby Dougherty](https://www.strongtowns.org/journal/2015/10/7/toby-dougherty-city-manager-of-haysks)
- [Strong Towns Podcast](https://podcast.strongtowns.org/e/toby-dougherty-1535377231/)
- [Municipal Water Leader Magazine](https://issuu.com/waterstrategies/docs/mwl_october_2020/s/11017849)
- [KWCH: $15M grant](https://www.kwch.com/2025/04/03/city-hays-awarded-15m-grant-secure-long-term-water-supply/)
- [E&E News/POLITICO: R9 water dispute](https://www.eenews.net/articles/farm-vs-city-kansas-water-law-gets-a-major-stress-test/)
- [OpenPayrolls: Hays highest paid](https://openpayrolls.com/rank/highest-paid-employees/hays-ks)
- [City of Hays: Dougherty](https://www.haysusa.com/directory.aspx?eid=6)

## 14. NEAL YOUNGER -- Ellis County Commissioner, District 2

### Full Profile (Confirmed from previous report + updates)
- **Title:** Ellis County Commissioner, 2nd District; Chairman of the Commission (2026)
- **Party:** Republican
- **Contact:** nyounger@ellisco.net | 785-656-0814
- **2026 Salary:** $21,584
- **Trade:** Electrician and plumber
- **In office since:** January 2021

### Electoral History
- **2020 Republican Primary:** Defeated incumbent Dustin Roths and Kerry McCue in three-way race. Younger: 639 votes (40.16%), Roths: 547 (34.38%), McCue: 405 (25.46%). Ran unopposed in general.
- Currently in second term

### "Mental Health Cheaper Than Jail" Context
During the 2026 budget process, Younger was quoted supporting a mental health funding increase with the reasoning: **"is less expensive than building a new jail."** This pragmatic fiscal conservative argument -- that investing in mental health services prevents more expensive incarceration costs -- was made during the commission's approval of a 1.96 mill levy increase for the $34.7M general fund budget. The full context: a homeowner with a $200,000 home pays approximately $45 more per year under the increase.

### Board Appointments (2026)
- Northwest Kansas Community Corrections and Juvenile Services board

### Policy Approach
- **Hands-on:** Pledged to spend 1-2 hours minimum in every county department to assess staffing
- **Fiscal:** "Ellis County spending too much money" was his top campaign concern in 2020
- **Economic development:** Favors proactive county role; wants to "work with the city of Hays to get more water to Hays and higher-paying jobs"
- **Housing:** During Big Creek Estates discussions, suggested residents explore forming a rural water district

### Family
- **Not identified** in any public record. No spouse, children, or family details found.

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified.** No church, denomination, or faith statement found.

### Social Media
- No Facebook page found
- No LinkedIn profile found
- No Twitter/X presence found
- **Very limited digital footprint** outside of Hays Post coverage and official county records

### Assessment
Younger is the blue-collar voice on the commission -- an electrician/plumber who brought trade-level fiscal discipline to county government. His mental health funding argument ("cheaper than jail") shows he's a pragmatist, not an ideologue. His complete absence from social media is notable in 2026 -- he governs through meeting rooms, not posts. No controversies, no red flags, no personal information publicly available. He is, in many ways, the most anonymous elected official in Ellis County.

## 15. NATHAN LEIKER -- Ellis County Commissioner, District 3

### Full Profile (Confirmed from previous report + updates)

- **Contact:** nleiker@ellisco.net | 785-621-1739

- **Farming philosophy:** Budgets on "basically only 2 paychecks a year" -- plans 2+ years ahead for inputs/expenses
- **40+ years farming experience** (family operation)

### Electoral History
- **2022 Republican Primary:** Won competitive four-way race. Leiker: 764 votes. Chris McGowne: 639. Randy Marintzer: 324. Incumbent Joe LeRoux: 286 (last place).
- District 3 is the largest in land area -- six townships covering the entire eastern edge of Ellis County and area north of Hays.

### Catholic Connection / Parish
- **TMP-Marian graduate (2004):** Thomas More Prep-Marian is the Catholic high school in Hays, operated under the Hays Catholic Schools umbrella (includes Holy Family Elementary). This confirms a Catholic upbringing.
- **Which parish:** Not confirmed. Hays has two main Catholic parishes: **Immaculate Heart of Mary** (IHM, 1805 Vine St) and **St. Joseph** (215 W 13th St). The Leiker surname is deeply rooted in the Volga German Catholic heritage of Ellis County. Without a direct public record, the specific parish cannot be confirmed -- but Catholic faith is effectively certain given the TMP-Marian education.
- **Board involvement:** Assigned to present for TMP schools during scholarship award presentations as a county commissioner, suggesting ongoing connection to the Catholic school community.
- **Additional boards:** Cottonwood Extension District (past), Kansas Hereford Association, Ellis County Farm Bureau Association

### Family
- **Parents:** David and Claudia Leiker of Hays
- **Spouse/children:** Not identified in public records

### Assessment
Leiker is the agricultural voice on the commission -- a working farmer managing 2,000+ acres across two counties. His TMP-Marian background places him squarely in the Catholic Volga German community that is the cultural bedrock of Ellis County. His 2022 primary win over the incumbent (who finished last in a four-way race) suggests the rural agricultural community wanted fresh representation. His budget discipline ("2 paychecks a year") translates directly to his government approach -- during the 2026 budget, he noted the commission spent "almost 13 hours going through each department, item by item, justifying costs and adjustments."

## 16. BOBBI DREILING -- Ellis County Clerk / Election Officer

### Full Profile
- **Title:** Ellis County Clerk and Election Officer (first elected 2020, re-elected 2024)
- **Party:** Republican
- **Age:** 61
- **Location:** Hays, Kansas
- **Education:** Associate's degree, Hutchinson Community College
- **Contact:** bdeed@ellisco.net | 785-628-9450 (note: email prefix suggests register of deeds, may be general county email)
- **Office:** 718 Main St, Hays, KS 67601
- **Facebook (Campaign):** [Bobbi Dreiling for Ellis County Clerk](https://www.facebook.com/people/Bobbi-Dreiling-for-Ellis-County-Clerk/100067810926476/)

### Career Path
1. **8 years as deputy clerk** under previous County Clerk Donna Maskus
2. **Elected County Clerk 2020** -- first term
3. **Re-elected 2024:** Defeated Democrat Laura Allen with 9,971 votes to Allen's 2,975 (77% to 23%)

### The 3,800 Misprinted Ballots (2020)
- **When Dreiling was Deputy Clerk** (not yet the elected clerk), 3,800 misprinted ballots were sent out
- A **Kansas Legislative race was mistakenly labeled as a U.S. Senate race** on the ballots
- **Result:** Three-day halt to absentee voting; all misprinted ballots had to be reprinted
- **Context:** This occurred under the previous clerk (Donna Maskus), though Dreiling was deputy. Dreiling's opponent Laura Allen used this incident against her in the 2024 campaign.

### FHSU Polling Location Controversy
This is Dreiling's most persistent public controversy:
- **Students at FHSU** and the **ACLU of Kansas** petitioned for a polling location on the FHSU campus
- **Hundreds signed the petition**
- Students presented a detailed proposal with university administration and campus police support
- **Dreiling refused,** citing that only 69 voters registered in Ellis County live on campus (by registration rolls)
- She **closed the voting location closest to FHSU** (601 Main) due to low voter turnout
- Students met with Dreiling "multiple times to no avail"
- Her defense: "I am the Clerk and Election Officer and I have to be comfortable with those decisions"
- Her stated reasoning: Numbers don't show need; security and logistics concerns
- **ACLU response:** Presented formal petition to county commission

### Election Security Measures
- Obtained **$6,000 election security grant** to install a camera at the ballot drop box
- Camera captures car license plate, driver, and ballots being dropped
- This allowed 24/7 drop box access
- **Township consolidation:** Helped county consolidate from 9 townships to 4 (cost savings in ballot prep)

### 2024 Opponent's Criticism (Laura Allen)
- Allen published a letter critical of Dreiling's handling of the clerk's office
- Primary criticisms: FHSU polling refusal and the 2020 misprint (though that was under the previous clerk)
- Allen received endorsement from the former county clerk

### Church/Faith
- **Not identified** in public records.

### Assessment
Dreiling is an election administrator in an era when election administration is intensely politicized. Her refusal to place a polling location at FHSU -- despite formal petitions from students, the ACLU, university administration, and campus police -- is her most controversial decision. The "69 registered voters on campus" defense ignores the broader population of students who live off-campus but near FHSU. Her election security camera installation and township consolidation show competent administration. The 3,800 misprinted ballots occurred on her watch as deputy clerk -- not directly her fault, but she was in the office when it happened. Her 77-23% re-election margin in 2024 shows the controversy hasn't cost her Republican voter support.

### Sources
- [Hays Post: Dreiling touts election security](https://hayspost.com/posts/64efa3e4-3296-4e5c-897f-8417a78e7fc3)
- [Hays Post: Dreiling candidate profile](https://hayspost.com/posts/3d32625b-57dc-4a18-9152-1013ddb13531)
- [ACLU Kansas: FHSU petition](https://www.aclukansas.org/press-releases/hundreds-ellis-county-sign-petition-polling-location-fhsu/)
- [Hays Post: ACLU presents petition](https://hayspost.com/posts/3a3f06a1-6b07-45c6-bf3c-8b76f4d564d7)
- [Hays Post: Students urge polling site](https://hayspost.com/posts/17997478-c7b3-4601-a433-c8f9623b09da)
- [Hays Post: Allen criticism letter](https://hayspost.com/posts/7c1c8817-1e3a-4c50-951e-895526935cf1)

## 17. REBECCA HERZOG -- Register of Deeds

### Full Profile

- **Party:** Republican
- **Location:** Hays, Kansas

### Service History

- This means she started working in the Register of Deeds office approximately 2016
